when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師時 , 她做了一些事 , 但真正要說的 , 未來將會遠遠超過這一點 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , alanturing , 1936年 , 又發明了電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械性的 。
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	圖靈的機器完全是理論上的 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但圖靈告訴我們很重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論如何製作電腦都不重要 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是不是像babbage的 , 或是像現在的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 還是細胞 , 還是機械性的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變小 。 所有這些都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做教堂反洗禮論文 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到了這個連結 , 你說這個東西babbage真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以做到我們今天用電腦所做的一切 , 只是非常緩慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	讓各位了解 , 它的速度有多慢 , 有1k的記憶力 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	使用打孔卡片 , 輸入的卡片 , 輸入的速度大約是第一張zx81的一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	牠的確有一群人 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加入很多額外的記憶體 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天我們來到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	這裡有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在瑞典 , 科學博物館的檔案庫 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由查爾斯•巴伯奇寫的 , 關於這個分析引擎的筆記 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一組計劃 , 我們稱之為28計劃 , 這也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字 , 他是科學博物館的策展人 , 也是推動這個計劃的人 , 來建造不一樣的引擎 , 我們的計劃就是建造它 。
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在南肯辛頓 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有好幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中一個是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計劃的計畫 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦 , 最後一部分是要在科學博物館內實體建構它 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你會終於明白電腦是如何運作的 , 因為你面前的不是一個小晶片 , 而是看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作 。 我聞到它的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫信 , 他說 , 一旦分析引擎存在 , 它一定會引導未來的科學發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有建造它 , 因為他總是在擺弄新計劃 , 但 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我來給各位看看它在動作中看起來像什麼 , 影片中只有一部分的cpu機制運作 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	這只是三組齒輪 , 加上這個 , 這是加上功能的機制 , 所以你可以想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代之前 , 我們將擁有它 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個影像充斥的演說中 , 雅諾•亞伯特德展示了他最近的三件關於人性的作品 , 我們的棲息地在他的系列中拍攝了一系列的空中攝影像 , 《從地面上來》 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談 , 他的網絡專案《六十億人》 , 他的即將拍攝《家》 , 記錄了人類透過拍攝環境的影響 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變遷、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarthhusbertand在廣闊的角度捕捉到地球的脆弱
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以搭飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸二氧化碳 ; 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態生態學 , 一年內 , 我以法國人的身分 , 排出的二氧化碳量就跟法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來抵消碳排放 , 每次都要這樣做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是向大家展示我們對地球的影響力 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些我去年拍攝的最後幾張照片的例子 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的油 , 很多污染 。

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們在七小時內不停工作24小時 , 盡可能抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油的終點 。

but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但是我們每年使用的油量比我們發現的還多三倍 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	在2050年之前 , 百分之百的珊瑚可能因為全球暖化而被消滅 。

the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自從1960年起 , 北極的厚度下降了超過40% 。

glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	對地球上的生命來說 , 冰河非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	就像高爾告訴你 , 有二十億人住在水面上 , 來自喜馬拉雅冰河 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston這場演講中 , 理查德•雷斯尼克指出 , 健康照護的成本和快速基因定序將會顛倒 。
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna , 生物科技 , 健康照護 , 科學 , 科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我向你們展示人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大型x染色體的複製品 ; 男性有x , 當然 , 還有一份小小的y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是個小東西 , 讓你與眾不同 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你把這個基因組放大 , 你會看到這個雙螺旋結構 , 生命的編碼是用這四個生物化學字母拼出來的 , 或者我們稱之為基礎 , 正確的:a , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	大家都可以隨意丟出很大的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但 , 事實上 , 如果我把這1280到800個解析度螢幕上的每一個像素都放在一個基礎上 , 我們會需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順道一提 , 有一群人 , 染色體決定要把染色體排序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美元後 , 基因組被定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	在2003年 , 最終的版本被出版了 , 他們繼續研究它 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這些都是在像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每一鹼基都要花一塊美金 , 非常慢的做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 沒有人知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們拿一個基因組 , 複製50個基因組 , 把這些dna切成50個鹼基讀取器 , 然後我們將它們排序 , 大量平行 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這些帶到軟體上 , 再組合起來 , 再告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	為了讓各位了解一下這是什麼樣子 , 人類的基因組計畫:3gbas , 沒錯 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器運行了:一週兩百gbabas
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 兩百人將會改變到六百人的速度 , 而這個速度的緩慢沒有任何跡象 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以 , 一個基礎的價格 , 要對一個基礎的排序做定序 , 已經下降了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這等同於你在1998年裝滿油氣的車 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開車到木星和兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc配置、所有醫學文獻的檔案、摩爾定律、舊式的定序方式 , 全都是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是木製的尺度 , 你通常不會看到像這樣上升的線條 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	全球人類基因組定序的能力今年大約是五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們根據已被分配的機器 , 知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預期在可預見的未來 , 年復一年會加倍、三倍或四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個特別的實驗室 , 代表了百分之二十的容量 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因組學院 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國在為新月球贏得比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	對醫學而言 , 這意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	女性37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她用第二期的雌激素受體乳腺癌來做示範 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受手術、化療和放射線治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她得了第三階段卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療來治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她42歲時有更多卵巢癌 , 更多化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她帶著嚴重的髓鞘白血病回來 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸衰竭 , 八天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女士在短短10年內被對待的方式 , 看起來就像在血液中 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	那是因為像我同事rickwilson , 在華盛頓大學的基因組研究所 , 她決定去看這位女士的後遺症 。
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他的基因定序 , 他用皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 和癌症的骨髓 , 在幾週內 , 他對兩組基因組進行了基因組測序 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩組基因組在軟體中比較 , 他發現 , 除了其他東西之外 , 有一個兩千個鹼基在一個叫做tp53的基因中 , 有一個兩千個鹼基 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你的基因中有這種特性突變 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對這位女士沒什麼幫助 , 但對她的家人來說 , 它的確有著很嚴重、很深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 他們得到了這個基因檢測 , 他們就可以去做常規的篩檢 , 他們可以早期發現癌症 , 而且很有可能活得更久 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我向各位介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在兩歲時被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信這些症狀並不相符 , 透過一些英勇的努力 , 和很多網路搜尋 , 她能夠說服醫界 , 事實上 , 他們還有其他的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的是雙向的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	所以他們得到了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但是他們沒有完全的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	結果 , 這張照片中的男士 , 名叫喬•貝耶 , 他很幸運能成為一家名為 「 生命科技 」 的公司的首席公司 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是製造大量基因組定序工具的兩家公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他的做法是幫他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們在一個叫做spr的基因中發現一系列突變 , 負責產生血清素的基因 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	除此之外 , 他們給這些孩子們一種血清素先驅藥物 , 現在的確是正常的 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有完整的基因定序 , 不可能發生這種事 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	幾年前的成本是十萬美元 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	現在是一萬美金 。 明年是一千美金 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	價格是100美元 , 或一年後 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動速度的快 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有個小nick , 喜歡蝙蝠俠和松鼠的槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	尼克出現在兒童醫院 , 患有這種異常的腹部 , 像個饑荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是說他沒有吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西時 , 他的腸子基本上會向外打開 , 然後從腸子裡溢出 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	一百個手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽 , 請為我禱告 。 我非常痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他不知道發生了什麼事 , 但是他說: 「 我們來讓這個孩子的基因組定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現一個基因突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	理論上 , 他對食物本質上發生的反應是免疫的 , 這是自然的反應 , 導致細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是管制下面的基因是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這就說明了 , 除了其他事情 , 當然 , 治療骨髓移植的治療之外 , 他還在進行中 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的辛苦復原 , 他現在正在吃牛排 , 加上一份醬料 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	今天 , 用基因組來做全面性的診斷 , 已經在我們面前了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	我們所有人的意思是 , 在這房間裡的每個人 , 都可以多活五年、十年、二十年 , 只因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想想人類在這個星球上的足跡 , 以及我們能持續生產糧食的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新一代的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 和其他農作物 , 非常包容乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植和吃基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天要講的唯一位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非在座有誰想自願停止吃東西 ?
none , not one .	沒有 。 沒有 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是個打字機 , 數十年來 , 每個桌上型電腦的主流 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	事實上 , 打字機基本上已經被這個東西淘汰了 。

so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	我最近只好買了生命保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我被要求回答:a , 我從來沒有做過基因測試 , b.我有過基因測試 , 來吧 , c.我有過基因測試 , 我沒有告訴別人 。
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我得以回答 , 我老實說 , 萬一我的保險經紀人都在傾聽 。

consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	消費者為基因組學申請應用 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。

how many people in the audience have the last name resnick like me ? raise your hand .	在座有多少人像我一樣有最後的resnick ? 請舉手 。

but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但 , 想像一下 , 如果我的基因被辨識出來 , 坐在軟體裡 , 第三個表兄弟的基因組也在那兒 , 還有軟體可以比較這兩組基因 , 並做出這些關聯 。

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫示範了他的骨髓採取的新裝置 , 很快地 , 能將救命的骨髓移植到捐贈者身上 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成體幹細胞可以被用來治療許多末期疾病 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。

so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是史丹佛大學的兒科醫生和幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床診斷專注於骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor的靈感來源 , 我沒有帶一個人的大腦 , 但我帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	我們用骨髓 , 來拯救數萬名病人的性命 , 他們大多已有較高的惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病、淋巴瘤 , 和其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植手術 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術室裡 , 這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓送到全國各地 , 拯救一個患白血病的孩子 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這塊骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.研發團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 還有另一位醫生從我身邊走過 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	包柏在桌上 , 我們拿著這根小針 , 你知道的 , 不太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是把它放到軟組織中 , 把它打入硬骨中 , 進入tuchus , 每次用針筒 , 大約十公升的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	把牠交給護士 , 牠將牠射入一個鐵桶裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它傳回給我 。 我們一而再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	通常是兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在我的手臂尾聲時 , 我手上接到一通電話 , 更不用說bob , 他的屁股看起來更像這樣 , 像是瑞士起士 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 大概40年來 , 這種程序沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	或許有更好的方法可以做到 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想出了一個最低侵入性的方法 , 一個我們稱之為 「 骨髓採礦者 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採礦者 , 這裡展示的原理 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準透明病人 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入骨頭前面或後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有彈性、有力的導管 , 帶著特殊的電線管 , 會留在骨髓的中間 , 跟著臀部的輪廓移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以 , 它能讓你很快地激發靈感 , 或說 , 非常快地 , 豐富的骨髓穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同一個入口多次 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , 鮑勃只能拿到一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 然後把這個當成是門診病人 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 , 在史丹佛得到了一些小的補助金 。
and played around with this a little bit .	隨便玩一下這個
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最終我們有兩種大型動物和豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 出乎我們的意料 , 我們不只得到骨髓 , 還得到骨髓幹細胞活動的十倍 , 相較於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個裝置在去年才被美國食品及藥物管理局批准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活生生的病人 , 你可以看到它沿著柔軟的曲線移動 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人 , 同一個洞 , 會有兩次通過 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是在局部麻醉劑 , 門診病人的做法 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	同樣的病患 , 我們的幹細胞數量比標準方法的幹細胞數量還要多三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 你為什麼要在乎 ? 骨髓是成人幹細胞的豐富來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成人幹細胞遍佈我們全身 , 包括骨髓中血液變形的幹細胞 , 我們已經用這種幹細胞療法 , 已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	近十年來 , 使用骨髓幹細胞的爆炸治療患者的其他疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、骨科醫學、組織工程 , 甚至治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們才剛出櫃 , 今年我們在商業化 , 第2.0代的骨髓礦工 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望會得到更多幹細胞 , 翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為潛在的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你把你自己的骨髓幹細胞給銀行 , 當你年紀愈小 , 愈健康時 , 用在未來應該要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最終 , 這是我們骨髓移植倖存者的照片 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者麗西提出了一個關於宇宙的有爭議性的新模型 , 它也許能回答所有的大問題 。 如果沒有的話 , 它是你所見過最美麗的八度空間模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技 。
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi提出了他對所有事物的理論
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 , 看看那些致命的方程式 。 甜心 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	事實上 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡我所能地描述粒子物理學的美麗 , 不用算式 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗且非比尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚的頭部有上千個獨立的珊瑚 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚不斷地繁殖和分成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這是一個高智能的珊瑚 , 我們可以從一個個體中取出並問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他在這個特定的地點與他的鄰居相比 , 假如只是偶然 , 或是命運 , 或什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們把溫度調高過高之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題非常愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以說是相當的有意義的 , 而且我有衝浪的疤痕證明它的存在 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這隻複方會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居很明顯地複製了他 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 但也將他們視為獨立的個體 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚而言 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的事物 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是 , 超級聰明的珊瑚是特別準備好要了解量子力學的 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學理論非常正確地描述我們的宇宙是如何運作的 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是一件很奇怪的事 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子奇怪最早的描述是薛丁格和他的貓 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個設定中 , 薛丁格是一個放射性樣本的盒子 , 根據量子力學的定律 , 將它分成一個放射性狀態 , 和一個不存在的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本輻射輻射的樹枝中 , 會引發一種刺激 , 釋放毒藥 , 薛丁格已經死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一邊 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都經歷著不同的現實 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	不管是哪一種都看得出來 , 另一個則不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每一個人只會經歷到一個個體的存在 , 而我們卻看不到其他分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格 , 都是在不同的可能性中分支出一塊珊瑚 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們 , 這就是世界在微小尺度下運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事情 , 都可以發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不代表一切都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	剩下的物理學就是要描述什麼會發生 , 什麼不會發生 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都歸結為幾何以及基本粒子的交互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動完全平衡時 , 事情才會發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	接下來我會描述我們對這些粒子的了解它們是什麼以及這個平衡如何運作
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 質子和反質子的束縛會加速接近光速 , 再加速撞擊 , 產生出巨大的純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量會馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴霧 , 探測器和電腦過去會找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這台巨大的機器 , 日內瓦cerncern的cernclider有17英里的圓周長 , 當它在運作時 , 比蒙特雷市的五倍大 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確預測哪些粒子會在任何對撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有的可能性 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子可以產生 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量是按質子和反質子所攜帶的 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這能量極限更大的粒子都沒有產生 , 且對我們來說都還不可見 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這個新粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它會把這個能量極限超出過去的七倍 , 所以我們很快會看到一些新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個動物園的亞原子粒子 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都熟悉電子 。
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的各位 , 許多人都能過著良好的生活來推動他們 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子也有一個中立的夥伴叫 「 中子 」 , 沒有電荷 , 質量很小 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相反的 , 上下的夸克有非常大的質量 , 將三分之一的質子和中子結合在原子裡 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都在左邊和右邊的多樣性中 , 帶有相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子也較不熟悉第二代和第三代 , 這些粒子的載荷和第一代相同 , 但質量較高 。
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子會和不同的力子相互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子傳導物質 , 與電粒子互相作用 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	另外還有一種非常微弱的力叫做弱力 , 不可思議的 , 只與左撇子的物質相互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 帶著不同的載荷 , 稱為顏色充電 , 由三種不同的品種組成:紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪莫瑞•蓋爾曼這些名字 , 他們是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 通過質量和旋轉 , 與物質產生交互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力相互作用 , 根據每個粒子的對應載荷 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子 , 但是我們很確定存在 , 就是希格斯粒子 , 讓所有其他粒子產生質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎可以確定它會不會發生 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的謎團是我們還能看到的 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要給你們看這場演講的結尾 , 一個美麗的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的旋轉和載荷計算出所有這些不同的粒子 , 總共有226顆粒 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	有很多的粒子可以追蹤 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	看來很奇怪 , 大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們根據他們的指控將他們畫出來 , 有些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的充電方式是電荷 。
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有一個負電荷 , 一個負電荷 , 而夸克的電荷只有三分之一 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合在一起製造一個質子時 , 它的電荷總和只有一個 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 它們的載荷相反 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷其實是另外兩個載荷的結合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開 , 把粒子的載荷在這二度載荷空間中 , 電荷就是這些粒子沿著垂直方向移動時的位置 。
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷相互作用 , 產生這種圖案 。
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做 「 電子弱點統一模型 」 , 它在1967年被放回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們大部分人只熟悉電荷 , 而不是這兩種都是因為希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量 , 打破了這個電子弱點圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它讓弱力非常弱 , 讓弱子有很大的質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	因為這個巨大的希格斯粒子沿著水平方向前進 , 電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量的光子 , 在這個載荷空間中與電荷荷相互作用 。
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力被2d空間中的粒子載荷模式所描述 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以將強力包括強力的力量 , 只要把兩個載荷方向分開 , 沿著這些方向畫出載荷的夸克粒子 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在一個四度載荷空間中畫出來 , 然後投影到二度空間 , 這樣我們就可以看見它們 。
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	當粒子相互作用時 , 大自然在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子碰撞 , 它就會產生能量和載荷的總方向 , 四個載荷方向都是零 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 且能維持總電荷的0 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這種弱力粒子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 收費總是平衡的 。
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中子 , 這三個仍然是零電荷 。
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些 「 載荷 」 的模式並不好看 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	他們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是可以發生的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間 , 以得到更好的觀察強相互作用 , 這種對稱性很強 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在一個強相互作用中 , 一個強力的粒子 , 例如這個 , 與一個有顏色的夸克相互作用 , 例如這個綠色的夸克 , 讓夸克有不同的顏色載荷這隻紅色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘發生數百萬次 , 發生在我們身體的每個原子上 , 把原子核放在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但這四個載荷對應到三股力量 , 並不是故事的結尾 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以再加入兩個載荷 , 來對應重力 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們把它們納入時 , 每一個粒子都有兩個不同的旋轉荷、旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以他們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中提供一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看到它很漂亮 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	現在 , 這個圖案符合我們對於大自然如何在微小的尺度下建造出最好的大自然 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們所知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	有些粒子的極限在實驗中 , 我們能達到的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個圖案中 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙和這些微小尺度的運作方式是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談一些新古老的想法 , 關於我們還不知道的事情 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要單獨用數學來拓展這個模式 , 看看我們能不能把我們的手伸向整個enchilada 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到組成宇宙的所有粒子和力 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張照片來預測新的粒子 , 當實驗到達更高的能量時 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	所以 , 在粒子物理學中有個古老的想法 , 就是這種不對稱的載荷模式 , 可以從一個更完美的模式中產生 , 會跟希格斯粒子如何打破電磁力學的模式相似 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要用新的載荷方向介紹新勢力 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們引入新方向時 , 我們可以猜出在這個方向上粒子的載荷是什麼 , 然後我們可以和其他的粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們明智地猜測 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中建構標準載荷標準 , 作為七度載荷空間中更完美的對稱性 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特殊的選擇 , 源自於1973年由帕蒂和薩姆引入的統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看這個新的統一圖案 , 我們可以看到一些空缺 , 粒子似乎在消失 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的原理 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家尋找更大、更對稱的圖案 , 其中包含了最先進的圖案 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的圖案讓我們能夠預測從未見過的粒子存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它的作用應該很像弱力 , 只有比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這個載荷組 , 考慮到物質粒子的奇怪現象:在六度載荷空間中 , 第二代和第三代物質的載荷跟第一代物質的載荷是一樣的 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子的六個載荷並非獨一無二 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在標準載荷空間裡 , 坐在標準載荷空間上 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 那麼我們可以給每個粒子分配出獨一無二的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	接著 , 我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣子 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代 , 由一種叫做 「 複數性 」 的對稱性 , 與第一代相似 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	這種八度載荷的特殊規則其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的特殊謊言團體e8的模式 。
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	這個謊言團體是一個平滑曲線的形狀有248維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	在這個圖案中的每個點都對應到這個非常複雜且美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論的曲線時空 , 用來解釋重力 。
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	用量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀可以描述宇宙在最微小的尺度下如何運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀生活在八度載荷空間中的圖案是非常美麗的它總結出了上千種可能的元素間的相互作用每一個都只是這個複雜的形狀的一面而已
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到許多其他複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	通過一個特定的旋轉 , 我們可以在八度空間沿著對稱軸看這個圖案 , 同時看到所有的粒子 。
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一的統一方式 , 我們可以看到一些孔 , 在那裡 , 新粒子是被這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	應該要有20個新粒子的落差 , 其中兩種粒子被patisalam粒子填滿 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該像希格斯粒子那樣狹隘 , 但卻能與強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子 , 完成了這個圖案 , 讓我們得到了全部e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	e8圖案有很深的數學根源 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被很多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美麗的物體可以用最小的尺度描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	數學界所描述的大自然 , 一點也不新 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫了這句話: 「 大自然的偉大書籍不斷地開放我們的目光 , 被寫在數學的語言中 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何圖形 , 若沒有這些 , 人類就無法理解它 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會在黑暗的迷宮中漫遊 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我試著遵循伽利略的指導 , 用只有三角形、圓形和其他幾何數字來描述粒子物理學的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家一起研究這些東西時 , 數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但這數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個生長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個位置的互動 , 根據一個美麗的圖樣 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	用大型強子對撞機來觀察更多的圖案 , 我們也許能看到大自然用了e8型態或另一種新型態 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是很棒的冒險旅程 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現符合e8圖案的粒子 , 那就太酷了 。
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新的粒子 , 但它們不符合這個圖案 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對e8理論不好 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人也不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	這樣會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 還蠻糟的 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但 , 預測大自然如何運作是很有風險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的理論是很長的一幕 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個人做了很多努力 , 知道大部分這些點子可能最後不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	這就是理論物理學的做法:有很多扭曲 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新的物理理論和新創公司很像 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	就如同任何大型投資一樣 , 當它運作不順利時 , 情緒上很難放棄一行研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有什麼行不通 , 你得要丟掉它 , 嘗試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	在這個不確定之中 , 要保持理智和成就快樂的唯一方法 , 就是保持生活的平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我盡我所能地過著平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著平衡我的人生 , 在物理、愛和衝浪中我自己的三個載荷方向之間 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣 , 就算我研究的物理學也沒有 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去10年來 , 我大部分時間都住在毛伊島 , 一個非常美的地方 。
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我父母最大的謎團之一 , 是我如何在沒有任何類似全職工作的情況下 , 一直活下來的 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們一個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊的家鄉辦公室的景色 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色很相似 , 但在有些許不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這是我在毛伊的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種很不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租讓我有足夠的時間做我所愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	遊牧的存在有時很艱難 , 但它讓我可以生活在美麗的地方 , 在我的生活中保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚相處 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能來到ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白百分之二 , 但我還是很喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你對所有東西的理論-garretlisi:我習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:是的 。 讓幾個人至少感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你是說 , 我們應該去思考宇宙 , 它的核心最小的東西 , 是否有e8的可能性 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度上 , 有沒有一個尺度 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	格林:嗯 , 現在我給你看的圖案 , 與我們所知的基本粒子物理學對應的結構非常漂亮 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這是我說的我們肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	那個形狀有著驚人的相似性它與e8圖片相符合的方式可能是其他的圖片
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 在我們體驗的時空中 , 會扭曲、移動、跳舞 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了我們所看到的所有基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但 , 如我所知 , 弦理論家解釋了電子在更小的弦震動方面的現象 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們怎麼看待電子與e8有關 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	格林:不 , 這會是e8形狀的對稱性之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以當它的形狀在時空中移動 , 它會扭轉 。 當它移動時 , 它扭轉的方向是我們看到的粒子 。 所以它會是:e8形狀的大小 , 和電子有什麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要我的照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	會變大嗎 ? 會變小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	格林:嗯 , 就我們所知的電子是點粒子 , 所以這會向下到最小的可能尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西的解釋是 , 所有的可能性同時在膨脹和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會用它來比喻珊瑚 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8就成了一個形狀 , 在時空中每一點都固定在一個形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如同我所說的 , 形狀的扭轉方式 , 隨著它在曲面上移動時 , 扭轉的方向 , 便是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	透過量子場理論 , 它們表現出點和相互作用 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能說得更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它引起了一種驚奇感 , 我肯定想了解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但 , 非常謝謝你們來到這裡 。 這真是令人著迷 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩珍•古德爾研究員談到塔司和其它的社區計畫 , 協助非洲城鎮裡的居民與受威脅的動物住在一旁 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學等 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍•古德能協助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 等等 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以去 , 果醬 , 果醬 , 糖果 , 邦索爾 , 但我們也可以喔 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這就是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前所打的電話 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一邊走到另一邊 , 從一群巢穴到下一層 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	昨天晚上我想聽聽我的演講 , 演講的主題是zeray昨天離開這裡 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇的 , 三歲的奧斯陸古猿兒 , 塞拉姆 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽過人類的歷史、家譜樹 , 透過dna的側寫 ,
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	那是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯.李基 , 他讓我踏上研究黑猩猩的道路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	當時的情況真是太神奇了
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在這已經很常見了 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺骸 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你能從那些化石中得知很多關於那些生物從化石中 , 從肌肉的形狀 , 到它們與它們一起生活的各種藝術品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想要知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張現在是個很普遍的理論 , 如果我們在我們最接近的活生親戚中發現行為模式或相同的行為模式 , 今天的人類 , 那麼也許這些行為在七百萬年前出現 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們從那古老、古老的過去 , 帶著這些特性 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	如果你看今天的教科書 , 內容是關於人類演化的 , 你經常會發現人們根據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為 。
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們比其他任何生物都更像我們 , 在ted會議中我們也聽過 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我還是要對黑猩猩和我們如此相似 , 在某些方面的行為做出評論 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每隻黑猩猩都有自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們取了名字 , 他們可以活到60歲以上雖然我們認為他們大部分人都不會在野外活到60歲
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	沃茲先生 。 女生在11或12歲時 , 生了她的第一個孩子 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那裡 , 她的孩子每五到六年僅有一個孩子 , 當孩子在哺乳期時 , 她的童年依賴度很長一段時間 , 晚上和母親上床 , 背上背著她 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這漫長的童年對黑猩猩很重要 , 就跟我們一樣 , 和學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同的動物進化過程中變得更複雜 , 我們發現 , 在個人的生命歷史中 , 學習扮演著更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長老的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿牠們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 藉由觀察、模仿和練習這些現在在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中已經看到不同的工具行為 , 這些行為是如何一代一代傳下去的 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習來傳遞的 , 如此一來 , 我們就能將這些工具使用的行為描述為原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口語語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	他們的確擁有非常豐富的姿勢和姿勢 , 其中有許多是相似的 , 甚至相同的 , 在相同的情境中形成 。 歡迎的黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會親吻、握手、拍背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會膨脹 , 丟擲石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會中 , 我們發現許多許多許多例子 , 都是同情心的前兆 , 愛的前兆者 , 以及真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 牠們和我們一樣 , 本質上有黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有能力進行極端殘酷的行為 , 甚至是一場原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些非常具侵略性的行為 , 大部分時間 , 都是針對鄰近社會群體的個體來做 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們非常的積極 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	黑猩猩 , 我相信 , 比起任何其他生物 , 已經幫助我們了解到 , 畢竟 , 人類和動物王國之間並沒有明顯的界限 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這條線非常模糊 , 每次當我們更加觀察時 , 它就會變得更模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我從1960年開始的研究至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	這些黑猩猩生活在野外複雜的社交生活中 , 已經幫助我們認識到 , 我們是其中的一份子 , 而不是與我們共享這個星球的神奇動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 很讓人難過 , 發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上其他許多生物一樣 , 正在失去棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張空氣拍攝的照片 , 它展示了哥倫比的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時 , 我飛越了整個區域 , 大約十六年前 , 發現在公園以外的這片森林 , 在1960年 , 這片森林在坦班尼卡湖東岸幾乎沒有被破壞 , 在那裡 , 小小的 , 30平方英尺的哥倫比國家公園就在那裡 , 一個問題來到我腦海中 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當全國公園周圍的人在掙扎求生存時 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比起土地 , 更多的人都住在那裡 , 可能還多 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	從蒲隆地和剛果湖的難民數目增加了 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	非常貧窮的人無法從別處購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這就帶出了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是一種整體的改善公園周圍村落居民的生活方式 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從十二個村莊開始 , 現在二十四個村莊 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	沒有時間深入探究 , 包括樹木護士之類的 , 目前最適合這種方式的養殖方式 , 非常退化 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣的降落在這些山區 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制、預防土壤流失的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	恢復過度使用的農地 , 這麼一來 , 農地就能再次有生產力 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	努力協助村民從井裡獲取淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 和一小群女性合作 , 提供她們微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的情況 , 大約有95%的貸款都回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	授權女性 , 和教育合作 , 提供女性獎學金給女孩們 , 如此一來 , 她們就能完成中學教育 , 清楚了解到 , 在全世界 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 有些事情會發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保育的情況是 , 在24個村莊裡 , 居住在24個村莊的農夫 , 與其視我們為一群白種人 , 來研究一大群猴子 , 順道一提 , 有很多員工現在是坦尚尼亞人 , 但當我們開始計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞的團隊進入了村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊 , 和村民交談 , 問他們感興趣什麼 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對沒有 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間的推移 , 當他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的必要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白 , 當山丘上層的樹木被砍掉時 , 土壤流失和泥土流失 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在發展所謂的 「 大腸桿菌生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是一個遠遠超出國家公園的區域 , 延伸到這些被破壞的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村莊有更好的生活標準時 , 他們其實同意將百分之十到二十的高地之外的土地放在一起 , 所以 , 再一次地 , 當樹木長回來 , 黑猩猩會穿著樹葉走廊 , 牠們可以在國家公園以外的遺傳性交互作用 。
so tacare is a success .	所以坦尚尼亞造林計劃是一個成功的案例 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方複製它 , 其它荒野地區也面臨著人口極大的壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們在ted的前幾天所討論的 , 正是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	有許多的貧窮問題 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量住在土地上的人 , 不是那種肥料 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 讓土壤開放給侵蝕 , 當絕望的族群砍掉更多的樹木 , 如此一來 , 他們就能嘗試種植食物給他們自己和家人 , 會發生什麼事 ? 有些事要付出 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	除了非洲以外 , 還有其他問題 , 還有其他發展中國家 , 到處都有 , 我們對地球做了什麼 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道 , 著名的科學家 , e.o.wilson曾說過 , 如果地球上每個人的平均生活水準是歐洲人或美國人的平均生活水準 , 我們需要三個新星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說的是四種 。 但是我們沒有 。 我們有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 在這裡 , 可以說是有史以來最聰明的人 , 帶著這非凡的大腦走過地球 , 能夠說出這些ted會議所描繪出的科技 , 但我們卻摧毀了我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	世界各地的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 曾坐在那 , 自問: 「 這個決策如何影響我們前七代的人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定--我在這裡不特別談論非洲 , 但已開發國家的重大決定涉及了數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是根據 「 這會如何影響下一次股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 以及牠們消失的森林 , 我越來越了解到 , 非洲的問題有多少 , 可以被擺在前殖民地利用的門口 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始到外面旅行 , 到歐洲演講 , 在美國和亞洲交談 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我說的那種 , 我說的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源可能是這個世紀最關鍵的議題之一 , 到處都是 , 水會被農業、工業、家庭的化學品污染 , 全世界仍然被噴灑到處都是 , 似乎還沒有從過去經驗中獲益 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 , 像海嘯的效應變得更糟 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤流失 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有無計可施的燃燒石化燃料 , 伴隨著其他溫室氣體 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界的人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候出現了一些問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混合在一起 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	貧窮的人受到更糟的影響 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 乾旱的狀況非常糟糕 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季來臨時 , 通常會造成洪水災難 , 以及貧窮、飢餓和疾病的循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在這片土地上的人數是無法支援的 , 貧窮到無法購買食物 , 無法搬走的人 , 因為整片土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以 , 隨著最後一棵樹木被砍掉 , 沙漠化、令人毛骨悚然 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都有 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 即原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這個聰明的大腦和這類聰明的大腦之間有一定的斷層關係嗎 ? 那種ted技術顯現出來的大腦 , 而人類的心 ? 用非科學的術語談論它 , 用愛和同情的術語來說 , 是否有些斷層 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	而這些年輕人 , 當我和他們說話時 , 基本上他們就是憂鬱或冷漠 , 或痛苦和生氣 。 他們說的多或少是這樣的: 「 我們會這樣想 , 」 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 而我們卻束手無策 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每次我看著他們 , 我想 , 我們從小時候就已經傷害了這個美麗的星球 , 我感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這導致我們稱之為 「 根與芽 」 這個計畫 , 開始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已擴散到全球97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它是象徵性的 。 根是堅固的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	射擊似乎很小 ; 為了抵達太陽 , 他們可以打破磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把這些磚牆看成是我們在這個星球上所遭受的所有問題 , 環境和社會問題 。 這是一種希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有成千上萬的年輕人可以突破這個世界 , 讓所有生物都變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的重要訊息:我們每一個人 , 每天都有所不同 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每個人 , 我們都有選擇要做什麼樣的不同 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	窮人別無選擇 , 由我們決定改變現狀 , 讓窮人也能選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽團體選擇三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 不管是哪個國家 , 不管是在城市或鄉村 , 或哪種計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼稚園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們的根部和槍擊團體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體中 , 選擇三個不同的專案計畫 , 來讓這個世界變得更好 , 了解到所有這些不同的問題都互相連結 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助他們自己的社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們有能力 , 他們就可以籌集資金來幫助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	其中一個計畫是幫助動物不只是野生動物 , 家庭動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助我們共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	在這些過程中 , 編織出一個訊息 , 關於學習如何在我們自己、家庭、社區中、國家之間、文化間、宗教間 , 和自然界之間生活的和諧 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以比率毀滅它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	就在非洲這裡 , 挑選一個或兩個專案 , 一個或兩個專案計畫 , 在坦尚尼亞 , 在烏干達 , 肯亞 , 南非 , 剛果 , 獅子山 , 喀麥隆 , 和其他團體 。 如我所說 , 在世界上的97個國家 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種植樹木 , 種植有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 和雞一起賣蛋 , 賺了一點錢 , 或只是用它們來養家糊口 , 感覺到一種驕傲感和賦權感 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依靠別人的蔬菜和雞肉 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予士兵一些心理上的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	像這樣的專案計畫是把他們自己帶出去 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以現在根與芽是沒有時間的 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	這是根與芽的重要成份 , 和年長的孩子對話 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不想要懷孕之類的 , 讓年輕人更能聽其他人的心聲 , 而不是成人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 我在世界各地都會被問到這樣的問題: 「 珍 , 你看過這麼多糟糕的事情 , 你看到你的黑猩猩從一世紀末 , 從一百萬隻到現在都在減少 , 到現在已經沒有超過一萬隻 , 和許多其他的動物一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經是森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? 」 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的會議 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是令人驚奇的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想這些技術 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	終於 , 我很開心 , 能來到大家談堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我的其中一個嗜好 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們把這些水沖到拉文底下 , 真的很糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	接著 , 談到再生能源 , 非常重要 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們關心孩子的星球嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有孩子或孫子孫女 , 姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為世界各地的精英 , 我們可以做點什麼 , 我們可以做點什麼 , 來選擇我們每天的生活方式 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 。 我們穿什麼 ?
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這會如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我孩子的人生 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 不管是什麼 。
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	人類的大腦 , 與人類的心相結合 , 我們與世界各地的人交手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	ted就是這麼幫助我們的 , google也幫了我們 , esri也幫我們繪製了gmbe國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有我們能使用的技術 。
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在我們把它們連結起來 , 開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你已經聽過了 , 已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這個改變 , 這個改變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 我們一定要看到改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	希望大自然的下一個理由 , 就是有驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以用一個完全被摧毀的區域 , 隨著時間 , 也許有一些可以幫助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	其中一個例子是tacare計畫 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你 , 看似已死的樹木在哪裡 , 如果你停止砍柴 , 那你就不用因為你有很多木頭 , 然後五年內你就有了30英尺高的樹木 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在絕種的邊緣 , 可以有第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這是很鼓舞人心的 。 這也帶到了我最後的希望類別 , 我們在過去的兩天中聽到了這麼多關於這個無止境的人類精神 。 這種人類的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所打擊的人們 , 或其他的 , 可以把他們自己從貧窮中拉出來 , 有時 , 用雙手 , 帶著他們的部分 , 讓他們改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想看非洲有一兩個人 , 他們真的很鼓舞人心 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但顯然是納爾遜•曼德拉 , 從十七年的辛勤勞工 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著很驚人的寬恕能力 , 讓他可以在沒有血腥的情況下 , 領導他的國家脫離種族隔離的惡劣政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的薩羅維瓦採取了大型的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人都盡力而為 , 但他們卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人很鼓舞人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們年輕非洲人需要的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境的榜樣 , 我今天已經聽到了一些模型 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	我很感謝這個機會再次和ted的所有人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中有些人可以聚在一起 , 來談談這些事 , 特別是根與芽計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後一句話是說 , 主持這整個會議的年輕女子 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她帶著證書 , 非常興奮 。 她的根與芽 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daresessalaam的領導階層
