she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說 , 協助她做她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	我非常興奮地見到她 , 看到一個例子 , 關於年輕人 , 當他們有能力去採取行動 , 讓世界變得更美好 , 真正是我們未來的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩分享了一些關於塑膠污染的艱難真相 , 和關於如何從塑膠膠漩渦中解脫自我的想法 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	daannacohen:關於塑膠污染 , 非常困難的真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在和塑膠袋合作 , 把它們剪下來 , 再縫合起來 , 做為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 過去二十年來 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維和三維的片段 , 雕塑和裝置 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年後 , 我開始研究塑膠 , 我的工作開始分裂 , 分解成更小的塑膠 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 很好 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	一旦我對塑膠的了解更深入一點 , 我就了解到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	不好的是 , 塑膠會分解成小塊 , 因為它一直都是塑膠 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 在海洋環境中有許多生物 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾處理器和健身房 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是很多人對這件事的第一反應是: 「 天啊 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得去那裡清理這些東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以 , 我開發了一個計畫 , 要帶著貨運船出去 , 和兩艘被退役的捕魚拖網漁船 , 一台起重機 , 一台拖網和一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我的目的是要出去健身房 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 開始將塑膠切成一塊 , 冷卻成磚塊 , 變成可以用來當作發展中社區的建材的磚塊 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟實際去過健身房的人聊天 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 後來我了解到 , 清理這些塑膠垃圾 , 相較於世界上每天所產生的量 , 將會非常少 。 我需要回頭看更大的照片 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更大的情況是:我們需要找到一個方法來關掉水龍頭 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要減少單一使用和丟棄的塑膠 , 它們每天都進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	看著這個 , 我也了解到我真的很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心在太平洋中間的塑膠 , 我已經知道有11個塑膠垃圾 , 可能是世界上五大洋的塑膠垃圾 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我不只關心塑膠垃圾 , 它是超市裡的塑膠垃圾回收廠 。
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是用塑膠包裝的 , 甚至在健康食品市場也一樣 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也關心冰箱裡的塑膠 , 我關心的是從塑膠到我們身體的毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群人一起研究這個議題 , 我們成立了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多倡議 , 正在進行中 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海裡發現的海洋碎片中有80%到90%是塑膠 , 那我們就稱之為 「 塑膠 」 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收所有人的書籍都結束了他們關於永續經營和綠化的書籍 , 用回收的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 你就不用再去想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	現實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 我們的塑膠回收率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的去看它 , 尤其是當談到塑膠瓶時 , 大部分的塑膠瓶只會被循環或燒掉 , 或被運送到中國 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它被循環回收 , 變成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶卻可以是玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再使用塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們在看的另一件事是 , 請大家想想 , 我們在 「 減少、再利用 」 、 「 回收利用 」 的前面加了一個第四個環 , 那就是拒絕了 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	盡可能拒絕單獨使用和丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案存在 , 有些則是很老式的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在正在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 用它們來取代高興和高興的容器 , 來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為我自己和家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要拿起一瓶不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶很容易 , 如果你要去旅行 , 且你忘了帶瓶裝水或過濾的水 , 和購買塑膠瓶的瓶裝水相比 , 要把塑膠瓶裝滿 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想在這裡對大家說的--我知道你們對這個議題了解很多--在海洋中這是個大問題 , 但這是個我們消費者製造的問題 , 我們可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以解決這個問題 , 做法是提高人們對問題的意識 , 並教導人們選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 有可能 , 選擇單一使用塑膠的替代方案 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些流行病的根源切成海洋 , 這樣就能拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這個示範是麻省理工學院的pattiemaes的實驗室 , 由panavmitry發起的 , 他是ted發起的 。 這是一個可穿戴式裝置 , 可以在我們與環境產生深刻互動的投影機 。 想像 「 少數族群報告 」 , 然後有一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、界面設計、技術 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	派提梅斯和帕納•米爾斯用第六感來示範 「 第六感 」 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很感興趣 , 這個問題是 , 我們能否進化或發展出第六感 , 能否讓我們無縫地取得資訊 , 且很容易取得資訊 , 或存在存在的某個地方 , 來協助我們做出正確的決定 , 來決定我們現在所面對的一切 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會說 , 現今的手機已經做到了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會拒絕 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted見到某人時 , 當然 , 這是最棒的網路平台 , 你不會搖某人的手 , 然後說: 「 你能停下來一會兒嗎 ? 我拿出手機和google搜尋你 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或當你去超級市場 , 站在那裏 , 站在那廣大的馬桶裡 , 你不拿出你的手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 上一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的馬桶文件中哪一個是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們無法輕易取得這些相關資訊 , 來協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定接下來要做什麼 , 以及要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以 , 我在媒體實驗室的研究團隊 , 已經在開發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能用一種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 卻不用要求使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭露我們最近的努力 , 到目前為止 , 最成功的努力仍然在進行中 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在正穿著這個裝置 , 我們已經將它與架上的零件結合 , 順道一提 , 目前只有350美元的成本 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著一台攝影機 , 一個簡單的網絡攝影機 , 一個可攜式 , 電池動力的投影系統 , 裡面有一面鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在我的口袋裡 , 與我的手機溝通 , 扮演著溝通和計算裝置的角色 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密特利 , 他真的是執行和設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面上 , 開始用他的手和投影在他面前的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	這個系統追蹤這四個重要的手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 他戴著你可能認得的簡單標記帽子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要一個比較時髦的版本你也可以用不同顏色的指甲油漆上指甲
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上會追蹤這四隻手指 , 並且辨識出他製造的任何手勢 , 例如 , 他可以直接去看長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	系統也能辨識出具代表性的手勢 , 比如 「 拍一張照片 」 的手勢 , 接著拍下你面前的任何東西的照片 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室時 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上 , 把他所拍攝的照片投影出來 , 把它們組織起來 , 再將它們放大 , 再使用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	兩年前 , 在座有些人可能有來這裡看過jeffhan的示範 , 有些人可能會想: 「 這不是看起來像微軟的平面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的差別在於 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他東西可以用 , 和這些投影的資料互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是完全可攜式的 , 有可能是......
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要的差異是 , 它是完全行動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另外一個更重要的差異是 , 在大量生產的過程中 , 這種成本不會比現在的手機還要高 , 實際上 , 包裝並不會比我脖子上戴的版本還要大很多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	但除了讓你們之外 , 在 「 少數報告 」 中看來像湯姆•克魯斯那樣酷炫的幻想之外 , 我們對這個裝置感到非常興奮的原因是它真的可以作為這六感裝置中的一個 , 它可以給你有關你面前的一切的資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到panav走進超市 , 他在買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品時 , 系統可以辨識出他拿起的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以 , 在他的個人標準下 , 這個選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	在座有些人可能會想要用最多的漂白廁所紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他就能得到亞馬遜的評分 , 專注在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是juan的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順道一提 , 在亞馬遜得到了很棒的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻轉了這本書的頁面 , 再看看書讀者留言的額外資訊 , 也許是他最喜歡的評論家所傳達的資訊等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到某個特定的頁面 , 他會找到我們朋友的一個註解 , 給他關於那特定頁面上的任何東西的額外資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙──它永遠不需要過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以得到你正在閱讀的事件事件的影片註解 , 你可以得到最新的運動比賽分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這個比較有爭議性 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個字雲的標籤 , 一個與該人在部落格和個人網頁中聯繫在一起的字 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個案例中 , 學生對照相機感興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延遲了 , 登機門也改變了 , 諸如此類 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道目前的狀況 , 就跟在你的手臂上畫一個手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前在發展第六感時所處的狀況 , 能讓我們取得關於我們可能遇到的事物的所有相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 像我說的 , 在這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到很多掌聲因為我不認為他在過去三個月睡得太多
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友大概也對他不太滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它還不是完美的 , 它是一項進展 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道 , 或許再過十年 , 我們會帶著第六感的大腦植入到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	在2001年9月11日 , 埃及的兒子因為無法想像的損失而生成了一場強而有力的友誼關係 。 rodriguez的兒子在世界貿易中心被殺害 ; 2001年9月11日 ; elwafi的兒子zacariasmoussaoui被定罪 , 在那些攻擊中 , 並在人生中發動一句話 。 希望能找到和平 , 這兩位媽媽媽了解了另一件事 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	9/11療癒:那些找到原諒、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	今天我們來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人所認為的不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在 , 我們覺得很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次了解到 , 我兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早上 ,
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死了 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治性的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們很害怕我們的國家會以我們的兒子之名來做這件事──我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它時 , 卻沒看到它 , 衝擊時 , 可怕的震驚 , 和我們生活中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾週後當zacariasmoussaoui被控告六項恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判死刑 , 如果被判死刑 , 我和我的丈夫在公開場合發表言論 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過那樣和透過人權團體 , 我們和許多其他受害者的家庭聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 她兒子被指控 , 我心想: 「 真是個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天當我強壯時 , 我想要和那位女士見面 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲傷中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我立即有同情心 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她的兒子被指控時 , 她沒有得到那樣的同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的苦難和我一樣 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	所以 , 我們在2002年11月見面 , 艾瑞卡將告訴你們這如何發生 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmousoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我請人權組織讓我接觸受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	他們把我介紹給五個家庭 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到了phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是群體中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他人是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我在她的眼中看到她是母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我常常遭受這種苦惱 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚了 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , 扎卡利亞的故事實在太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然很苦惱 , 因為我兒子就像活著一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她兒子哭泣 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 。 我不知道他是否被虐待 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定說我的故事 , 這樣我的苦難對其他女性來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以給予她們 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女性 , 因為我們是女性 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們必須要親手合作 , 一起做點什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	不是反對女性 , 而是針對我們 , 對我們女人 , 對我們的孩子 。

by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	在午餐後 , 午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得好像彼此永遠認識了 。

i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有見過這麼艱苦的生活 , 從一個完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我非常重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我想這一切都是因為害怕對方 , 但要踏出這一步 , 然後了解: 「 嘿 , 這不是那麼難 。

by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全世界有一萬三千人患有腹瀉 。

i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaverver濾水瓶 , 因為我很生氣 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和你們大多數人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那一天 , 當我在看亞洲海嘯的毀滅性新聞時 , 我坐下來 , 在電視上播放 。

that really stuck with me .	這真的困擾了我 。

now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	我花了很多時間在我的車庫裡 , 接下來的幾週、幾個月 , 還有在廚房裡 , 讓我老婆很沮喪 。

okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lissaver之前 , 最好的手工過濾器只能過濾200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以 , 一個200奈米細菌將會穿越200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這一定會貫穿200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lisaver濾水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以 , 沒有什麼能撐過 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我要給你們一些示範 。
would you like to see that ?	你想看到嗎 ?

okay . there we go .	好了 , 開始了 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些幫浦 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這些都是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我跳出這個茶 , 無菌的飲用水就會流出來 。

okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	好 , 世界各地有數千人使用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	它能持續6 , 000公升 。
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用失敗安全技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	跑出去 , 跑出一個新的 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	再過6000公升就好了 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看這項應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	然後 , 幾個禮拜後 , 我們成立了營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到難民營 , 取得他們安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在一個難民營會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病會散播開來 , 需要更多的資源 。
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題變成了自我延續 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但透過不同的思考和運送這些東西 , 人們就可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這不需要天然災害才行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道的工作實在太昂貴了 。
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你用計算機運算這些數字時 , 你就用完了 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這就是 「 思考不同 」 的位元 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造的程序 , 不如使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費將水分解 , 將它運送到那邊 , 將它丟到山上、河流和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 靠近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它不成熟 。 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	我們可以用lifesaver濾水瓶 。

the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 在jerry罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這將會處理2萬5千公升的水 , 這足夠給四個家庭 , 三年的時間 。
and how much does it cost ?	它的成本是多少 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	一天大概半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 用不同的方式處理水 , 母親和孩子不再需要每天四小時去收集他們的水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的來源取得它 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 減少人們的數量 , 卻無法取得安全的飲用水 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	為了說明這一點 , 英國政府每年花了大約120億英鎊在外國援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但為什麼要停在這裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	只要兩百億美金 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果是 , 每年都有三十五億人受苦 , 每年有兩百萬個孩子死去 , 將會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	帕迪阿什丹聲稱我們正生活在歷史上的一刻 , 權力正在改變 , 以往從未有過的方式改變著 。 在一場拼命的tedxbrussel演說中 , 他突顯了他所看到的三大全球轉變 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 。
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	帕迪•阿shdown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	在十九世紀末 , 有一首詩是由一位非常有名的英國詩人所寫的 。
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在1930年代 , 教堂的大腦裡 , 有人說它是回音 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩寫道: 「 夏日的伊德爾山上 , 躺在溪流之中 , 我聽到一個遙遠的鼓聲 , 像在夢中 , 遠處、近處、低聲 , 和大聲地呼喊著: 「 親愛的朋友和食物到粉末 , 士兵步行 , 很快就會死亡 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩歌感興趣的人 , 這首詩的作者是《shropshirelad》 , 作者是e.housman 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但是 , 休斯曼所了解到的 , 你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽過 , 尼爾森的交響曲中 , 十九世紀的長期、熱、天氣的夏天也在緊密的接近中 , 我們即將進入歷史上那些恐怖的時期 , 當權力改變時 , 那些恐怖的時期 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期總是 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著亂流 , 常常都是血 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責了 , 如果你願意 , 在歷史上只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當既有的秩序開始改變 , 新世界的新外貌 , 世上存在的新勢力開始形成時 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些就是我們今天所看到的非常明顯的 , 幾乎總是非常混亂的時代 , 非常難熬的時代 , 甚至是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順道一提 , 每一世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你可能會爭辯說 , 上次發生時 , 主教會的感受是這樣的 , 教堂的感受也是如此 , 當權力從古老的國家 , 歐洲的舊勢力通過 , 橫越大西洋 , 到美國的新興勢力 , 美國在世紀初 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人的權力會被用在上個世紀發生兩場血腥的大災難中 , 第二個是:兩場大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經稱他們為歐洲內戰 , 這可能是一種更正確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們住在其中一個時代 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一種 , 第一兩種 , 差不多是權力的轉變 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於我要提到的一個新的維度 , 這在現在從來沒有發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談權力正在發生的轉變 ,
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	今天所發生的事 , 在某種意義上 , 很可怕 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們已經看到過橫向的權力轉移 , 希臘轉移到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉移 , 但我們看到有些微的不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不僅僅是從國家移轉到國家 。
it's also moving vertically .	它也垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	今日的情況是 , 承受責任的權力 , 遵守法律規則的權力 , 在國家的制度之內 , 已經在全球的舞台上大量移民 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力 , 我們談論的是市場全球化 , 但實際上 , 它是全球化的真正權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	在國家的層面上 , 負責人的權力會受到法律的影響 , 而不是國際舞台上的權力 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台和全球舞台 , 現在就有了:網際網路的力量 , 衛星廣播的力量 , 貨幣改變的力量 , 巨大的金錢大筆貨幣流通的力量 , 現在是交易所需要的32倍 , 應該是用來資助金改變金的人 , 如果你們願意的話 , 已經把我們帶到膝蓋的金融推動器 , 最近 , 發展中國家的發電量比發展中國家還要大32倍 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球化的空間裡 , 主要是沒有規範的 , 沒有受到法律規則的限制 , 而在這個空間中 , 人們可能會不受約束 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在這套裝備的效果 , 可說是強大的一刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	對於那些有能力在沒有限制的空間中操作的人 , 總是很適合的 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 沒有規範的空間 , 不受法律規則的限制 , 不單單是你想要國際貿易、網路等等的事物 , 還有你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義的事物 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911的揭示是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 儘管如此 , 住在那空間的那些人 , 可以攻擊你 , 即使是在9月1日的早晨 , 仍然會攻擊你 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	有人說 , 大約有60%的四百萬美金被帶到9/11的基金會 , 實際上是通過雙子星大樓的機構 , 9/11被摧毀 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也用這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播──來繞過他們的毒藥 , 來摧毀我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	早些時候 , 早晚些時候 , 歷史的規則就是權力的統治階層必須跟隨著 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	假如我相信我們這個時代的全球化就是權力的全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代所面臨的挑戰之一就是將統治者帶到國際空間 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信 , 未來的幾十年 , 將來會是更大或更小的亂流 , 或多或少我們能夠達成目標:將統治者帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要成立全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順道一提 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 這在聯合國的機構不太可能實現 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明它 。
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一種方法 , 可以讓國際行動合法化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當我們談到全球空間的管理時 , 我猜想 , 透過更多聯合國機構的創建 , 這種事並不會發生 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	強大的力量聚集在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的系統 , 以協議為基礎的協議 , 來管理這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你看得到 , 你可以看到他們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約的以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全以條約為基礎的組織 , 但 , 強大到足以支撐最強大的美國 , 如果有必要的話 , 美國就負責 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:正在努力打造一個以條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在 , 我們知道我們必須組成一個機構 , 能夠把政府帶到金融空間 , 做為財務推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	而這就是二十國集團協定的基礎機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題 , 我們等下會再回來談這個問題 , 那就是 , 如果你把最強大的組織結合在一起 , 把協定為以規則為基礎的機構規則 , 填滿了統治的空間 , 那麼 , 那些被遺忘的弱者又會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們馬上就會回到這個問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一個信息是 , 如果你在亂度時 , 或多或少是亂度過這些亂流 , 那麼我們的成功 , 大體上 , 會取決於我們有能力把合理的統治帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看著這一切發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不一定要和像這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是垂直的轉變 , 也是橫向的轉變 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你也許會說這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 一直以來文明聚集在海洋上 , 最先出現在地中海 , 最新的文明出現在大西洋的西方國家 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	對我來說 , 似乎我們現在看到的是一個基本的權力轉移 , 廣泛的說 , 遠離各國聚集在大西洋棋場附近的國家 , 轉移到太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這一切都從經濟權力開始 , 但一直都是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的增長 , 在世界上其他成長勢力的地區 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得其實這不是從西方移轉到東部 , 有什麼不一樣的事正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我猜 , 值得一提的是 , 美國在未來的十年、十五年 , 仍然是地球上最強大的國家 , 但她掌握權力的背景現在已經徹底改變了 , 已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們已經走出了五十年 , 最不尋常的時代 , 在這個時代 , 我們已經擁有了一個完全獨立的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每個羅馬人的指南都需要被它的位置來引導到華盛頓一個世界 , 一個被哥倫斯世界給侵蝕的世界 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但在歷史上 , 這不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在所浮現的 , 是更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到多極化的世界出現了 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主要特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保留最強大的國家 , 但在日益擴張的世界中 , 他們會是最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	而你會開始看到其他的權力建設在中國 , 當然 , 我自己的猜測是 , 中國的偉大之處並不平穩 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	會很糟糕 , 因為中國在自由化後 , 將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同討論的主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到印度 , 巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到事實上 , 對我們歐洲人而言 , 世界看起來更像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	歐洲在十九世紀時 , 一位偉大的英國外交部長 , 坎寧神 , 曾形容它為 「 歐洲的權力協會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一種平衡 , 一種五面的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國總是在扮演平衡的角色 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在一個由獨立世界主導的時期 , 你有固定的聯盟北約組織 , 華沙協議 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定的兩極性 , 意味著固定的結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的兩極性就意味著改變和改變盟友關係 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們正在進入的世界 , 我們會漸漸發現我們的盟友不是固定不變的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交部長坎寧曾說: 「 英國有共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們會漸漸看到 , 即使我們身處西方世界 , 亦必須伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 與他人結盟 , 只要我們想把事情搞定 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 對西方國家來說 , 光靠利比亞是不夠的 ; 我們得要把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我猜想 , 伊拉克和阿富汗是最後一次 , 當西方國家嘗試自行完成時 , 我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經達到400年的終點了 , 我說400年是因為這是奧圖曼帝國的結束 , 結束了西方強權、西方制度和西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	要知道 , 直到現在 , 如果西方國家能團結起來 , 它就能在世界上的每個角落提出和丟棄 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不再是真的了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以上次世界大戰後的最後一次金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家合作了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金會--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在其他人面前呼籲 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造g20 。
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我預測一下 , 這可能更令人吃驚 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我懷疑我們已經達到400年西方勢力足夠的終點了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國人 , 當然 , 他們永遠不會介入到世界各地的調停和平之中 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	哦 , 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特下服役 , 在藍色旗幟下服役 , 在聯合國的指令下服役 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 11人 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	要解決索馬利海盜最大的海軍艦隊問題是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍陸戰隊
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	他們當然是 , 他們是一流的慈善家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓航道保持開放 。
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	逐漸地 , 我們要和那些不共享價值的人做生意 , 但現在 , 那些人 , 我們有共同的利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是一種全新的看法 , 現在正在興起 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素則完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們的現代世界中 , 由於網路 , 因為人們在這裡所談論的各種事物 , 每件事都與萬物有關聯 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在相互關聯 , 國家 , 個人 , 以一種前所未有的方式 , 從未有過的案例 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的關係總是存在的 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交是管理國家的相互關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被緊密封鎖在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	墨西哥的豬流感 , 24小時後 , 查爾斯degaulle機場出現了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉了 , 大量的崩潰 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯大草原上有火災非洲的食物暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深切地、深切地相互連結 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	這意味著 , 一個國家的概念獨立行動 , 而非與他人建立關係 , 而非與他人合作 , 不再是個可行的建議 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動既不受限於自己 , 也不足以控制自己的國土 , 因為其國外的影響已經開始影響到國內發生的一切 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我是英國最後一次帝國戰爭的年輕士兵 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國家的國防大概有一件事 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在城牆外 。
now the enemy is inside the walls .	敵人就在城牆裡 。
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	如果我想要談談我國家的國防部 , 我必須和衛生署談談 , 因為流行病對我的健康造成威脅 , 我必須和農業部長談談 , 因為糧食安全對我的安全造成了威脅 , 我必須和工業部長談談 , 因為現在 , 我們的高科技基礎建設很脆弱 , 正如同我們從網路戰爭中看到的那樣 , 我必須和農業部長談 , 因為在我國內發生過的事 , 這件事 , 已經在7777年內發生了 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	再也不是一個國家的安全就只是它的士兵和國防部的問題 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它是鎖定它的機構的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴我們一件非常重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴我們 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 垂直建立起來 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式 , 垂直階層 , 專門化的任務 , 指令結構完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	各位在商業界都知道 , 我們這個時代的典範架構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	重要的是 , 網絡網絡的能力 , 不論是政府或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三條法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我第一條法則和第二條法則 , 因為我還沒發明出來 ; 如果第三條法則有更好聽起來 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三個法則是 , 在現代社會 , 一切都與一切相關 , 最重要的是 , 你能做的是 , 能和他人做同樣的事 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 不論你是政府 , 不論你是軍隊的監管 , 不論你是企業的監控點 , 你的相互連結的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	在工業界 , 政府不懂 。
but now one final thing .	但 , 最後一點 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是的話 , 女士們先生們--而這就是我們現在被緊密結合在一起--以前從來沒有如此過 , 那也是我們互相分享命運的例子 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 那些支配我們國家安全的概念已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我就安全了 , 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 我的盟友 , 像北約組織 , 比他們的盟友更強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	情況不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的出現 , 意味著 , 漸漸地 , 我和我的敵人有著同樣的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官的時候 , 在1970年代和蘇聯在日內瓦和蘇聯的斷層協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們了解到 , 我們和他們有共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平已經來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著共同的命運 。
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	中東和平最大的阻礙之一 , 就是以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 都不明白他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 突然間 , 各位先生女士們 , 一直以來 , 由於有遠見的人和詩人的建議 , 變成了我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 以一首詩來結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰的偉大詩作 。
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 請不要為鈴聲響亮 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我參與了人類 , 不去問鈴聲是誰 , 鈴聲為我崩潰 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對於約翰多恩 , 道德的建議是道德的建議 。
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 算是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽生活和健康的道路 , 丹•布特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍色區 」 , 他們的長者和vim和vinvigor一起生活 , 在tedxtc , 他共享9個常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 使他們在一百歲以上不能忘懷 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索食物、健康、生命、科學 。
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到一百歲 ?
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個叫做丹麥雙胞胎的研究指出 , 在某些生物限制下 , 平均一個人的壽命只有10% 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	剩下的90%是由生活方式主宰的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以 , 藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能提出一個長壽的實質方程式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 , 他們大概不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南海灘減肥法 , 或阿特金斯減肥法 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	還有美國食品藥物管理局的金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉說過的話 。
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲博士告訴我們 ,
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於真正幫助我們活得更好的事物 , 有許多的困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當談到補充品時 , 你要拿它們嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	那麼這些荷爾蒙或雷斯多德呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的在其中嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性呢 ? 那我們如何社交呢 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們尋找長壽的方法 , 是與國家地理和國家老化學院合作 , 找到四個人口統計學的確受地理定義的地區 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 讓一組專家來到那裡 , 經常會經過他們所做的事 , 來分析這些人所做的事 , 來進行跨文化的分析 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	到最後 , 我要告訴各位那片斷是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但 , 首先 , 我想要揭露一些常見的迷思 , 關於長壽的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你真的努力嘗試過活到100歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國 , 大約五千人當中 , 只有一個人活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機率非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然它是美國成長最快的一百歲人口 , 但很難達到 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們沒有長壽的規劃 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為 「 程序性成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起我大學的日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家稱之為 「 成功 」 , 意思是你有孩子的年齡 , 接著是另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類動物 , 如果你是老鼠或大象 , 或中間的人類 , 都是一樣的 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 若要做到一百歲 , 你不只得要有很棒的生活方式 , 你也得要贏得遺傳學的樂透 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療方法可以緩慢、逆轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	想想看 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘的時間 , 那些腦細胞就死了 , 它們永遠不會回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太難 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 打破你的軟骨 , 軟骨永遠不會回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈可以堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊來連結 , 然後我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用 「 t 」 來計算 , 我們在這裡談的是國家債務的數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當它們自己翻過來 , 就會造成一些損害 。 而損害會累積起來 。
and it builds up exponentially .	它是以指數成長的 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像以前我們都有披頭四的專輯或老鷹專輯 , 我們會在錄音帶上做一份複製 , 讓我們的朋友複製錄音帶 , 很快地 , 幾世代以來 , 錄音帶聽起來像是垃圾 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化速度比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡幹什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約九十年 , 女人的身體多一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在這條線的某一刻 , 我們在桌上留下了12年的美好時光 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 大部份時間都沒有慢性病、心臟疾病、癌症 , 和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要消失這些年 , 最好的辦法 , 就是去看世界各地的文化 , 那裡的人活到一百歲 , 比我們活得大上十倍 , 那些預期壽命延長了十幾年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們在義大利海岸以外的125英里外發現了我們的第一個藍色區域 , 位在薩丁尼亞島上 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整個島嶼 , 整個島嶼大約有一百四十萬人 , 但只有在高地上 , 有一個叫做努羅省的區域 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們看到的是男人最長壽的地區 , 百歲人瑞的數目 , 比美國人多十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這是一個地方 , 人們不只活到一百歲 , 他們還活得很厲害 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	那些年紀102歲的老人仍然騎單車去上班 , 砍木頭 , 還能打敗比他們年輕60歲的人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上會回到耶穌的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它實際上是一個孤立的青銅時代文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地實在太虛弱了 , 大多是牧羊人 , 牠們的活動規律很低 , 身體活動也很低 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要以植物為主 , 以他們能帶到田野的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種尚未發酵的全麥麵包 , 叫做 「 卡塔小麥 」 , 一種由草原餵養的動物所製成的乳酪 , 這種乳酪在omega-3脂肪酸中高 , 而不是omega-6脂肪酸 , 由玉米餵養的動物所製成 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何酒都還要高三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為 , 真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老年人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會公平似乎在24歲左右達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 你越能得到越多的公平 , 你就越有智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧 , 與其看運動畫出泳衣日曆 , 你看到百歲人瑞的月曆 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不只適用於你的老年父母親 , 讓他們與家人親近 , 還將預期壽命延長了大約四到六年 , 對那些家庭的孩子來說 , 這對那些家庭的孩子來說是有益的 , 他們的死亡率較低 , 疾病的比率也較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一邊發現了第二個藍色區域 , 位於東京南部的800英里處 , 位在俄亥俄州的阿基拉威 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	主要島嶼的北端是世界長壽的0 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是最古老的女性居住地 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	在這個地方 , 人們平均壽命最長的人是沒有殘疾的人 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很久 , 通常在他們的睡眠中死亡 , 很快 , 常常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性交之後 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們的壽命比美國人的平均壽命長七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	在美國 , 百歲人瑞的比例是五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	五分之一的結腸癌和乳癌 , 美國的大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實是 , 文化產生了這些數字 , 強烈的暗示他們有東西要教我們 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為基礎的飲食 , 裡面滿是蔬菜 , 裡面有許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	美國人吃的豆腐量大約是8倍 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們所吃的更重要的是他們如何吃它 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略來避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們吃的盤子比較小 , 所以每次坐著時的熱量都比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其服務家庭風格 , 當你在說話時 , 你可以無心地吃東西 , 他們在櫃台上 , 把食物拿走 , 然後帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一句3000年的格言我認為這是有史以來最偉大的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	它是由孔子發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食稱為 「 騷擾 」 、 「 仇恨 」 、 「 飲食 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	簡單來說 , 這些人在一餐前會先說 , 提醒他們不要吃東西 , 吃到他們的胃有80%是滿的 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	整個感覺要花上半小時才能從腹部移動到腦部 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住 , 記住要在80%時停下來 , 這會幫助你不去做這件事 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有幾個社會結構 , 我們可以用長壽來連結 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會致命 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經下降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運地出生在琉球 , 你出生在一個系統中 , 你自動有五十個朋友 , 與他們同行 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為 「 模仿 」 。 如果你在模仿中 , 如果你幸運的話 , 你會被期待分享 「 反彈 」 。 如果情況不好的話 , 孩子生病了 , 父母死去 , 總是有人背著你的背 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這五位女士 , 這五位女士 , 已經在一起97年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們把成人的生活分成兩部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這代表要退休給簡單的椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中 , 沒有退休的字眼 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是 , 整個人生中有一個字 , 那個字是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗略來說 , 意思是 「 早上起床的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位102歲的卡爾特大師 , 他的ikigai帶著這種武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對於這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 他每週捕魚三次 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 。 國家老化研究所實際上給我們一個問卷 , 給這些百歲人瑞 。
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題是 , 他們的文化非常敏銳 , 那些問卷問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為什麼早上起床 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太太來說 , 她的生平只是她的曾曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩在101歲前就分開了 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 拿著一位曾曾曾曾孫女的感覺是怎樣的 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把頭放回去 , 說: 「 感覺就像跳上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得這是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理雜誌的編輯希望我能找到美國的藍色區域 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子 , 我們檢視明尼蘇達的草原 , 那裡百歲人瑞的比例非常高 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的人口住在七天的新教徒之中 , 集中在加州的羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守派的方法論者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們從星期五日的日落慶祝安息日 , 到星期六的日落 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 時間24小時的庇護 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 相較之下 , 牠們的壽命非常長 ,
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均的女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位新進主義的女性來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯 , 他們預期會比美國的對手多活11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林的研究 。 而且我認為它完全說明了這個藍色區域計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個異質族群 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	它是白色、黑色、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一套非常微小的生活習慣他們大半輩子都遵循著儀式式的生活
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中得到他們的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀:第一章 , 第二9節 , 上帝談到樂高和種子 , 再談到綠色植物 , 很明顯地少了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個庇護所 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不管他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要被駕駛 , 他們停下一切 , 把焦點放在上帝、社交網路上 , 然後 , 在宗教裡 , 基本上就在走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大之處在於 , 它偶爾會做 , 權力是每週做一次 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	這些都不難 , 都不需要花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	新進主義者也傾向和其他的新進主義者混在一起 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個臨終關節派對 , 你不會看到有人在嘲笑吉姆貝姆 , 或滾一個關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	取而代之的是 , 他們在談論下一個自然步行 , 交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻、可測量的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化已經產生了ellswhareham
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•沃倫97歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是百萬富翁 , 但當包商想要6 , 000美金去建一座隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了那樣的錢 , 我會自己做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他出去了挖水泥 , 到處拖著桿子 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料的 , 也許 , 在第四天 , 他來到手術室 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是桌上的那個人 ; 做開心手術的人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	97歲的他仍然每個月做20次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 103歲的現在 , 活躍的牛仔 , 從每天早上開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡在董事會上 , 把公雞尾巴丟出去 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子真的住在這兩個城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重開始 。
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她進入她根部的根部 , 1994年凱迪拉克賽維爾 , 在聖貝納迪諾高速公路上 , 她仍然是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾參加過19次硬體考察 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你見過唯一一個騎著腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠的人 , 卻沒有防曬霜 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何冒險比和瑪格頓騎車的機會更恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三種文化中有什麼共同點 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功地歸結為九個 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 自從此以來 , 我們已經多做了兩個藍寶地考察 , 而這些共同點也成立了 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一個 , 我即將要說一個瘋狂 , 沒有一個運動 , 至少我們對運動的看法 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之 , 他們建立自己的生活 , 使他們經常被迫進入實體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這一百歲的奧金納瓦女性在離地而去 , 她們坐在地板上 , 一天30或40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 住在樓梯上下 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店 , 或教堂 , 或去朋友家裡 , 偶爾會走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何便利 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以做院子或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想要混合蛋糕 , 他們會用手做蛋糕 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跑步機燃燒的熱量和跑步機一樣多 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 這是他們享受的東西 。 他們會走路 , 唯一證明的途徑是停止認知的衰退 , 而且他們都會有花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式生活 , 所以他們有正確的前景 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一種文化都需要時間才能下降 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 七天的新教徒祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的調查 。
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你趕時間或緊張的時候 , 會引發發發炎性反應 , 這和阿茲海默症、心血管疾病有關 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢十五分鐘 , 你就會把那發炎狀態變成更加反炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們用詞語來表達目的性 , 伊基吉 , 像琉球人一樣 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 和退休那年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道自己的人生目標 , 他們活躍起來 , 這大約值七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天都喝點酒 , 而對美國人口來說 , 賣得並不難 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向以植物為主的飲食 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略可以避免過食 , 有些小策略會讓他們在對的時間把他們從桌子上移開 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何連結 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的老父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全部都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 一個月4到14年的預期壽命值得多出4次 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的事情是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就有孩子 , 就是他們主動圍繞在自己的周圍 , 和對的人在一起 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從弗蘭明罕研究中得知 , 如果你的三位最好的朋友都過胖了 , 有50%的機率會讓你過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人在一起 , 隨著時間 , 會有顯著的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的休閒活動是實體活動 , 保齡球 , 或打曲棍球 , 騎腳踏車或園藝 , 如果你的朋友喝了一點 , 但不多 , 他們吃得好 , 他們吃得好 , 而且信任和值得信任 , 那會隨著時間產生最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	減肥是行不通的 。 世界歷史上從來沒有任何飲食可以供應超過2%的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計畫通常從一月開始 , 通常都是十月完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到壽命長壽 , 藥丸或其他任何東西都沒有短期的修復方式 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想一想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要的事情是 , 多年的生命 , 非常謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水是導電的一扇窗口 , 從明顯的窗口轉向開關的不透明 ; 一個會製造音樂的果凍 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 而且卡塔琳娜莫塔說:該是時候了 。 mota帶領我們參觀驚奇而酷的新材料 , 並建議我們找出它們的好處 , 去做實驗、修飾 , 和有趣的事 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個在葡萄牙的朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造了一台車 , 這樣他就可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他買不起車 , 也因為他知道如何建造一台車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾經有段時間 , 我們明白事情是如何運作的 , 如何製作的 , 如此一來 , 我們就能建立並修復它們 , 或至少有知情地知道要買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀後半葉 , 許多這些塗鴉做法都被遺忘了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者社群和開放原始碼的模型正把這些知識帶到我們生活中 , 了解事物是如何運作的 , 以及它們是什麼組成的 。 我相信 , 我們需要把它們帶到下一個階段 , 到組成的組成階段 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分時候 , 我們仍然知道紙張和紡織品的傳統材料是由什麼製成的 , 以及它們是如何生產的 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些令人驚奇、未來化的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀 , 能導電的顏料 , 可以改變顏色的顏色 , 可以發光的織物 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電油墨讓我們不用傳統印刷電路或電線來繪製電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個我手上拿著的小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 藉由開啟這個小光源 , 來對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家使用導電油墨 , 但近期的發展顯示 , 我們很快就能在雷射印表機和筆中使用它 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是一片加密器 , 裡面裝滿了無色光源的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的aclic只會在邊緣散播光線 , 但當我開燈時 , 這個光會在整個表面上散發光線 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這種材料的兩種應用包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	在特定的溫度下 , 溫度會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	我要把這個放在一個熱盤子上 , 裝在溫度上 , 只比環境的溫度稍高一些 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這種材料的其中一個原則是 , 在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它會指示內容物是否酷到可以喝 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧型材料的東西 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 它們會出現在我們日常使用的物品和科技當中 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有讓科幻小說裡的飛天車承諾過我們 , 但是我們有能隨著溫度改變顏色的牆壁 , 鍵盤會滾上去 , 窗戶會變得很不透明 , 在開關的瞬間 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一名社會科學家 , 所以 , 為什麼我今天要來這裡談智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是製造家 。
