i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事情如何運作 , 如何製造 , 也因為我相信我們應該更深入了解組成我們的世界 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技複合物的了解不夠多 , 我們的未來會是由這些高科技組成的 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料在少量的情況下很難取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 幾乎沒有人知道它們是如何被製造出來的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	目前為止 , 它們的存在主要是商業秘密和專利 , 只有大學和企業才能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 奇絲.男孩和我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 開放式材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	在這個網站上 , 我們和任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗、發佈資訊 , 鼓勵大家盡可能做出貢獻 , 並把資源結合起來 , 像是其他像我們一樣的自造者 , 像是研究論文和課程 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能成為一個大型、集體生成的資料庫 , 用在智慧型材料上的塗鴉資訊 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要在乎智慧型材料是如何運作的 ? 它們是由什麼組成的 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不明白的 , 而我們不明白的 , 最終卻塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用的物品、穿著的衣服、住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要了解並理解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是被tinker公司推動 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 都是發明家和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機等 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜的 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學的兩位科學家了解這一點 , 當時他們發表了一篇文章 , 用比較簡單的方法製作導電墨水 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker , 在讀到這篇論文之前 , 他一直沒有化學經驗 , 並在他的自造者空間中重現這個實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱 , 甚至做了他自己的旋渦混合器 , 基於另一位科學家/製造者的指導 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登接著在網路上發表了他的成果 , 包括他嘗試過、不成功過的所有方法 , 讓其他人可以學習並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬登的創新主要形式是將一個在大學設備良好的實驗室裡所創造出來的實驗在芝加哥的車庫裡 , 用他自己製作的便宜材料和工具來重現它 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以在他離開的地方 , 進行更簡單的處理和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子我想提一下她的專案的目標是要強調材料的表達性質同時著重在建造者的創造力和技能
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子裝置的功能非常強大 , 能教我們物件如何運作 , 但在設計中 , 內在的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	另一方面 , 漢娜的做法是規劃一系列的技巧 , 來創造出不尋常的物體 , 透過教導我們關於材料本身的設計限制 , 來解放我們 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜許多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙 , 上面有銅線 , 和mp3播放器和磁鐵連接起來 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以 , 根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究 , 漢娜製作了一系列的紙喇叭 , 用各式各樣的材料 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電的布料和墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登和其他許多製造者一樣 , 漢娜出版了她的食譜 , 讓任何人都可以複製和複製 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是最有前景的材料科學分支之一 , 讓我們能創造出便宜又有彈性的電子產品 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的工藝工作 , 還有她共享的發現 , 打開了一系列新的可能性 , 既既有美感又有創意 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的是 , 我們創造出了熱情和好奇心 , 而我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們常常從不尋常的角度來處理問題 , 在過程中 , 我們發現了替代方案 , 或甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人用材料做實驗 , 研究者就越願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造出他們的知識 , 我們就越有可能創造出能服務我們所有人的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得tednelson在1970年代早期就寫了: 「 你現在一定要懂電腦了 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是大型的主體系 , 只有科學家在乎 , 沒有人在家裡有一台 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡 , 說: 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料了 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 學習新興科技的先入為主的知識是確保我們能在未來發聲最好的方法 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入一個玻璃泡泡 , 鎖上門 , 按下加速器 , 依靠我們的眼睛來引導我們儘管我們只能看到前方的幾輛車 。 但如果車能彼此分享資料 , 分享他們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算路上所有人的最安全的路線 , 用珍妮佛的想像沒有意外的世界發生 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛:如果車子能說話 , 意外事故可能會被避免 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧:開車是很危險的 。
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教圖標和好運氣魅力出現在全世界的儀表板上 , 背叛我們知道這是真的 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16歲到19歲的死因 , 車禍是造成死亡的主因 , 其中75%的車禍與毒品或酒精無關 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定地說出 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	在高速公路上 , 我是年輕的駕駛人 , 在我面前的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也慢了下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踏上煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停了下來 , 死了 , 在高速公路上死了 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只剩65 ~ 0 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我按了煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs踢進來 , 車子還在運作 , 而且它不會停下來 , 我知道它不會停下來 , 空氣袋子的部署 , 車子全部完整了 , 幸運的是 , 沒有任何人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道那輛車停了下來 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我想 , 我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 讓汽車彼此對話 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只是想讓你們稍微思考一下現在的駕駛經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 , 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是用分散式路徑來導航 , 在其他的金屬巨人之中 , 在超人的速度之中 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指導你兩隻眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 這就是你所有的眼睛 , 不是為這個任務而設計的 , 但人們會問你做這樣的事 , 像是 , 你想要做改變 , 第一件事他們要你做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路上移開 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	別看你要去哪裡 , 轉 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須必須選擇 , 我是看這裡還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們在路上做一個很棒的工作 , 選擇我們要走的路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會漏掉一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會覺得不對勁或太遲了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數次的意外中 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它來了 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信 。 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看太多 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現有的科技可以幫助我們改善這一點 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了汽車交換資料 , 我們不僅能看到前面三台車 , 後面三輛車 , 左邊和左邊 , 同時 , 鳥瞰眼睛 , 我們還能看到車子裡的車 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們能夠看到前面車輛的速度 , 看看前面的車子走得多快或停止 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個傢伙要去零分 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算和演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能會認為這是不可能的 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	其實 , 不 , 車子的確不可能 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是三維的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	它們沿著路行走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們會在已出版的路線上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測在不久的將來汽車會在哪裡是很困難的 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使你在車上 , 機車上 , 每小時85英里外 , 車道降落 , 車道降落--我知道你有過這個經驗--那個人不是 「 無中生有 」 。
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那傢伙可能已經在路上跑了半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里後 , 有人看到那傢伙 , 當一輛車看到那傢伙 , 把他放在地圖上時 , 他的速度很快 , 估計他會以每小時85英里的速度繼續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為那輛車會在他的耳朵中小聲說出: 「 順道一提 , 五分鐘後 , 摩托車 , 請小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測汽車的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	對他們來說 , 這是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的開始 , 分享我們車子之間的位置 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有一台gps和一台攝影機 , 我就能很精確的知道我在哪裡 , 還有我多快的前進 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我就可以估計我身邊的車子在哪裡 , 以及它們往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道他們在哪裡 , 對於其他車輛的位置 , 有點模糊的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛汽車共享那些數據 , 如果它們彼此交談 , 會如何 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	鮑勃wang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬 , 估計當混亂的估算結合在一起時 , 甚至在輕鬆的交通流中 , 當汽車只是分享gps的數據時 , 我們把這項研究從電腦模擬中移到機械測試床上 , 裡面有真實的感應器 , 現在在這些機械上:立體攝影機、gps , 以及2d雷射測量器 , 這些都是很常見的系統 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還安裝了一台短距的無線電設備 , 讓機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人互相靠近時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 且它們能避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在這個組合中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你的聊天太多時 , 很難處理所有的包裝 , 所以你得要優先考慮 , 那就是預測模型能協助你的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機械汽車都在追蹤預測的軌跡 , 你不會注意到那些包裝 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把一個看起來有點偏離航線的傢伙排在第一位 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他會偏離航線 , 你知道的 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道你需要警告哪些駕駛 , 才能離開 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做 , 我們要如何警告大家 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些汽車怎麼會小聲說: 「 你需要走出去 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	這取決於兩件事:第一 , 車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上或者 , 你知道的 , 做點什麼 , 他們可能不是在緊急情況下做出最好的反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們成立了一系列的研究 , 做 「 司機州立模式 」 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用三台攝影機一系列的鏡頭 , 我們可以偵測出駕駛向前看 , 向下看 , 看手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測意外發生 , 我們可以預測是誰 , 哪輛車是最好的位置 , 可以走出去 , 為每個人計算最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 現今這些技術是存在的 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面對的最大問題是我們自願分享我們的資料的意願 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我想這是個非常令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子對話 , 我們會走在一片八卦海洋中 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它可以用一種方式來保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我不太了解你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的牌照數字 , 我不會知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在我們的背後談論我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位思考一下 , 如果你真的不希望你背後那個被分心的青少年 , 知道你在煞車 , 知道你正要來到死胡同 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過願意分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做到最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 讓你的車停下來談你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize的創辦人彼得.戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金完成了他上太空的夢想 , 讓他搭上大氣層 , 體驗到0g的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短的談話、空間、科技、宇宙 ,
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得.戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金的零g00gro霍金 , 彼得•戴曼迪斯 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我有多熱衷打開太空邊境 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這個世界的重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 真是令人難以置信 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們這個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是基因組學的archonxprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們現在所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 目的是為了在10天內完成100個人類基因組定序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有所謂的 「 基因組100個獨立個體 」 , 我們將它定序為其中的一部分 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克雷格•凡特是那場活動的主席 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你到那裡 , 但我能帶你進入無重力的世界 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	要體驗地球上零度的唯一方法 , 其實是用拋物線飛行、無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭乘飛機 , 飛越頂部 , 重達25秒 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	回到下面 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一次又一次地這樣做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 美國太空總署長久以來都在訓練太空人 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一間政府機構 , 一間航空公司的操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下來 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們開了一場記者會 , 我們宣布了我們想要做一個0的拋物面鏡 , 給他25秒的0g 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果進行得非常好 , 我們可能會做三個拋物面鏡 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他要上去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	對我來說 , 他說的非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命正面臨著被災難摧毀的風險不斷增加 ,
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為人類的未來沒有進入太空的未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在太空總署的車內 , 進入0g飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有約二十個人捐款 , 我們捐款給十五萬美金的兒童慈善機構 , 他們和我們一起飛 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾個tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整個急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監控他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	以緊急情況為例 , 天曉得 , 你不想傷害這個世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落設施起飛 , 太空梭降落的地方 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴donlichtenberg小心地將他吊在零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那兒 , 我們就讓他體驗無重力是什麼樣子的 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物面鏡之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 然後我們說開始 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物面鏡 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實是把一顆蘋果當成向牛頓爵士致敬的蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在波士頓劍橋有同樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四次 , 第五次和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七個和第八個 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他非常開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在一顆珍貴的珠寶上 , 在我們一生中 , 我們要離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入這個史詩般的冒險旅程 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫師davidbolinsky有3分鐘驚人的動畫展現在一個細胞內的忙碌生活
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計 , 娛樂 , 電影 , 健康 , 醫學 , 科學 , 科技 , 視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫了一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是一個醫學插圖師 , 從一個稍微不同的觀點來看 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我一直在觀察 , 在藝術、真與美的表現 , 以及科學中的真與美 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自己的美好事物 , 但它們都有很美好的事物 , 可以用科學和數學來當理想的美麗事物 , 幾乎就像是理想的結合雙胞胎 , 科學家想要和他們約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真實的表達方式 , 令人敬佩的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你能崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是理想的、強大的、無法分解的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時很有用 , 通常 , 在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你們可以播放一些照片 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看著我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真與美往往對那些不在科學領域的人來說是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來描述美的事物 , 這種方式通常只有當你了解語言以及研究真相和美麗的語法時 , 才會被用它來描述 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有一個人類學的理想 , 你看到生命從描述宇宙的數字中進化出這些是很難理解的 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當了醫學插圖師的訓練之後 , 我就想做的事 , 自從我被教導動畫師動畫 , 他是一位雕塑家 , 也是我的視覺導師 , 我試圖找出一種方法 , 來幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 透過圖片 , 來了解故事 , 那些對人們來說不一定是有證據的 , 可以被帶到這裡 , 並且被教導 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今的學生通常沉浸在一個環境中 , 他們所學到的主題中 , 有著真與美 , 被嵌入其中 , 但他們被教導的做法是不完整的 , 且被縮小到不見得是事實和美麗的等級 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就好像雞湯的老式食譜 , 你煮雞肉 , 直到香味消失 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對學生這樣做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放的教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我在哈佛大學分子和行動生物學系 , 打電話給robertlue 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊有興趣 , 願意改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以 , 我們開始了一個計畫 , 來探索細胞 , 來探索分子和細胞生物學中的真與美 , 如此一來 , 學生就能了解一個更大的圖片 , 可以把這些事實掛在身上 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能對細胞的印象是一座巨大的、破壞的、極為複雜的城市 , 由微機械人佔據的 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械真的是生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械人 , 微機械人是世界各地奈米科技專家的嫉妒 , 都是自我導向、強大、精準的裝置 , 這些裝置是由胺基酸的弦所組成的 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械能讓細胞移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們能賦予細胞複製的力量 。 它們能激發我們的心 。
they power our minds .	它們能激發我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以 , 我們想要做的是 , 要想出要如何把這個故事變成動畫 , 讓它成為哈佛生物分裂的中心 , 它是一個哈佛大學的網站 , 用來做分子和細胞生物學學生的網站 , 除了所有的文字資訊 , 除了所有的文字資料 , 以外 , 所有的文字都能視覺化地組合在一起 , 所以 , 這些學生能夠內部看出細胞的真與美 , 並能夠研究這個想法 , 這樣他們就能被激發出去 , 這樣他們的生活 , 這樣他們就能被激發出生命 , 如此熱情 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們的主題是 , 巨噬細胞在微血管下流 , 它們會觸碰微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁上收集信息 , 這些細胞在微血管壁上 , 被賦予信息 , 讓它們在外面某處有發炎的資訊 , 在那裡 , 它們看不到和感知不到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓他們停止 , 會讓他們內心內化 , 他們需要做出各種各樣的零件 , 來改變他們的形狀 , 試圖脫離這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家及數據庫的模型一起研究 , 找出它們是如何移動的 , 找出它們是如何移動的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	想出如何用一種真誠的方式來做這件事 , 讓它能在細胞內完整的群眾中做這件事 , 卻不太誠實 , 這樣就能避免視力發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要給你們看的是我們製作的這部電影的第一部份 。 這是一個持續進行的專案計畫 , 將要再花上四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請各位看看這個 , 看看細胞製造這些步行機器的路徑 , 它們被稱為驅動蛋白 , 負責大小相對的大量挑戰一隻螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些能驅動細胞內部的機器真的很了不起 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器都能彼此互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們會彼此傳遞資訊 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內發生不同的事 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會在果蠅上製造出它需要的零件 , 用讀取基因的分子所傳遞的資訊來源 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到每一個人 , 如果沒有這些小微機械 , 生命就有可能成真 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯的出席率真的很高 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex遞送人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做 「 驅動蛋白 」 , 他把一袋滿是新的製造蛋白質的袋子拉到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不管是細胞膜 , 不管是與器官有關 , 不管是用來製造或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人身上都有大約10萬個這種東西正在跑來跑去 , 現在 , 每一百兆個細胞裡面都有 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你覺得有多懶惰 , 你在本質上什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你們回家後 , 我希望你們想想這個 , 想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們正在學習的細胞機制 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了所有這些事 , 相信我 , 我們就知道將來發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們搞懂了發生了什麼事 , 我們就能掌控很多事情 , 了解我們對健康的影響 , 了解未來的世代 , 以及未來的壽命 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用它來發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很神奇 , 它們知道細胞需要什麼 , 才能做到它們的棲息地 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們一起工作 , 讓細胞做它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起工作 , 協助我們身體的巨大團體 , 它們永遠不會看到有正常功能的實體 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	享受其他的節目 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪.布蘭頓計畫在她的車上住一年 , 看這個國家 , 但當憂鬱出現時 , 她的露營之旅就結束了 , 在這個親密的演說中 , 她描述了成為一個美國無家可歸者的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險 , 快樂 , 生活 , 個人成長 , 貧窮 , 社會改變 , 說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:當時我無家可歸的那一年 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家 , 也是記者 , 我也是一個瘋狂的好奇人 , 所以身為記者 , 22年來 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了無家可歸者 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉了身為報紙編輯的工作 , 那年二月我父親去世 , 決定要去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事時 , 我有很多想要感受和處理的事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 我決定住在一輛旅行車裡一年 , 要這樣做 , 大概要一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓 , 羅威爾和我的露營裝備 , 打進1975年的雪佛蘭旅行車 , 然後開車到日落 , 完全沒意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一 , 社會等同於永久的結構 , 甚至是一座小屋 , 以人的價值觀存在 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 其他人的負面看法有多快就能影響我們的現實 , 只要我們放手 , 就會影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到無家可歸是一種態度 , 而不是生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車上很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在難民營地洗澡 , 我常常會吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆和悲慟 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 父親的死亡讓我感到憤怒和沮喪 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 我必須找一份全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	真正溫和的春天 , 變成了非常熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到哪裡都不能停車 , 很明顯的我有隻貓和一隻狗 , 牠真的很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓從車窗穿過來 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	這隻狗進入了杜姬日照護中心 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	無論何時 , 我都可以用辦公大樓的員工淋浴間和卡車站 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者 , 我在公共廁所洗澡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下 , 夜間的溫度會下降 , 讓它難以入眠 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	幾小時之內 , 冰層的冰層融化了 , 非常悲慘 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法找到一間公寓 , 或無法負擔得起一間公寓 , 讓我能有一隻老虎和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當暖氣讓我病得無法在50英尺外的公共廁所走到我車外的公共廁所時 , 我用一個桶子和一個垃圾袋當作馬桶 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度下降到凍結以下 , 溫度就在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一大堆新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上都會停個不同的地方 , 這樣我就能避免被警察察察察察察察注意到和惹火 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得自己無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時、何時發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 轉變成一名無家可歸的女人 , 住在一輛車裡 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有變 。 我的智商沒有變 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的誠信、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的一切 , 都一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我已經改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在憂鬱症中越深入越深 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人把我稱為無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我已經三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊裡的任何人一樣聞起來也一樣沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒有醉酒或高潮 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家者了解到 , 包括前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的人 。 你為什麼會在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者並沒有把我視為無家可歸的人 , 但我卻把我視為無家可歸的人 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有一份工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的藥的反應讓我自殺了 , 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺了 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆.羅素 , 一位全國知名的記者 , 一直在對我講國家電視節目 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 , 在他死前的那一年 , 在提姆的新書裡寫了一篇關於我父親的文章 。
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他正在演說節目電路 。 他在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆•羅斯特 , 前主持人 「 見見媒體 」 的會談 , 當時我住在沃爾瑪停車場 , 我開始笑了 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 因為它到達了那個時候 , 我是一個作家 , 還是一個無家者 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	所以我進了書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重新讀了我的文章 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是作家 。
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久 , 我搬回田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車上 , 和沙發上衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天 , 我是工作記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我在贏得獎項 , 我住在自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再被隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	成千上萬的人全職和兼職工作 , 住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化和犯罪化住在你車上或街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家者、無家者 , 主要還是看不見的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何希望 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡做無家可歸的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是要鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個相遇的乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在哪裡 , 不論他們在哪裡睡覺 , 或是他們在任何時候的生活狀況 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在一台沃爾瑪超市的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是找到方法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在泰國的泰國 , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , 米奇維拉瓦迪亞 , 帶領我們走遍全國大膽的計畫 , 從1970年代開始 , 從人口控制開始 。 這代表著很多法蘭克、好笑 , 和非常有效的談論安全套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	墨西維拉瓦里亞:保險套先生是如何讓泰國變得更好 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	40年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常非常貧窮 , 有很多人生活在貧窮之中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利方案開始 , 或是減少貧窮方案開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭規劃計畫開始 , 遵循一個非常成功的母子健康活動 , 一系列的活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以 , 基本上 , 沒有人會接受家庭規劃 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存下來 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:帶到孩子面前 , 帶到母親面前 , 然後跟著家規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭規劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回到為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的情況 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭有7個孩子的成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	只是沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 我們的醫生很少 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有把 「 不 」 當作答案 ; 我們沒有把 「 不 」 當作一個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找護士和助產士 , 他們也是女人 , 他們在解釋如何使用藥丸時 , 做得很棒 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但它只涵蓋了全國20%的人口 。

we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個小額貸款計畫 , 女性組織了它 , 說: 「 我們只想借助實踐家庭規劃的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你還沒有懷孕 , 你就可以向我們借錢 。 」

it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真正的銀行 , 但它是種基金 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來執行這個計畫 , 由村民自己管理 。

these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些小學三年級的小學三年級 , 四年級的小朋友 , 每個村落的家庭 , 每個泰國的家庭 , 給予愛滋病的資訊和保險套 , 由這些小孩子提供的家庭 。

we had condoms in all the refrigerators in the hotels and the schools , because alcohol impairs judgment .	我們在飯店和學校都有保險套 , 因為酒精會造成判斷 。

after all this time , everybody joined in .	在這段時間之後 , 每個人都加入了 。
according to the u . n . , new cases of hiv declined by 90 percent , and according to the world bank , 7 . 7 million lives were saved .	根據聯合國的統計 , 愛滋病的新案例減少了90% , 根據世界銀行 , 拯救了770萬人的性命 。

and then we decided to help people out of poverty , now that we got aids somewhat out of the way this time , not with government alone , but in cooperation with the business community .	接著 , 我們決定要幫助貧窮的人 , 現在我們讓愛滋病從這次的方式中消失 , 不是只有政府 , 而是與商業界合作 。
because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和信譽 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	這些都是商業界提供的 。
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著把他們變成赤腳企業家、小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法 , 就是透過企業 。
so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	公司的經費透過樹木移植 , 從村莊到村莊 。
it's not a free gift .	這不是免費的禮物 。
they plant the trees , and the money goes into their microcredit fund , which we call the village development bank .	他們種植樹木 , 把錢投入到他們的微型貸款基金中 , 我們稱之為村落發展銀行 。
everybody joins in , and they feel they own the bank , because they have brought the money in .	每個人都加入了 , 他們覺得自己擁有銀行 , 因為他們把錢帶進去 。
and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在你能借錢之前 , 你得要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信用權利就一定是人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用信用權必須是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠不會脫離貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	在取得貸款之前 , 你必須要接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	我們稱之為 「 赤腳mba 」 , 教導人們如何做生意 , 如此一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就能成功地從事這行 。
these are some of the businesses: mushrooms , crabs , vegetables , trees , fruits , and this is very interesting nike ice cream and nike biscuits ; this is a village sponsored by nike .	這些是一些企業:蘑菇、螃蟹、蔬菜、樹、水果 , 這些事非常有趣 , nike冰淇淋和nike餅乾 ; 這是由nike贊助的村莊 。
they said , " they should stop making shoes and clothes .	他們說: 「 他們不該再做鞋子和衣服了 。
make these better , because we can afford them . "	把這些做得更好 , 因為我們能負擔得起 。 」
and then we have silk , thai silk .	還有泰國絲綢 。
now we're making scottish tartans , as you can see on the left , to sell to all people of scottish ancestors .	現在我們在做蘇格蘭的瀝青 , 就像你在左邊看到的 , 賣給所有蘇格蘭祖先 。
so anyone sitting in and watching tv , get in touch with me .	任何人只要坐下來看電視 , 跟我聯絡 。

see , starbucks you awake , we keep you awake and alive .	你看 , 星巴克你醒著 , 我們讓你醒著並活著 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能感覺像個朋友 , 但一位真正的朋友會給你一會兒的笑容 。 在2013年的ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多展示了romo , 智慧型手機驅動了mini機器人 , 和你一起散步 , 滑過桌子 , 和一杯咖啡 , 並且對你做出可編寫的表情反應 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人 , 由你的手機供電給你的 。

not very many of you .	不在座很多人 。

that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們在romotive公司試圖解決的問題 , 我和romotive公司二十位迷戀者 , 著迷於解決這個問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以 , 我們真的很想建一個任何人都可以使用的機器人 , 不管你是八或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這是個很困難的問題 , 因為你必須建造一個小型、可攜帶式的機器人 , 不只可以負擔得起 , 而且它必須是人們真的想要帶回家 , 帶著孩子們到處走 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能是詭異或不可思議的 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要很友善、很可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo是一個機器人 , 使用你已經知道且很喜歡你的iphone作為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	透過iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造一個無線網路的機器人 , 可以用150塊美金的電腦視覺影像 , 大約是過去機器人所付出的150塊美金 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo醒來時 , 他在動物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	他其實是用這個裝置上的攝影機來跟著我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我蹲下去 , 他會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很小心 , 所以他會把他的眼睛留在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來這裡 , 他會轉身跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我過來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他會像其他生物一樣害怕 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以在很多方面 , romo就像一隻擁有自己的心智的寵物 。
thanks , little guy .	謝謝 , 小傢伙 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他實際上在任意兩個智慧裝置之間串流雙向音頻和影片 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以登入瀏覽器 , 有點像在輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們先前談到遠端臨場 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲的女孩 , 例如 , 她有一支iphone , 她媽媽會給她買一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送電子郵件給祖母 , 她住在這個國家的另一邊 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	祖母可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每天晚上十五分鐘 , 否則 , 她可能只能一次見到她孫女兩次 。

but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但我只想談談我們未來正在努力的事情 , 來結束我的演講 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這是我們其中一個工程師 , 多姆 , 在一個週末建造的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在谷歌開放的架構上 , 叫做blockly 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這樣你就可以拖曳這些語義編碼的積木 , 創造出你想要的這個機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	實際上你可以模擬這個行為在瀏覽器中 , 這是你看到romo在左邊的行為 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載到你的機器人上 , 並在真實人生中執行這個程式 , 執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有你自豪的東西 , 你可以和世界上每個擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以這些無線網路的無線網路飛行器其實是互相學習的 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們如此專注於建造一個人人都可以訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為個人機器人中最引人入勝的使用案例是私人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以我們認為 , 如果你在家裡要有個機器人 , 那機器人應該要是你自己的想像力的表現 。
