to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但是我們知道的是 , 這不是10年或100億美金 , 或一個大型的人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來將發生 , 依賴像你這樣的小型敏捷機器人 , 以及像你自己這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以 , 我們等不及要讓你們所有機器人 , 我們等不及要看你們建造什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和活動家伊莎貝爾•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女性、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德訴說著熱情的故事
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你們 。 能來到這裡是最聰明的智慧之一 , 真的很可怕 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴各位幾個關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我很喜歡 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真實的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個比事實更真實的東西 , 比我們共同的人性更真實的東西 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都吸引我 , 有些故事一直困擾著我 , 直到我寫下它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們身邊的謎團 , 所以我寫了巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年中 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直以匿名的方式生活 , 直到2006年2月 , 我帶著奧運旗 , 在義大利冬季奧運會 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在 , 人們認出我是梅西的名人 , 而我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴各位我四分鐘的名聲 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	其中一個籌辦奧林匹克儀式的籌辦人 , 打電話給我 , 說我被選為一個旗手 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答說 , 這肯定是誤認身分的案例 , 因為從你身為運動員的角度 , 到目前為止 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不敢肯定我可以走在體育館裡 , 不用步行者 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是笑事 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 和三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 穿著制服 , 要求我的測量值 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我對自己在一個鬆軟的動脈中 , 看上去就像一個米其林人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我在土耳其 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾歡呼 , 當時在街上 , 80個奧運團隊中的任何一員都在 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員犧牲了所有的競爭對手 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得贏 , 但幸運之處在於 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一片雪花 , 一英吋的冰 , 一股風力 , 可以決定種族或遊戲的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 除了訓練或運氣之外 , 最重要的是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都和熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	土耳其的街道上滿是紅色海報 , 宣佈奧運標誌 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情存在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅動我們的動力 , 決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	那就是我在我的書中角色所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要瘋狂主義者、異議者、冒險家、局外人和反叛者 , 他們會問問題 , 扭轉規則 , 並承擔風險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有 「 常識 」 的好人 , 不會變成有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會做好前配偶 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他護旗手三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊•沙蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	此外 , 有兩位有熱情心的女性 , 旺加利馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 以及許多村落的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有索馬利媽媽 , 柬埔寨的活動家 , 很有熱情地對抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父把她賣給妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 他們相信和年輕的處女做愛 , 會治療她們免於愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	在這些妓院中 , 孩子被迫每天接到5、15個客戶 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們就會被電力折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我收到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的那種服裝 , 但它離我預期的米其林男裝還很遠 , 真的很糟 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但是 , 除了蘇菲雅羅倫 , 還有其他大部分的旗幟 , 都是美麗和熱情的通用象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅七十多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很渺小、很高 , 帶著一根深色的坦克 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有深色的坦克而沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	電視訪問中 , 當被問到: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直的 , 而我不會發出老人的聲音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 在這裡 , 你有來自地球上最美麗的女性之一的免費建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不痛苦 , 不咳嗽 , 不吹噓 , 不跟自己說話 , 不痛不癢 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	她並沒有說得那麼清楚 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	大約在午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚到體育館的翅膀 , 大聲的創作者宣布奧林匹克國旗 , 音樂從一開始 , 和這裡的音樂一樣 , 艾達大遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一英尺 , 數不清頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走路 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿 , 把旗子放在她的肩膀上 。 我在我的尖端上緊握著旗子 , 手臂延伸出去 , 這樣我的頭其實就在該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的相機都在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說很幸運 , 因為在大部分的媒體照片中 , 我也出現了 , 雖然常常出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大多數男人都想去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘就是奧林匹克球場 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	當我說這句話時 , 我丈夫很生氣 , 雖然我向他解釋說 , 我們私下所做的事通常會花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不應該親自承受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	在那四分鐘裡 , 我有了所有的媒體剪輯 , 因為當老年人摧毀了我的腦細胞時 , 我不想忘記它們 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠帶著我的心 , 奧運的關鍵詞:熱情 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是關於熱情的故事
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 地點是在剛果的圖西難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是女性和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的一個死亡集中營 , 因為沒有殺戮的人 , 會因疾病或饑餓而死 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	故事的主角是一位年輕女子 , 蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵強迫她看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她成功讓七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生下了早產兒 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷臍帶 , 用頭髮連接 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的命令命名雙胞胎 , 讓雙胞胎得利 , 用黑色茶來餵他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持她們的奶味 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的牢房裡大聲強暴她最大的女兒時 , 她會抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們手上拿著槍頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這個家庭存活了16個月 , 然後 , 幸運的是 , 一個年輕的美國人 , 沙夏•查諾夫 , 她成功地把她送到美國救援機上 , 羅絲•瑪德歐和她的九個孩子最後到了亞利桑那州的鳳凰 , 在那裡生活和茁壯成長 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	在斯瓦希里語中 , 繪製地圖的意思是很棒的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是堅強且熱情的女性 , 像是蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編造它們 , 不需要它 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都看得到 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在為女性和女性工作 。
i know them well .	我很了解他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末期 , 在父權的天主教和保守的家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪在5歲時 , 我是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然這個詞還沒有到達智利 , 所以沒有人知道我有什麼問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 要支付我的自由 , 還要付出很高的代價 , 還要質疑我的父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出它 , 因為每當我收到的一擊 , 我都能提供兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義已經過時了 , 我應該繼續向前走 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一場令人難忘的戰鬥 , 女性主義的約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於我女兒及今天在這裡所有人的特權女性來說 , 沒錯 , 但對我們在世界其他地方的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫結婚、賣淫、強迫工作 , 她們有孩子不想要或她們無法餵飽的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 也沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴 , 被毆打 , 有時遭到處死刑 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分的西方年輕女性 , 被稱為 「 女權主義者 」 是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來沒有性感過 , 但讓我向各位保證 , 我從來沒有因此停止調情 , 而我很少受過缺乏男性的苦惱 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義還沒死 , 絕對沒有 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱之為 「 愛樂蒂 」 , 金星 , 或 「 金星 」 , 或任何你想要的 ; 名字並不重要 , 只要我們明白它的意義 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 一個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉一個村莊的女性診所 。
the year is 2005 .	那一年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 在她的三週假期間 , 她當過診所當志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備了乾淨牙齒 , 但當她到達那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一間充滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一排女子等了好幾個小時來治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在痛苦中非常痛苦 , 因為她有幾顆腐爛的金星 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮了解 , 唯一的解決方案就是拔出不好的牙齒 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有申請許可 , 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她常常冒險 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有適當的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些不可思議的 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢且充滿熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她鼓起了一名禱告 , 然後她就跟著手術前進 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病患親吻了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生專家又拔了很多牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	第二天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人和她的丈夫在等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉像個塞爾蒙 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	它實在是太腫脹了 , 你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 憤怒 , 威脅要殺了美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被她所做的事嚇壞了 , 但翻譯解釋了病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打她 , 因為她沒有在家準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬的女性是這樣生活的 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最窮的窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界上有三分之二的女性勞動力 , 但她們卻擁有不到1%的全球資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男人還低 , 如果他們有薪水可以領到同樣的工作 , 而且他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 而且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實是 , 給予女性教育、工作 , 控制她們自己的收入、繼承和財產權的能力 , 讓她們能受惠於社會 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人有能力 , 她的孩子和家人就會更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家人能繁榮 , 村落的繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也一樣 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai去肯亞的一個村莊 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談 , 解釋土地是貧瘠的 , 因為他們砍了樹並賣掉了樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓女性種植新的樹木 , 將它們澆灌 , 再倒下 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五或六年之內 , 他們有一片森林 , 土壤很豐富 , 村落就被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最窮、最落後的社會總是那些讓女性失望的社會 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府和慈善事業忽略了 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每一塊錢給女性的計畫 , 每一塊錢就有二十塊錢給男性計畫 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	授權他們能改變一切 , 不僅僅是科技、設計、娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性合作 , 結合、有知識、受教育的女性 , 就能為這個偽造的星球帶來和平和繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何戰爭中 , 大部分的傷亡者都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 她們是永遠的傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看著我們這一團糟 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大部分人都在問的根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個世界 , 在那裡 , 生命被保存下來 , 生命的品質也被賦予所有人 , 不只是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月時 , 我看到費南多•波特羅在柏克萊圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊 , 除了紐約畫廊 , 帶著博特羅的作品 , 卻膽敢展示這些畫作 , 因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是大量的酷刑和權力濫用的畫作 , 用大量的博特羅風格 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法從我的心中得到那些影像 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的 , 是無辜的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個物種中 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 迫使其他群體接受現實 , 並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則無時無刻都在改變 , 但他們總是對他們有好處 , 在這個例子中 , 規則的效應在經濟學上是行不通的 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	虐待從梯子的頂端打到底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧窮的男人也有自己可以虐待女人或小孩的人 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了這股力量 , 少數人透過性別、收入、種族和階級 , 來控制許多人 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 該是成熟的時候了 , 可以在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但真正的改變 , 我們需要女性的精力來管理世界 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一大群有權力的女性 , 我們需要培養男性的女性能量 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的當然是年輕男性 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老年人是沒有希望的 ; 我們必須等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想有蘇菲雅羅倫的長腿和傳奇的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若要選擇 , 我寧願有顆勇敢的心 , 來自上海的巫師、珍妮 , 和蘿絲馬達多 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界變得更美好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是要把它做好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看這個房間裡的所有知識、精力、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們離開我們的風扇 , 捲起袖子 , 開始有熱情地工作 , 創造一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市裡 , 有三千萬份餐是服務過來的 。 但所有食物從何而來 ? 建築師卡羅琳鋼鐵討論過日常食物食物的奇蹟 , 並展現出古老的食物路線如何塑造現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅琳•鋼鐵:食物如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但卻很少被問到 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們走進一間商店或餐廳 , 或在大約一小時的時間內 , 會有一個食物 , 等待著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為 , 倫敦這麼大的城市 , 每天有足夠的食物要被生產、運輸、購買、販售、煮飯、被吃掉 , 同樣的事也發生在地球上的每個城市 , 每一天都要發生 , 都很了不起 , 都市的食物全都被餵飽了 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們住在這樣的地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的事物 , 忘記了因為我們是動物 , 我們需要進食 , 事實上 , 我們對於自然世界的依賴和我們古老的祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們愈來愈多人搬到城市裡 , 更多的自然世界被轉變成了非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的那張 , 是巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些都是非凡的景觀 , 但少數人見過這些景觀 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多這樣的景觀不僅僅是供給我們食物 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們愈來愈多人搬到城市裡 , 愈來愈多人吃肉 , 全球的穀物三分之一現在被餵食給動物 , 而不是給我們動物吃 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於花了三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物如果以動物為首的話這就不是非常有效率的餵食方式
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個逐步的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計會有兩倍的人口住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 有兩倍的肉類和奶類消耗量 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市主義正在興起 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是一個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 六十億個肉食性動物要餵飽 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 事實上 , 如果我們繼續下去 , 那我們就不太可能解決問題了 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有1千9百萬公頃的熱帶雨林被砍掉 , 創造出新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了同樣數量的鹽化和侵蝕性武器 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方每一卡路里的食物所消耗的熱量約10卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然我們所生產的食物非常昂貴 , 但我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國目前有一半的食物被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要結束這一切 , 在漫長的過程結束時 , 我們甚至沒有妥善的供給地球食物 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人肥胖 , 同時也有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一點都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為全球80%的全球貿易都是由五家跨國企業所掌控的 , 這是很糟糕的狀況 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們進入城市 , 世界也接受了西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看向未來 , 這是一種不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 要回答一個較簡單的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 大約是這個過程的開端 , 是在古老的近東 , 也就是所謂的肥沃冰淇淋 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是近期的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡 , 兩種非凡的發明 , 農業和城市主義 , 大致上發生在同一個地方 , 同時發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是偶然 , 因為農業和城市是相互連結的 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們古老祖先首次發現穀物的來源 , 生產出的糧食來源足夠大、穩定 , 足以支撐永久居住地 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些居住地的樣子 , 我們會發現它們很緊密 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被有生產力的農地包圍 , 由大型神廟般複雜的神廟所統治 , 像是烏爾街的這一個 , 實際上 , 是精神化的 , 中央食品分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神廟安排了收成 , 收集穀物 , 將之獻給神 , 接著提供穀物 , 讓神不吃的穀物回饋給人民 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你也可以這樣說 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活 , 都是由穀物和收成來支配的 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	最有名的是 , 羅馬在西元前一世紀就有大約一百萬個公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市是怎麼供給的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古代食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬可以接觸到大海 , 這使得羅馬可以從很遠的地方進口食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代世界上唯一能做到這一點的方法 , 因為運輸路線非常困難 , 這條路很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就壞掉了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地發動戰爭 , 例如卡瑟和埃及 , 只為了得到他們的穀物儲備 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張 , 其實算是很長一段時間 , 已經被拉出來的軍事化的購物速率 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到羅馬事實上 , 羅馬在某一個階段 , 從倫敦來的牡蠣出入口 。 我覺得這很特別 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬通過食慾 , 塑造了它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 工業化前的世界也發生了另一件事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物是從泰晤士河出來的 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	從他們走到便宜的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以看出三百年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚類也是如此 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚當然是從河裡進來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	比林斯門 , 著名的是倫敦的魚市場 , 一直到1980年代中期才開始運作 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這真的很特別 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他所有人都帶著手機到處跑 , 看起來像是磚頭 , 有點像港口上的魚聞起來很臭 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是關於城市食物的另一件事:一旦它進入城市的根源被建立起來 , 它們就很難移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類則是另一回事 , 因為動物可以走進城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦大部分的肉都來自西北部 , 來自蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達西北部的城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦非常有名的肉市場 , 位在那兒 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽從安格利亞東部進來 , 到東北部 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像天氣女士在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥兒用雙腳穿著小畫布的鞋子進來 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當牠們到達了便宜的東邊時 , 便宜的就被賣掉了 , 這就是牠們被賣掉的原因 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何一座城市的地圖 , 在工業時代之前 , 你可以追蹤食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何被食物生成的 , 不管是透過閱讀街道的名字 , 都能給你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在前一個人生 , 就是你星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一能買到食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面你會發現 , 在這樣的城市生活是非常困難的而且你不知道你的食物是從哪裡來的
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你的午餐時間是星期天的午餐 , 很有可能在你的窗口外氣氛或在三天前出血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這顯然是一個有機城市 , 一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年的偉大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的火車旅客中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場了 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被視覺和思想屠殺了 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們用鐵軌進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	一開始 , 它讓它第一次可以種植城市 , 任何地方的大小和形狀都可以 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	以前城市受到地理限制 ; 以往 , 城市必須用非常困難的物理方法來取得它們的食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們就從地理上解放出來了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如同你所看到的 , 從倫敦地圖上的這些地圖 , 在火車出現後的九十年 , 從一個很容易被動物用腳餵食的小球體 , 到很大的噴霧器 , 到大噴霧 , 非常難以用腳餵飽任何人 , 無論是動物或人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了汽車之後 , 這整個過程就結束了 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	它是城市的最終解放 , 完全是從任何明顯的大自然關係中解放出來 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是一種沒有嗅覺的城市 , 沒有混亂 , 顯然沒有人會想要走在這樣的地景中 , 因為沒有人會夢想走在這樣的地景中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了得到食物 , 他們上了車 , 開車到郊區某處的一個箱子 , 帶回一個星期的購物價值 , 然後想著 , 地球上到底該怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物及城市的關係 , 已經完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	過去的食物是城市的中心 , 邊緣的社交核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	過去是社交活動 , 購買和賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前煮飯時 , 只要加點水 , 或加一點蛋 , 只要你做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看它能不能吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需在包裝上讀取一個標籤的背部 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍視食物 , 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	與其珍視它 , 我們把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統最諷刺的一點是 , 他們做出了他們承諾要讓事情更加困難的事 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市在任何地方和任何地方都能建立起來 , 它們其實已經讓我們與我們最重要的關係相距甚遠 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且他們也讓我們依賴他們所能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 這些系統是無法持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那我們要怎麼做呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是一個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 湯瑪士多次問他自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的《烏托邦》的新書《烏托邦》
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 如果這聽起來很遙遠 , 那一天的散步 , 每個人都養殖 , 在自家的後花園裡種植蔬菜 , 一起吃飯 , 等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以爭辯說食物是烏托邦的根本原則儘管如此 , 食物是烏托邦的根本原則
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另一個著名的 「 烏托邦 」 願景 , 埃貝內斯•霍華德的 「 花園城市 」 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列半自給自足的城邦 , 周圍有可耕地的小型都會區 , 透過鐵路連接彼此 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以被說成他願景的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建立起來了 , 但和默斯克韋茲的願景一點關係也沒有 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦的點子的問題是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯.摩爾刻意使用的字 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	有點開玩笑 , 因為從希臘人來講希臘語有雙重衍生 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它的意思可能是好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 它是想像的 。 我們不能擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 作為一個概念性的工具 , 用來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 這樣就不太有用了 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是西索比亞 , 來自古希臘 , 「 糧食 」 的地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西烏托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個由食物形塑的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們可以將食物當作一個很強大的工具 , 一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 以不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這麼做 , 希托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我覺得它看起來有點像這樣 。

here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有種植物 , 叫做凱文 , 或它是種植物 , 屬於凱文的孩子 。 我不知道 。

and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就會不再把城市視為是大的、大都市的、沒生產力的團體 , 像這樣 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看得更像這樣 , 作為生產力的有機架構的一部分 , 無可避免地 , 它們是一部分 , 具有共生的連結性 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是很棒的圖像 , 因為我們不需要再像這樣生產食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要更深入地思考永續農業 , 這也是為什麼我認為這張圖可以總結出我們應該做的那種想法 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這是一種重新思考食物如何塑造我們的生活方式 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道最棒的影像 , 是在650年前 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的《好政府的寓言》 。
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	重點是城市和鄉下的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為 , 這句話非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在要問大家 , 如果他今天畫出這張圖 , 安布羅吉歐•羅倫澤蒂會畫什麼 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天好的政府的寓言是什麼樣子的 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。

but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們採取這個想法 , 我們可以將食物當作一個非常強大的工具 , 來改善世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	二十一世紀 , 從同情心的憲章開始 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯研究宗教在二十一世紀的角色:它的教條會把我們分開嗎 ? 或者它會讓我們團結起來嗎 ? 她檢視能夠驅動世界的信仰 , 重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝 , tedprize , 全球議題 , 政治 , 宗教 , tedglobal , 2009年的暴力 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:咱們重新審視黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直感到挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我急切地意識到同情心在世界上主要的宗教信仰中 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	他們每一個人都演化出他們自己的黃金法則 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候它會出現在一個正面版本: 「 總是把所有人當作你想被對待自己的方式 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面版本 「 別對他人做你不想對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的心 , 發現讓你痛苦 , 然後在任何情況下拒絕 , 讓任何人受傷 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們強調同情心的重要性 , 不只是因為它聽起來很好 , 而是因為它有用 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則如孔子所說的: 「 一整天 , 每一天 」 , 不只是做好你該做的事 , 接著 , 回到貪婪和自我主義的人生 , 一整天都在做 , 每一天 , 你就把自己從世界的中心深化 , 再放到另一個地方 , 然後超越你自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	這就帶你進入了所謂的 「 神 」 、 「 涅盤 」 、 「 猶太人 」 、 「 猶太人 」 、 「 猶太人 」 、
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	這超出我們所知的自我限制 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道這對宗教生活而言是如此的重要
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚在一起 , 他們會爭論深信不信教的教義 , 或說出一堆仇恨或歧視同性戀的議會之類的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不太想要有同情心 。
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我在和一群宗教人士交談時 , 我會看到 , 有點像是在跨越他們的面孔 , 因為人們常常想是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我如此感激ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們很溫柔地把我從我的書籍研究帶到21世紀 , 讓我能夠和比我想像更廣大的觀眾對話 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這很迫切 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們無法在全球實施黃金法則 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論他們是誰 , 就像我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來傳遞給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如我所說的 , 讓人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種充滿想像力的行為 , 把你自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 似乎對我而言 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續宣揚或強調我們信仰的教條和不寬容的面向 , 或者我們也可以回到猶太教義 。 拉比•希爾 , 當代的耶穌 , 當時的猶太教徒 , 一邊站在一邊 , 一邊說: 「 那對你來說是仇恨的 , 不要對你的鄰居做 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉和其他的都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	教堂的早期教堂的父親拉比和早期的父親說 , 任何對仇恨及廢棄的詮釋 , 都是不合法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要恢復那個精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅僅是因為愛的精神將我們壓垮 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這一切成真 , 而且我們能用ted介紹的現代溝通來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的回應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 有一群人要用憲章來治癒新加坡社會的分歧 , 而一些國會的成員想要用政治的方式實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將會有一個藝術展覽 , 在這展覽中 , 頂尖的藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 向他們展示同情心也在所有藝術的根源上 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 穆斯林社區舉辦活動和討論 , 正在討論伊斯蘭和所有信仰的中心思想 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 , 不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教義 , 這是我們犯錯的地方 , 只專注於相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學必須一直採取行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	直到我臨終前 , 我都打算在做這件事 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我想要繼續和我們的夥伴一起做兩件事 , 來教育和刺激同情心思考 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經失去了同情心
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為這只是對一個人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但 , 當然 , 如果你只是想一想 , 你就不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這麼做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望他們能讓媒體參與其中 , 因為媒體能協助解決一些我們對他人刻板印象深刻的看法 , 正將我們彼此分開 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也是一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能夠了解動態 , 一種充滿同情心的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	此外 , 它也需要急性智能 , 而不只是愚蠢的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要呼籲學者 , 去探索他們自己以及他人的傳統中 , 同情的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 鼓勵他們對無情的演講有敏感性的敏感度 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這篇憲章 , 不論他們的信仰或缺乏信仰 , 他們都覺得有能力去挑戰不滿足的言論 , 不忠誠的論點來自他們的宗教領袖、他們的政治領袖 , 來自產業的首長 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來沒有想過要把這篇文章放上網 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我仍然被困在一個舊式的世界裡 , 一大堆巴芬坐在一個房間裡 , 然後又被引用了另一種奇怪的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted向我介紹了一種全新的思考方式和展示想法 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為這就是ted最棒的地方 。

and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有些時候 , 問題似乎很明顯 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想引用最後的作者 , 作者是英國作家 , 牛津作家 , 我不太常引用李威士的話 。
but he wrote one thing that stuck in my mind ever since i read it when i was a schoolgirl .	但他寫了一句話 , 自從我在學校時讀到它時 , 心中總是牢記在我腦中 。
it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的書《四愛》中 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 當兩個人凝視著 , 拼命地凝視著對方的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	接著 , 他把這個和友誼比較 , 兩個人站在一邊 , 肩膀肩膀肩膀上 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不一定要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們對 「 vey 」 的小小考慮中 , 我感到非常強烈 , 當所有不同說服的人聚在一起 , 為共同的目標努力 , 工作的差異就融化了 。
and we learn amity .	我們學會了 「 性 」 。
and we learn to live together and to get to know one another .	我們學會了一起生活 , 去認識彼此 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。

i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我經常管理好自己的延伸 , 所以從來沒有想過要讀這段指示 , 但我終於搞懂了 。 我必須弄清楚 , 因為隨著邀請的出現 , 恐怕的是 , 沒有投影機 , 所以 , 把這些汽車帶到不必要的另一種形式 , 再也不必要 。
now , i could talk about something that i'm known for , something that would be particularly appropriate for many of the more technically minded people here , or i could talk about something i really care about .	現在 , 我可以談談我所知道的一些東西 , 一些特別適合在座更多專業的人們 , 或我可以談談我真正關心的事物 。

now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	為什麼我特別在乎羅馬呢 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	60年代後期 , 我到羅德島設計學院念建築
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 能在去年、第五年 , 身為學生 , 在羅馬 , 改變了我的人生 。
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	最不是因為我花了頭四年的時間住在家裡 , 每天開車回家 , 開車回家 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了1960年代 , 讀到他們 , 我知道他們很有趣 。 我錯過了他們 , 但是我在羅馬度過了非凡的一年 , 那個地方從來沒有出現在我腦海中 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 每當有機會時 , 我都會嘗試去做些什麼 , 或為它做點什麼 。
i also make drawings to help people understand things .	我也畫圖來幫助人們理解事物 。
things that i want them to believe i understand .	我希望他們相信我所理解的事 。
and that's what i do as an illustrator , that's my job .	身為一個插畫家 , 我的工作就是這樣 。
so , i'm going to show you some pictures of rome .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些羅馬的照片 。
i've made a lot of drawings of rome over the years .	多年來 , 我畫了很多羅馬的圖 。
these are just drawings of rome . i get back as often as possible i need to .	這些只是羅馬的圖畫 。 我盡可能多回去 。
all different materials , all different styles , all different times , drawings from sketchbooks looking at the details of rome .	所有不同的材料 , 各種風格 , 各種不同的時代 , 從草圖書籍 , 看羅馬的細節 。
part of the reason i'm showing you these is that it sort of helps illustrate this process i go through of trying to figure out what it is i feel about rome and why i feel it .	我給你們看這些的原因有一部分是因為它可以說明我所經歷的這個過程 , 試圖找出我對羅馬的感覺 , 以及我為什麼會有這種感覺 。
these are sketches of some of the little details .	這些是一些細節的草圖 。
rome is a city full of surprises .	羅馬是個充滿驚喜的城市 。
i mean , we're talking about unusual perspectives , we're talking about narrow little winding streets that suddenly open into vast , sundrenched piazzas never , though , piazzas that are not humanly scaled .	我的意思是 , 我們在談非比尋常的觀點 , 我們在談的是狹窄的小小的風路 , 突然間通行到廣闊的陽光下 , 人類從來沒有過那種廣闊的廣場 。
part of the reason for that is the fact that they grew up organically .	部分的原因是 , 他們在有機的環境中成長 。
that amazing juxtaposition of old and new , the bits of light that come down between the buildings that sort of create a map that's traveling above your head of usually blue especially in the summer compared to the map that you would normally expect to see of conventional streets .	新舊和新舊有驚人的交叉點 , 建築物之間的細小的光線 , 像是在你腦海上方移動的地圖 , 特別是在夏天 , 相較於一般的街道 , 相較之下 , 你通常會看到的地圖 。
and i began to think about how i could communicate this in book form .	我開始思考我要如何用書本形式來溝通這件事 。
how could i share my sense of rome , my understanding of rome ?	我要如何分享我對羅馬的感受 , 我對羅馬的理解 ?
and i'm going to show you a bunch of dead ends , basically .	基本上我會給你們看一堆死胡同 。
the primary reason for all these dead ends is when if you're not quite sure where you're going , you're certainly not going to get there with any kind of efficiency .	所有這些死胡同的主要原因是如果你不太確定自己要去哪裡 , 你絕對不會達到那樣的效率 。
here's a little map . and i thought of maps at the beginning ; maybe i should just try and do a little atlas of my favorite streets and connections in rome .	這是一張小地圖 。 我一開始就想過地圖 , 也許我應該試著在羅馬做一些我最喜歡的街道和連結 。

maybe that line of text could be a story to help give some human aspect to this .	也許這一行的文字可以是一個故事 , 來協助我們對此有一些人性的觀點 。
maybe i should get away from this map completely , and really be honest about wanting to show you my favorite bits and pieces of rome and simply kick a soccer ball in the air which happens in so many of the squares in the city and let it bounce off of things . and i'll simply explain what each of those things is that the soccer ball hits .	也許我應該完全遠離這張地圖 , 誠實的說 , 想要給你們看我最喜歡的羅馬的部分 , 並在空氣中踢足球 , 在城市中有這麼多的正方形 , 讓它反彈 。 我會簡單的解釋一下 , 足球擊中了什麼 。
that seemed like a sort of a cheap shot .	這似乎是個很便宜的機會 。
but even though i just started this presentation , this is not the first thing that i tried to do and i was getting sort of desperate .	但即使我剛開始這場演說 , 這不是我嘗試要做的第一件事 , 我有點急迫 。
eventually , i realized that i had really no content that i could count on , so i decided to move towards packaging .	最終 , 我了解到我沒有什麼可以依賴的內容 , 所以我決定搬到包裝上 。

but one of the ideas that emerged from some of those sketches was the notion of traveling through rome in different vehicles at different speeds in order to show the different aspects of rome .	但從這些草圖中衍生出來的一個想法 , 是透過不同速度的交通工具穿越羅馬的概念 , 來展現羅馬的不同面向 。
sort of an overview of rome and the plan that you might see from a dirigible .	有點像是羅馬的總觀 , 和你從可怕的角度所看到的計劃 。
quick snapshots of things you might see from a speeding motor scooter , and very slow walking through rome , you might be able to study in more detail some of the wonderful surfaces and whatnot that you come across .	很快地 , 你從速度超速的摩托車司機看到的景象 , 走過羅馬 , 你也許可以更詳細地研究一些美妙的表面 , 和你所經歷的一切 。
anyways , i went back to the dirigible notion .	總之 , 我回到了可怕的概念 。

this thing would be flying over or past or be parked in front of , but it would be like having a ruler sort of travel through the pages without being a ruler .	這東西會飛越或者飛越或是停在前面 , 但就像是有一把尺子穿越頁面 , 而不是尺子 。
not that you know how long number 11 actually is , but you would be able to compare number 11 against the pantheon with number 11 against the baths of caracalla , and so on and so forth . if you were interested .	不是說你知道11號到底有多長 , 但你能把11號和萬神廟做比較 , 和卡拉卡拉浴場做比較 , 以此類推 。 如果你有興趣的話 。

unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 這是個問題:它們靠得太近了 , 而當你在可怕的情況下 , 你必須非常小心尖刺 。

waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務生趕上了 , 但已經太遲了 。

right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	透過廣場廣場德拉•羅頓達 , 在萬神廟的前面 , 再次令人毛骨悚然 , 終於開始工作 。

that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但似乎還不夠傳達我想要傳達的關於羅馬的任何事 。

and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不 , 我只會把我最喜歡的零件和碎片放到萬神廟裡 , 然後保持它的尺度 , 這樣你就可以看見聖誕節的頂端 , 和塞斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 和巴拉曼特的聖殿 , 一邊站在這個神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一幅畫 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮拉尼認識escher了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我開始失去控制權 , 也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	這裡有一條很薄的藍色線 , 有點累人 , 穿過了這條線 , 讓所有路線結合在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在幹什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不僅僅是用來收集和儲存資訊的好方法 , 它是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝下來 , 我們認為它們是頁面 , 用一種特定的方式去做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想像成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個層次地平行的層次 , 垂直的層次 , 我想 , 只要剝下一張頁面 , 就可以讓我用正確的方式來思考 , 可以讓我呈現出層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	在羅馬大部分建築物的牆壁上 , 黏土覆蓋了這些傷疤 ; 當這些建築物被適應時 , 數世紀以來 , 改變的傷疤已經被摧毀了 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁 , 讓你把它展開 , 你就會看到我所說的疤痕組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 把小窗戶縮小是很重要的 , 因為壞傢伙要來了 , 等等 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	所有的適應措施都埋藏在黏土裡 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這張palazo的頁面給你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也可以給你看那些壯觀的建築物的角落 , 那些巨大的石塊 , 或用磚頭和黏土做成的假石塊 , 這種東西比較常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它變得有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你從那些狹窄的小街上帶到其中一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 藉由使用雙大門檻摺疊頁面 , 如果你像我一樣小時候在讀一本彈出書 , 你希望把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把頭上的頁面包在那廣場上 , 就在那短暫的時間內 。

ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	好 , 如果我不完全打開這本書 , 如果我把它打開90度 , 我們會從萬神廟的前面看下去 , 我們會從最上面看下去 , 或多或少在正方形上方 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書翻過來 , 我們就在萬神廟的正面 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有任何秘訣 , 只是本書沒有完全打開 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我會把它內部做出來 , 甚至可以把摺痕和唯一部分開放的書做結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	所以 , 我們進入萬神廟 , 它會成長 , 諸如此類 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我在正確的軌道上 , 但它似乎失去了它的人性 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 總是有件好事 , 如果你想要讓人們注意看一本書 , 一路上接收信息 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 讓我大吃一驚 ,
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果那是一只寄宿鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德西 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果一個標題行得通 , 就用它吧 。 但那會是一個經過羅馬的旅程 , 展示我喜歡羅馬的所有東西 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	一隻鴿子坐在教堂頂端 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天起床 , 做一般的鴿子事 。 回來後 , 整個地方都被支架和綠色網絡覆蓋著 , 沒有辦法讓這隻鴿子回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以現在它是隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找到另一個居住地 , 這樣才能讓我通過我最喜歡的目錄 , 從最高的鴿子開始 , 以此類推 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人同住 ; 這不一定是好事 , 但它確實能讓鴿子再次聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我在想 , 這有點有趣 , 但也許有一個人應該用某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會到哪裡去 , 把他們帶到危險的地方 , 什麼都沒有 , 他們和這個傢伙成了朋友 , 學會了為他製作戲法 , 在午餐時間娛樂他 , 諸如此類 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	老人和這些鴿子之間有著真實的連結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 。 他在故事結束時真的生病了 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , 艾爾多 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在三、四天沒見到他之後 , 出現了一天 , 他住在這個小車庫裡 , 然後拼他的名字 , 飛來飛去 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	他終於有了足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子到屋頂上 , 所有鴿子 , 一頭紅色的氣球 , 都在等著他 , 然後他們把他帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到:每當他丟了一隻鴿子時 , 他都會把那隻鴿子帶到城牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在古羅馬時期 , 死者從來沒有埋藏在牆裡 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很棒的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我走過了...再說一次 , 如果包裝沒有用 , 如果故事沒有去任何地方 , 我只想出了頭銜 , 希望頭銜能把我踢向正確的方向 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時它的確把我關注得夠專注 , 我甚至會寫一篇標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些頁面最終讓我找到了解決方案 , 也是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她把一封信寄給一位愛慕的鴿子 , 住在羅馬城外的一個人 , 和一個城市裡的另一個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	這隻鴿子正飛向阿巴尼亞的上方 。
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松樹等等 , 一路上都是如此 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅色線 , 你看到鴿子的軌跡 , 如果你看不到紅色線 , 你就是鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它變得有必要性且可能性 , 試圖傳達那種感覺 , 那種感覺會像飛越城市而不動的感覺 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了cestius的金字塔 , 這些對你來說似乎很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒有去過羅馬 , 穿過大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一些最可愛的鴿子沒有做的事:它走了一條景色的路線 , 這是我覺得有必要把這本書延伸到四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞著羅馬競技場繞圈 , 穿越了宇宙教堂的聖母堂 , 以及海克力士神廟 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們差點撞上了由米開朗基羅所設計的palazofarnese的角落 , 建造的石頭是從羅馬競技場狹窄逃脫的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們向下穿過柬埔寨的fiori 。
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這完全是把任何觀點規則都拒絕了的 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點規則是 , 如果它看起來可信 , 你成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著找出消失點在哪裡 ; 這裡有幾個點在火星上 , 還有一些在克雷蒙那州 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在聖母堂前面的廣場中 , 在那裡 , 一個足球賽正在進行中 , 我們被足球撞擊 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是被足球擊中的可怕例子 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的片段:聖誕老人瑪麗亞.戴拉.帕斯 , 有一個足球 , 一隻小鳥翅膀什麼都沒發生 , 所以我必須重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看到聖誕老人瑪麗亞.戴拉的步調 , 這些書非常靈活 , 非常互動 , 只要轉個頭 , 轉個頭 , 轉向另一邊 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到紅色線上的影響力 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥兒在中世紀的高塔上自行拉下了一座中世紀的塔 , 前往聖地阿根尼斯教堂的中世紀教堂 , 沿著穹頂向下看 , 向下看向廣場的納佛納粹 , 我們已經看到並飛過了好幾次 ; 伯尼的雕像有四條河流 , 經過美麗的布羅米諾瓦索 , 在26英尺深的天堂上停下來 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們就可以在裡頭亂轉 , 因為我們在飛 , 我們不用費心在這個特別的時刻 , 重力 , 所以這幅圖可以在頁面上隨時隨地方位 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會變得有點自在 ; 用這種方式模仿建築物並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過了一道美麗的牆 , 充滿了我剛才提到的混音帶 ; 美麗的雕刻裝在 「 新生 」 上方的牆壁上 , 等等 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後 , 我們到達了帕拉索的庭院 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從這隻鳥的腿上移除了這條訊息 , 這是牠說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著畫板 , 我們會看到他正在畫的其實是鴿子剛完成的旅程的地圖 , 紅色的線會延伸到所有的畫面 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的研究者skylarlartibbits自行組合的概念是 , 與其建造一些東西 , 我們可以創造出一些材料 , 讓它們自行組合 , 就像一股dna短片一樣 。 這是個大概念 , 在初期的階段 。 tibbits告訴我們三個自組裝未來的樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	skylarlartibbits:我們能創造出能自己的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向各位展示我們製造東西的未來 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快我們的建築物和機器就會自行組合、複製、修復它們自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我將向你們展示我相信是目前的製造業狀態 , 然後將它與一些自然的系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓兩年半的時間 , 五十萬到一百萬個零件 , 相當複雜、令人興奮的新技術 , 鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器可以帶我們進入太空五年--250萬個零件 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你看看自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬奈秒折疊 , 或是有三十億鹼基對的dna , 大約一小時就可以複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中有這麼多複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建造的東西 , 遠遠比任何我們可以建造的東西都還要更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎從來沒有犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們能修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以 , 自然系統有一點非常有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把這些翻譯成我們建設的環境 , 那麼我們就有一些令人興奮的潛力來建造東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵在於自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想在實體環境中使用自我組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建造的東西的複雜性 , 像是我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要將它解碼成簡單的序列--基本上就是建築物的運作方式的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的零件 , 可以使用該序列來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能激活的能量 , 讓我們的零件從程式中折疊起來 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的矯正措施 , 以確保我們已經成功地建構出我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以 , 我要給你們看一些計畫 , 是我麻省理工學院同事和麻省理工學院的一些計畫 , 正致力於達成這個自我組合的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩種是巨型機器人和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些專案是大規模的可重組的機器人-8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們嵌入了機械電子裝置 , 感測器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你將你想摺的東西解碼成一串的角度120 , 負120 , 負120 , 0 , 120 , 負120 , 負120 , 像這樣 。 所以 , 一連串的角度 , 或轉彎 , 你將這序列發送到弦中 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每一個單位都帶著它的消息--負120--它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到達那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 在這個專案上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的能帶來光明:這真的是可擴展的嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 很多男人小時 , 為了製作這八英尺高的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個放大尺度嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人裝進每個部位嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題是 , 看向被動的本質 , 或被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它更進一步 , 它嘗試著實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	基本上 , 它嵌入了最基礎的計算機積木 , 數位邏輯閘道 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是nandgate.
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	有一個四面體 , 就是將要做計算的大門 , 你有兩個輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 當你在建構你的磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一個是從先前的磚塊上取下來的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你一個3d空間的輸出值 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著 , 使用者可以開始把他們想要的磚頭加進去 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算出它之前的行為 , 以及你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動 , 上下或下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左手邊 , 輸入等於0的輸出值 , 下降了 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 上升了 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這真正的意思是 , 我們的結構現在包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們把所有的資訊嵌入在建構之中 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	那就表示 , 我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱之為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含了精確的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以取代一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有本地的資訊都嵌入在你身上 , 告訴你如何修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有爬上去閱讀的東西 , 並且在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 , 沒有外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以 , 我將要展示的最後一個專案叫做偏頗鏈 , 它可能是目前被動自組裝系統中最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以需要可重組性和可編程性 , 讓它成為完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一連串的元素
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每一個元素都完全一模一樣 , 且它們有偏見 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以 , 每條鏈 , 或每一個元素 , 都想要向右或向左或向左 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組合電鏈時 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每一個單位是否應該向左或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你搖晃鏈時 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的結構 , 在這個例子中 , 一個螺旋 , 或者 , 在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體旁邊 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以基本上你可以設計任何立體形狀或單面的 , 二維的設計 , 完全被動地進入這條鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼關於未來 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想這告訴我們 , 自我組裝、複製、修復的可能性 , 存在於我們的實體結構、建築物、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些地方有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那之後 , 你就有了新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 我們所有的磚塊都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的平行電腦運算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	對於這點 , 這是很令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以 , 我認為我剛剛展示的這些專案 , 只是朝向未來的一小步 , 如果我們將這些新技術應用在一個新的自組裝世界中 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了非洲大陸的地圖 , 甚至去了海底深處的兩次 。 下一代要探索什麼 ? 生物學家和探險家沃爾夫提出了這個答案:幾乎所有事情 。 我們都可以開始 , 他說 , 帶著那些看不見的小世界開始探索 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾菲:還有什麼要去探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡榮耀一位偉大的二十世紀探險家 , roychapmanandrews 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	安德魯斯在美國自然歷史博物館的時期 , 帶領了一系列的探險 , 前往未被發現的區域 , 就像這裡的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個很棒的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說 , 他後來是印第安那瓊斯角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛特市時 , 我向一群中學學生演講 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 如果在ted演說中 , 有什麼比在ted演說更恐怖的話 , 它會試著把焦點放在一個45分鐘的演說中 , 一群12歲的孩子的注意力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講結束後 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時開始 , 我一直被困在一個問題上 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問: 「 我們該去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 很多人有一種感覺 , 就是地球上最偉大的探索時代已經結束了 , 在下一代 , 他們得要去外太空或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索事物 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有什麼值得我們去探索的重要性嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回想起生物學史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , 馬丁圖斯•貝耶金克 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , beijerinck開始發現菸草鑲嵌疾病的起因 。
