what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他的做法是從菸草植物中取出受感染的汁液 , 然後用越來越小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他到達了那個時候 , 他覺得一定有什麼東西比當時最小的生命形式還要小 , 更小的東西 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘經紀人出了個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 的拉丁文
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒組成地球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 比所有其他形式生命形式的基因信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 已經有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關的應用 , 像是天花的消滅 , 預防子宮頸癌的出現 , 現在我們知道 , 人類乳突病毒大部分是由人類乳突病毒所引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現 , 這不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約一百多年前 , beijerinck發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們卻不知道組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索那些看不見的世界 , 像是深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得更好 , 不僅僅是表面上滑動 , 看看特定物種的個別基因組 , 還可以看完整的微生物群落 , 還有我們周遭的微生物群落 , 以及記錄所有這些物種的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚之間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織中 , 我們現在定期這麼做 , 來找出造成未知的爆發原因 , 正是造成這些疾病的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓各位了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從你們每一個人身上取下了鼻子代謝 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會找呼吸道病毒 , 像是流行性感冒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究基因信息 , 我們會看到一些常見的嫌疑犯 , 當然 , 很多人類的基因信息 , 但也有細菌和病毒的信息 , 大部分來自你鼻子裡完全沒有傷害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了一些非常非常令人驚訝的現象 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 大約20%的鼻子裡的基因信息與我們從未見過的基因信息完全不符合 , 沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌的基因信息 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們根本不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們這些真正研究這類資料的小團體 , 我們當中有些人開始稱之為 「 生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何我們以前看過的東西 ; 它有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子裡有20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%或50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對比較無菌的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的資訊是暗物質無法被分類 , 不能被輸入或和我們以前見過的任何東西配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為這可能是人造的 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序工具相對比較新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定 , 這些資訊是一種生命的一種形式 , 至少當中有一些是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 其實只在它們的初始階段 , 有一個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那埋藏在生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 是對尚未被發現的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一系列a、t、c、g的生命 , 我們可能會發現 , 像beijerinck , 將會從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這也許能讓我們找出折磨我們的癌症的原因 , 或找出我們不熟悉的爆發病源頭 , 或是創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 與史丹福大學、加州理工學院和加州理工學院和加州理工學院的同事一起 , 我們正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 來探索新生命的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們意識到病毒 , 一種組成地球上大部分基因信息的生命形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們也許會驚嘆我們可能完全沒意識到在我們眼前的新生命階級 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能已經繪製了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有其他可以探索的生物 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同伴為下一代的探險家提供了重要的教訓 , 像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們說出了這一課 , 它會變成這樣:不要認為我們目前所認為的全部就是故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	去追蹤你選擇去探索的任何領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知 , 他們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳奇人物科學家大衛•迪希在研究更迫切的問題時 , 將理論物理學放在背後 , 來討論一個更迫切的問題:我們物種的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	宇宙中的大衛•迪希在我們所在之處 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知要走出肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	首先 , 事實上 , 歷史上大部分的記錄都以此聞名 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的 , 可以維持我們的演化或創造 , 就像以前的思想和現在的存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們的未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今這個想法有個很戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的概念是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是有著不可思議的 , 而內在的一切 , 是我們賴以生存的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸了我們的太空船 , 我們就沒有其他地方可以去 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 第二件大家都知道的事 , 與我們所相信的人類歷史大多相反 , 事實上 , 人類並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如斯蒂芬霍金說的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 就是在一個典型的星系的郊區 , 等等 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	大家都知道的前兩件事 , 都有點像是在說我們在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的服裝等等 , 第二件事是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是 , 如果你把這兩種說法當作深切的真相 , 來做你的人生決策 , 那麼它們似乎會和彼此產生衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能完全阻止兩者的錯誤 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 所以 , 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們環顧四周 , 環顧四周 , 看向一個隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢--而這一點也不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所要做的 , 就是朝著同一方向走幾百英里 , 然後回頭看 , 你不會看到任何牆或化學污垢 , 你只能看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你更進一步去看 , 你會看到太陽 , 太陽系 , 恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是典型的宇宙 , 因為星星是從星系來的 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 一個典型的宇宙空間 , 都沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再進一步 , 直到我們在銀河之外 , 再回頭看 , 沒錯 , 巨大的星系裡有螺旋手臂 , 在我們面前擺著 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	此時此刻 , 我們已經有十萬光年了 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們仍然離宇宙中典型的地方很近 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地點 , 你必須走一千倍到達星系間的空間 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的位置長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	在昂貴的代價之下 , ted安排了高解析度的虛擬實境 , 呈現了星系間空間的外觀 , 從星系間空間的角度 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 這樣我們就能看到了嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 並不是很完美 , 在星系間的空間中 , 星系間的空間是完全漆黑的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	太暗了 , 如果你正看著離你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星是一顆超新星爆炸 , 而你正目瞪著它 , 當它的光射向你時 , 你仍無法看見一顆閃光 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是這麼大、黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星是如此的亮 , 非常出色 , 讓你在幾光年內死去 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而 , 從星系間的空間 , 它離你非常遠 , 你甚至看不到 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	外面的溫度也很低 , 溫度比絕對零度還低三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	空無一物 。 真空中有一百萬倍的密度 , 比目前地球上最好的科技所能創造出的最高的真空量還少一百萬倍 。 這就是典型的這個地方的不同之處 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	請把燈光打開 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們如何知道一個如此遙遠的環境 , 和我們熟悉的一切都如此不同 , 如此陌生 。
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球的環境 , 以我們的形式 , 正在創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	這是什麼意思呢 ? 嗯 , 再往外看 , 比我剛才所說的還要遠--從這裡 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到一些看起來像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們叫做 「 quasars 」 , 原本是 「 量子星 」 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著有些東西看起來有點像星星 , 但不是星星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 幾十億年前 , 在數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質向一個超大質量的黑洞倒下 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈的磁場引導了那重力崩塌的一些能量 。 一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射機形式 , 以露天的亮度 , 照亮了葉片 , 我認為它是一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現今 , 人類大腦的物理學可能和這種噴射機的物理學差不多 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法存活一瞬間 。 當這些噴射流中 , 語言會分解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	這有點像經歷超級新星爆炸 , 但在時空有數百萬年的時間 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射流發生得非常精確 , 幾十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 預測 , 並解釋 , 最重要的是 , 你在宇宙中所發生的一切 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個四軸的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的表面形象 , 還包含了它 , 還包含了解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係 , 以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	那就是知識 。 如果這還不夠驚人 , 相似的結構 , 與另一種結構相似的信念會隨著時間逐漸增加 。 那就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有這樣的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體物體 , 不像彼此一樣 , 儘管它們可能是 , 仍然可以體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越長 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一個不一樣的化學污垢 。 這個化學污垢有普遍性的 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了永無止境的精準度 , 所有事物的結構 。 這個地方 , 而不是宇宙中的其他地方 , 是一個中心 , 它本身包含著整個物理現實的結構和因果的本質 。 所以 , 遠遠不被忽略 , 物理定律允許 , 甚至允許它發生 , 成為物理世界中最重要的事之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼 , 太陽系和環境 , 以我們的形式 , 如何才能取得與宇宙其他部分的這種特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬霍金的評論中有一點是正確的 , 但它的重點是錯的 , 但它是錯的強調 。 其中一個事實是 , 它沒有用任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟 。 它只用了三種我們在這富足中所擁有的 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是很重要的 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊處理是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 沒有物質的就無法製造出電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地記錄我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 較不明顯 , 但對於開放式知識和解釋的重要性 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據淹沒 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好在300年前開始測試 , 舉個例子 , 牛頓的重力定律 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但我們過去所做的證據 , 在那之前數十億年前 , 都在地球上落下 , 之後的數十億年還會持續下去 。 其他的科學也是如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 去發現所有科學中最基本的真相 , 就在我們的星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的地點充滿了證據 , 還有物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 創造開放式知識的這三個前提條件是最低可能的 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	正如我所說的 , 它是空的 ; 它是寒冷的 ; 那裡是黑暗的 。 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另外一個狹義的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個立方體存在於星系間的空間 , 就像我們家的大小 , 太陽系 。 現在 , 立方體非常空 , 依然存在著超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠製造一個自給自足的太空站 , 那裡有一群科學家致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類的 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 要把現有的技術從星系間空間的氫氣 , 轉換成其他元素等等 , 就要用現有的技術了 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但 , 問題是 , 在一個完全無法理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麼 , 除了知道如何 , 還能防止我們這麼做 , 還有什麼能防止我們這麼做 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而非資源的問題 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們可以自動使用能源供應 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再說一次 , 人類的感官是黑暗的 。 但是你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是現在的一個設計 , 往外看 , 然後你會看到跟我們這裡一樣的銀河系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	利用一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你可以看見恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在這些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 並且學物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最難做科學研究會是生物學的實地考察 , 因為要花上數億年才能回到最近的有生命的星球 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , 理查--但我從來沒有那麼喜歡生物學實地考察--我想我們每隔幾億年就可以完成一次.
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間的空間確實包含了開放式知識的所有前提條件 。 任何一個立方體 , 任何在宇宙的任何一個角落 , 都可以變成我們這樣的一個中心 , 如果知識的確存在的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並不是唯一適宜居住的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間的空間有能力創造出開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都一樣 。 地球就是污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制性的因素 , 在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源豐富 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙知識為基礎的觀點 , 或許我認為應該要讓我們感到非常特殊 。 但也應該要讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為 , 若沒有具體的知識 , 能夠生存宇宙的挑戰 , 我們就無法生存下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	只要一顆超級新星在幾光年之外 , 我們都會死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	最近martinrees寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出了差錯 , 最重要的是 , 恐怖主義有大規模毀滅性武器 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能存活這個世紀 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚些時候會在研討會上談到這一點 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為這可能性是正確的分類來討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他的看法 , 我們可以生存下來 , 無法生存下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否時間創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是前所未見的 。 物種總是會絕種 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明的結局 。 絕大多數的物種和文明 , 都是歷史上的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為例外的話 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用這個特徵來區別我們的物種 , 和我們的文明 , 和其他所有其他的特徵 , 即 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新解釋的能力 , 新知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我把這個應用到目前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 來說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是物理學家 , 但我不是那種對的物理學家 。 關於全球暖化 , 我只是一個層級人 。 做一個層級人 , 理性的做法是認真看待普遍的科學理論 。 根據這個理論 , 已經太遲了 , 無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為 , 如果我們目前最好的選擇就是用京都議定書來防止二氧化碳排放 , 因為它的經濟活動限制了它的經濟活動 , 且它的成本是數千億美元以上 , 不論它是什麼 , 那就已經是一場災難了 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡議的行動甚至都不是為了解決問題 , 只是稍微拖延一下 , 所以已經太遲了 , 無法避免它 , 自從任何人意識到這危險之前 , 已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代可能已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放量即將爆發一個新的冰河時期 , 數十億人將會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	現在我學到的教訓似乎很清楚 , 我也不知道為什麼這不是在公開辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能總是知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難時 , 以及如何以比災難本身的代價來解決問題 , 那麼其實根本沒有什麼爭論 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 沒有預防原則 , 就能避免我們還沒預料到的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個解決問題的平衡點 , 而不只是問題解決 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解藥 , 但那只是我們知道預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被鼻子打了 , 那麼醫學的科學並不會教你如何避免穿刺 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學界不只尋求治療和專注在預防上 , 那麼它也幾乎無法達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	目前世界正在興起 , 計劃著要把氣體排放減量的方案 , 不計代價 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該要以計劃來降低溫度 , 並計劃在高溫下生存 , 不論花什麼成本 , 都要很有效率且便宜 。 有些規劃存在 , 例如在太空中鏡子之類的 , 來把陽光給偏移 , 並鼓勵水生生物吃更多二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	目前 , 這些東西正在進行研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力解決這個問題的核心 , 或一般的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	在我們還沒有意識到的問題之中 , 若要正確地解決問題的能力 , 不是無限期的避免好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 還能生存下來 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩塊石頭平板為例 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個刻畫: 「 問題是可以解決的 。 」
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一幅是: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家要如何脫離貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不好的體制中 ? 經濟學家保羅默揭開了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區城市 」 , 城市規模管理區 , 由一個國家的聯合國統治 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	企業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治 。
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅•羅默的極端想法:特許城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	對我們來說 , 這是個很棒的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們這樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色上衣的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們也給他一個名字 , 尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢打賭nelson有手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	這是謎題 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森有像手機一樣先進的科技 , 但沒有一百年前的科技 , 可以在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以預防類似雙贏的解決方案 , 只要有人能把新技術帶進來 , 讓像尼爾森這樣的人都能使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的電力公司遵守一條規則 , 電力公司必須以非常低的補助金來銷售電費 , 事實上 , 電價非常低 , 每賣一個單位都會損失金錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既沒有資源 , 也沒有獎勵措施 , 可以吸引許多用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 規則是企業賺取小額利潤 , 所以他們有動機要簽名更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這是nelson買下電信公司的一種規則 , 下面的電信業者就是這樣 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他嘗試改變電力價格的規則 , 但他碰上了一場來自企業和消費者的抗議 , 他們想保存現有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困在規則之中 , 以避免他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在路燈下學習 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 要想出如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們能否發展出一些改變規則的規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為 , 有一個普遍的抽象概念 , 我們可以實踐 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人民更多選擇 , 在許多國家 , 更多的選擇 , 給予領導者更多選擇 , 那些領導人也是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但是 , 介紹這兩者之間的對立是有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者這種選擇 , 像是給總統提高電價 , 取消經濟中人們想要的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續消耗補助的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以 , 如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更能給雙方更多選擇的方法 , 那就給我們一套改變規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離困境 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能上網 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則的損害效應 , 規則可以讓人們留在黑暗中 , 看著太空總署在夜晚所拍攝的地球照片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大來看這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這裡 , 比起它的鄰居 , 這就像一個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則讓人們留在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但 , 要了解到北韓和南韓的規則 , 起始於一模一樣的規則 , 不論是法律或法規 , 都一樣 , 更深層的理解 , 規範 , 文化 , 價值觀 , 和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了一些選擇 , 這些選擇導致他們在規則的條件下非常分歧 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 可以改變我們與人互動的規則 , 讓它更好 , 或更糟 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 和鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國的鄰居數目差不多 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	相較於波多黎各這兩個國家都很黑暗 , 波多黎各的居民數目是海地或多明尼加共和國的一半以上 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們 , 規則之所以不好 , 是因為政府很軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不只如此 , 規則也不好 , 因為政府太強大了 , 太壓迫了 , 就像北韓一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以 , 如果我們想要創造出有良好規則的環境 , 我們就不能就這樣撕裂 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須想辦法建設 。
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示出與規則合作的潛在和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到剛開始的數據圖表 , 中國是世界高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國有先驅的技術 , 像是鋼鐵、列印、火藥 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則鼓勵傳播這些想法 , 一個獲利的動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播開來 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國不再是世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 中國也發展了更新的規則 , 那些進步都被阻斷了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	那裡的收入停滯不前 , 因為它放大了世界其他地方的收入 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它描繪收入、中國的平均收入佔美國平均收入的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到大約3%的氣候變遷 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國經濟開始下降 , 中國也開始快速趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在晚上回到地圖上 , 就會得到一個線索 , 這個過程會導致中國的規則發生劇烈改變 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點 , 各位可以看到 , 這張圖的邊緣是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國的一小部分 , 在20世紀大部分的時候 , 都遵守著非常不同的規則 , 比起其他主要的中國大陸規則 , 這些規則都被當時的勞動市場經濟所複製 , 並由英國來管理 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個地方 , 數百萬人可以從大陸前往職場 , 像是縫紉衣服、製作玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了取得收入增加的過程 , 技能越來越快的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港也是個典範 , 讓像鄧小平這樣的領導人可以複製 , 當他們決定把整個大陸移到市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫每個中國人立刻轉移到市場模式上 , 他們採取的做法是建立一些特殊的區域 , 從某種意義上來說 , 英國所做的是:讓機會和市場規則合作 , 讓那些想要進入市場的人都能參與 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍設立了四個特別的經濟區 , 在那裡 , 中國人可以來工作 , 城市的發展非常快 ; 外國企業也能來到這裡 , 創造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有個叫做深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有台台灣的公司 , 讓你們許多人都擁有iphone , 他們把iphone的勞動力從中國移到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特別區之後 , 有十四個沿海城市 , 以同樣的方式開放 , 最終在這些地方展示了成功 , 人們可以選擇 , 因為他們提供的優勢 , 他們聚在一起 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	證實了成功導致了整體經濟轉向市場模式的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一:保留人們的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模是正確的 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村莊的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但這個村莊太小了 , 無法得到你所能得到的好處 , 只要有數百萬人在有好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給人們一個機會 , 看看事情如何回頭 , 然後讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給你機會 , 創造出新地方 , 讓人們可以選擇的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	當數百萬人以良好的規則一起工作時 , 他們的利益夠大了 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以 , 我們的建議是 , 我們想出了 「 特區市 」 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一個特定規則的憲章開始 , 來吸引建造城市的人們 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者 , 來建造電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你需要吸引公司 , 他們會先僱用那些先搬到那裡的人 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 那些將來會永遠住在那裡的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子而做教育 , 並且得到他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那篇文章 , 人們就會搬到那裏去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造出來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模型 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍的做下去 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	為了讓它運作 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	這些是在圖表中捕捉到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們能在無人居住的土地上建造城市 , 那真的是建立在模型上的 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領土開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以來到新的憲章底下生活 , 但沒有人被迫活在它底下 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們想要領導者的那種選擇 , 我們必須允許國與國之間的合作有潛力:國家合作的案例 , 實際上 , 中國和英國合作的案例 , 首先是建立一個小小的市場模式 , 然後再擴大到中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國在香港所採取的行動 , 無意間 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫所做的更多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們允許這種合作關係再複製一次 , 我們就能在世界各地得到那樣的好處 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會牽涉到責任的代表權 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的代表權 , 來接管一些特定的行政責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	當我這麼說時 , 有些人開始思考: 「 這只是把殖民主義帶回來嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	並非如此 。 但重要的是要意識到 , 當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的情緒 , 可能會造成我們退縮 , 可以阻止我們的能力 , 以及我們想要探索新點子的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 常常是很糟糕的 , 是因為它涉及到強制和擁擠的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式的重點在於選擇 , 不論是領導者或將來住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強制和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談在實做上 , 要如何做到這一點 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	以一個特定的領導人raulcastro , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定想到 , 他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平對中國有什麼用處 , 但他在古巴島上沒有香港 。
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	然而 , 他的確在南方有一點點的光 , 南方有著非常特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣附近有一塊區域 , 在那裡 , 一個條約給美國政府的責任 , 一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚去找加拿大總理 , 說: 「 看 , 雅各有嚴重的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要逃出去 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	為什麼你不 , 加拿大 , 接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊的管理區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一個新城市在上面建造 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會支持 。 但這將是通往現代經濟和國家的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	此外 , 這個模型還能在哪裡試驗 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	許多人完全了解特區的想法 , 讓人們可以選擇成為規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	這是改變規則的一條規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人們選擇不受任何強制性 , 而強制性可以強迫的反對意見 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全明白 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更為可信的承諾 , 這些投資者會來建造港口 , 建造道路 , 在新城市中 , 他們可以做出更可靠的承諾 , 如果他們能和夥伴國家合作的話 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	甚至在某些安排中 , 這有點像信託管理帳戶 , 把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡 , 而合夥的國家卻為此負起責任 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多的土地可以用來建設新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我在沿著海岸飛行時拍的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的大地 , 有好幾億人可以住在那裡 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們把這個概念歸納成一個或兩個特區的城市 , 會有數十個城市 , 能協助成千上萬 , 甚至數十億人搬到城市裡 , 是否有足夠的土地供給他們 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在世界各地 , 如果我們在夜晚看著燈光 , 有一樣東西誤導了 , 就是 , 視覺上看來 , 世界上大部分的人都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這所有的土地為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方形 , 代表地球上所有的耕地 。
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經被30億人居住的城市所佔據的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把點移到長方形的底部你會發現現存的三十億城市只佔地球上可耕地的三分之三
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為其他十億人建造城市 , 他們會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從百分之三的可耕地 , 降到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅縮減了地球上人類留下的足跡 , 做法是建立更多可以移居的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市的治理是好的規則 , 它們可以是一些城市 , 在那裡 , 人們可以安全地從犯罪、疾病和不良的衛生設施 , 在那裡 , 人們有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	他們可以得到一些基礎設施 , 像是電力 。
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造出第一座特區城市 , 要花多少時間 , 才能建造出更多 ?
it would help to have a manual .	擁有一份手冊就很有用 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授所能做的就是寫下這些手冊中的細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 走出去 , 設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者在野外學習 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們開始思考像這樣的問題 , 假設不只是加拿大的拉爾•卡斯楚的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西是參與者 , 西班牙也是 。 也許古巴想成為四方聯合大企業的合作夥伴之一 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何訂定條約來做這件事 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	前所未有的 , 但那很容易解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這項資金 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	結果發現 , 新加坡和香港是能在他們剛開始時 , 取得大量的土地價值的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地價值來支付像是警察、法庭等的收入 , 但同時 , 學校和健康照護體系也讓這變成一個更吸引人的地方 , 讓人們有更高的收入 , 順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 那些協助建設這塊區域的人的獎勵 , 建立起了基本規則 , 往正確的方向發展 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有很多其它的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們要如何讓低成本、負擔得起的建築物 , 讓第一份工作的人們 , 組裝iphone , 讓建築物的能源效率提升 , 確保它們是安全的 , 讓他們不會在地震或颶風中下降 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節尚未解決 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些事情的人 , 已經知道沒有路障 , 沒有阻礙 , 除非想像失敗 , 會讓我們無法實現全球雙贏的解決方案 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片來做結論 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以能做得好 , 是因為地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和他人分享想法 , 當他們發現這些想法時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀少物品 , 分享意味著我們每個人都得到較少的資源 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以這種方式來思考想法時 , 我們通常會去思考科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:支配我們彼此互動的規則 , 例如 , 讓我們來設立一個稅收系統 , 來支持一個研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個系統 , 在那裡 , 我們有土地的所有權 , 在政府辦公室內註冊 , 大家可以保證它是附屬的 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能繼續創新規則 , 尤其是創新的制度 , 改變制度的制度 , 這樣我們就不會卡在不好的制度上 , 我們就能持續進步 , 真正地讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森和他的朋友不再需要在路燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因先驅克雷格•凡特從他的史詩級的圓形探險中休息一下 , 來談談數百萬個基因 , 他的團隊目前已經在探索 , 要繪製出海洋生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna , 生物圈 , 生物科技 , 企業家 , 基因 , 發明 , 海洋 , 科學 , 科技 , 科技 。
craig venter on dna and the sea	克雷格•凡特在dna和大海上 ,
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	剛開始 , 很多人問我關於老化的辯論 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這是我對此唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者大大勝過悲觀主義者 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	在我18分鐘內 , 我要告訴各位的是我們如何從解讀遺傳密碼轉換到開始自己寫程式的第一階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅在10年前的一個月 , 我們發表了第一組免費的有機體的基因序列 , 也就是嗜血桿菌的流行病 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這個計畫花了13年的時間 , 才到4個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	過去十年間 , 許多基因組被加上:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	大約十年前 , 這種想法的基因組學 , 到今年底 , 我們可能已經完成了三到五組基因組的定序 ; 已經完成了數百次了 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從godon和bettymoore基金會得到了一項補助 , 來為今年的130個基因組排序 , 作為環保有機體的副產品 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們觀察時 , 地球上有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有抓住這個星球上可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人不知道 , 因為它們是肉眼看不見的 , 但微生物佔據了地球半數的生物量 , 而所有的動物只佔了生物總量的1/4 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許在牛津的人們不太常這樣做 , 但如果你曾到過海面 , 吞下一口海水 , 請記住 , 每一毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	兩年前 , 只有不到五千種微生物物種被分類 , 所以我們決定要做點什麼 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了索爾第二次考察 , 在那裡 , 我們進行了很棒的海洋學探險 , 每200英里一次採集樣本 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做我們的測試計畫 , 接著搬到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿越加拉巴哥群島 , 橫越太平洋 , 現在我們正在橫越印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	非常困難的責任 ; 我們在帆船上做這件事 , 有一部分是要協助年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只需要用海水來過濾 , 我們在不同過濾器收集不同大小的有機體 , 然後把它們的dna帶回洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們可以在24小時內完成一億封基因編碼的基因序列 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	透過這麼做 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 有人認為我們的眼睛裡有視覺色素 , 環境中只有一或兩種有機體有著相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 幾乎在全球暖化的海上每一個物種都有相同的光感接收器 , 把陽光當作能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬個新基因 , 和多達50 , 000種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	現在我們將這個計畫延伸到空氣中 , 得到史隆基金會的獎勵 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們在測量有多少病毒和細菌 , 我們每天都在呼吸中和出去 , 特別是在飛機上或封閉的觀眾區 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的裝置來篩選 ; 我們從僅僅一天的時間內 , 就在紐約市的一棟大樓頂上 , 就收集了十億微生物的數量 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	目前我們正在進行測序 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在資料收集方面 , 我們在加拉巴哥群島的位置 , 我們發現幾乎每200英里 , 海洋樣本就有極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在不同溫度下 , 合理的說法是合理的 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 根據紅色的溫度 , 藍色是溫暖的 , 藍色是低溫的 , 我們發現 , 溫暖的水樣本和低溫的水樣本之間有很大的差異 , 用大量的物種來說 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們相當驚訝的事是這些感光受體偵測到不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列預測出這些波長 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些變化從地區到地區都非常不同 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	也許不出所料 , 在深海 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光器通常會看到藍色的光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有很多葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠色的光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化更大 , 極端的是紅外線和紫外線 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因庫是什麼 , 我們把所有的資料組合起來 , 包括我們所有的基因資料 , 包括遠離考察的所有資料 , 這代表地球上一半以上所有的基因資料 , 總共大約有2千9百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因放進基因家庭 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們只是發現已知家庭的新成員 , 還是發現了新家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因家族 , 但我們在環境中所採取的每個新樣本 , 都以線性的形式在這些新家庭中加入 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	我們正處於最早的發現基礎基因、組成和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看看所謂的進化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物在一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約2億9千萬個基因中 , 我們的基因組只有24 , 000個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有的動物放在一起 , 我們的基因組大概只有不到三萬個 , 也許還有十多個或上千個 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認爲這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計成分 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們認為以基因為中心的觀點 , 也許會回到理查德•達金斯的觀點 , 比起以基因為中心的觀點 , 這觀點不同 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 合成dna的能力已經改變了 , 和過去十年或二十年間dna測序的速度差不多 , 且成本越來越低 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對人造基因組學的第一個想法是1995年我們將第二組基因組定序 , 也是從菌根生殖器取得的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤上面寫著: 「 我很愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但大約有500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問一個問題 , 如果一個物種需要800種 , 再另外的500種 , 會不會有一組比較小的基因 , 可能是由最小的作業系統所組成的 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始做轉子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因密碼的一小片dna片段 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果它們插入到基因的正中間 , 就會阻斷它的功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張地圖 , 標示了所有可以接受轉位子插入的基因圖 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明 , 環境對此非常重要 , 你只能依據環境中的本質或非必要的基因來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試用比較直接的智能方法來處理13種相關的有機體的基因組 , 我們試圖比較這些基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們發現了這些重疊的圓圈 。 我們發現了173個基因 , 所有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一個細胞寄生蟲 , 這個池塘會再膨脹一點 , 當我們觀察核心基因組的310種左右時 , 它會擴張得更多 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴大或收縮基因組 , 依據你的觀點來看 , 到大約300到400個基因 , 從最少的500個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用這些基因來建構一個人造的染色體 , 而我們必須以一種隨機方式來進行 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 在大片區域中 , 合成dna的確是非常困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	史密斯和clydehutchison , 我的同事 , 開發了一種令人興奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內合成一組五千個鹼基對的病毒 , 這種方法的準確度是百分之百 , 就其序列和生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個非常令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始製造病毒粒子 , 然後殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是第一次合成病毒 , 小兒麻痺病毒一年前就被製造出來了 , 但只有十分之一的活性 , 而且花了三年才完成 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的卡通結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是軟體自己製造的硬體 , 這是生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立即跳入對生物戰爭的擔憂 , 最近我在參議院委員會前發表了證詞 , 美國政府設立了一個特殊委員會來審查這個領域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 把現實放在心中是很重要的 , 而不是人們的想像力會發生什麼事 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 現今任何已經被定序過的病毒 , 都可以被製造出來 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們馬上會對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐 , 但這個有機體的dna卻沒有傳染 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使有人做了天花基因組 , dna本身也不會引起感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正的問題是 , 安全部門有設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 曾有過重大的努力 , 試圖創造生物戰士 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果這個研究真的被解除了 , 在未來 , 設計師病毒的知識應該不會有太大的活躍性 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為兩年內 , 單細胞生物就有可能成真 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而我們擁有的真核細胞 , 在十年內就有可能成真 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在做數十種不同的建構 , 因為我們可以改變這個人造染色體中的序列和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 你要如何把其他的都放進去 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將它們組合成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從生物體中衍生出來的 , 致命的無線電波 , 可以讓三百萬拉德輻射被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆炸之後 , 它會在12到24小時內重組它的基因組 , 在它的染色體被完全炸開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 可能因為我們在外太空旅行 , 已在外太空中生存 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是一個玻璃啤酒杯 , 經過約50萬倍的輻射 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始燃燒和裂縫 , 而微生物坐在最底層 , 愈來愈開心 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這裡有一張實際發生的照片 , 上面的圖片顯示了在一百七十萬拉德輻射之後的基因組 。
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被炸開了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	令人驚訝的是 , 這些生物可以做到這一點 , 我們的地球上也許有數千種 , 甚至數萬種不同的物種能做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被合成之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了了解生物學的基礎 , 同時也為了環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們測序的第三種有機體中 , 甲烷-jannaschii-它的沸騰水溫 ; 它的能量來源是氫氣 , 所有的二氧化碳--它從環境中收集回來 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的路徑 , 數千種不同的生物 , 都活在二氧化碳之外 , 可以回收到 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其用從石油中取出的碳來進行合成過程 , 我們有機會使用碳 , 將碳從大氣中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種有機體 , 活在一氧化碳之外 , 我們用它來當作減少水分來分解水 , 來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多方法可以被改造成代謝甲烷 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦在挪威 , 主要的計畫是採用現金燃料 , 將甲烷從天然氣場轉換成有用的產品 。
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之後 , 我認為會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些巨大的基因組重組 , 和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 一天可以製造出一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	所以 , 就像所有生物學一樣 , 你在篩選螢幕時 , 是否在篩選氫氣生產 , 或化學生產 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 將會是非常容易取得的 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們嘗試修改光合作用的過程 , 直接從陽光下直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的氫化酶會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也結合了纖維素 , 分解複雜糖分解成簡單糖和發酵的酵素 , 在同一個細胞中製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物 , 製藥生產已經在大型實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學成分比我們最好的化學家所能製造的更為複雜 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的修復 , 也許可以取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策研究來做結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	我們在1999年開始實驗 , 直到我們完成一年半的生物倫理審查 , 是否應該嘗試製造人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖使用他們的經文當作法律 , 他們無法在他們身上找到任何東西 , 禁止製造生命 , 所以這肯定是沒問題的 。 唯一的擔憂是生物戰的方面 , 但前提是我們要開始進行這些實驗的原因 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在斯隆基金會剛剛資助了一項多制性的研究 , 來找出對社會有哪些風險和益處 , 以及像我這樣的科學團隊應該在這個領域中使用的規則 , 在我們往前走時 , 我們試圖建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了對生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計出乾淨的能源 , 也許能革新發展中國家能做些什麼 , 並透過各種簡單的程序來提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•辛巴多說 , 快樂和成功根植於我們大多數人不認同的特徵中:我們對過去、現在 , 和未來的方向 。 他建議我們在改善我們生活的第一步 , 校正我們的觀點 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心靈、心理學、科學、科學 。
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利普津巴多開處方是健康的服用時間 。
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好的 , 開始計時 。 三十秒鐘 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安靜下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間到了 , 結束序列 。 選一個 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利普•辛巴多:咱們來調整一下亞當的誘惑對話 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 亞當 , 別太希望 , 咬一口吧 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	" 一口 , 亞當 , 不要放棄 "
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹上麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好 , 咬一口 , 到底怎麼了 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	人生是誘惑 。 重點是要產生 , 抗拒 , 是 , 沒錯 , 現在 , 稍後 , 要有衝動性 , 要有現在 , 和未來的焦點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾的美德會落入當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些在婚前承諾性別絕種和處女的少女們 , 直到婚姻感謝喬治.布希--大多數 , 60%的少女 , 在一年內被性誘惑所誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大部分都沒有採用避孕措施 。
so much for promises .	很多的承諾 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 來試試四歲小孩 , 給他們治療 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	現在他們可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但是如果他們等到實驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 若你喜歡棉花糖 , 它會付出代價 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	孩子給予三分之二的誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等待 , 其他人則等著 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 。 他們延後了現在 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米歇爾 , 我在史丹佛大學的同事 , 十四年後 , 試圖發現這些孩子的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在許多層面上 , 被拒絕的孩子和被分配的孩子之間有著巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	抗拒分數的孩子 , 在sat考試中得分250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	非常龐大 。 這就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上麻煩 , 他們是比較好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們是自信且有決心的 。 今天對我來說 , 對你來說 , 關鍵是 , 他們是以未來為中心 , 而不是以現在為中心 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是 「 時間觀點 」 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	時間觀點是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 把你經歷的流向分成時間區或時間區別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地去做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	在文化、國家、個人、社會階級、教育水平之間 , 都不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得有偏見 , 因為你會學會過度使用它們 , 並忽略其他的部分 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 決定你要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在當下的情況下 , 其他人在做什麼 , 和你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們以那種形式做決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現場化 」 , 因為他們關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在是無關緊要的 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是說 「 我過去經歷過的情況是什麼樣子 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決策是基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 「 被遺棄的 」 , 因為他們關注的是 「 被遺棄的 」 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人 , 不是過去 , 不是現在 , 只是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於預期的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們的重點在於未來的將來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想要爭論 , 時間觀的悖論 , 是會影響你做的每個決定 , 你完全沒意識到 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	也就是說 , 在這樣的程度上 , 你有一個偏頗的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	嗯 , 其實有六個 。 有兩種方式可以當成現況 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被牧養 , 兩種方式可以成為未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面的、或負面的 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 " 服從主義者 " , 也就是你把焦點放在人生的喜悅上 , 或 " 當下主義者 " , 這無關緊要 , 你的生活被控制著 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是未來導向的 , 設定目標 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者 , 你也可以是超然的未來 , 也就是說 , 生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展出靈活性靈活性 , 來改變時間觀點 , 會根據情況的需求而流暢地變化 , 這是你得要學會做的事 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	所以 , 很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔案 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高於正面懷舊 , 適度高於未來
and moderate on presenthedonism .	並且調節當下的 " 現在主義 " 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	不論是負面的還是現代的 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最理想的暫時性混合是你從過去的正面積得到的 , 給予你根源 。 你將你的家人、身份和自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	從未來你會從翅膀到耳朵 , 到達新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的 , 是探索你自己、地方、人、感性的能量 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何時間來看 , 在過剩的情況下 , 負面的程度都比正面的多 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來會為了成功而犧牲什麼 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲好玩的時光 , 犧牲個人的寬恕 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 , 犧牲了睡眠 , 影響了他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們為了工作、成就和控制而活 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我肯定會和一些tedster們產生共鳴 。
