and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這讓我有所共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯貧民區長大 , 一個西里島家庭 , 大家都住在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位未來導向的人 , 他在頂端 , 做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入了 , 讓我成為未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到兩顆棉花 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上了 " 服從主義 " , 我把焦點放在 " 正面主義 " , 所以 , 在76歲的時候 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 而且我比以往更開心 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們把這個應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學率 , 化解成癮率 , 增強青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群 , 來促進永續性和保育 , 減少身體康復率 , 在那裡 , 有50%的退出率 , 改變了恐怖分子的自殺傾向 , 改變了家庭衝突的時間 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	所以我想以此作結:生命的謎題可以藉由理解你的時間觀點和他人的觀點來解開 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 顯而易見 , 但我認為後果是很深刻的 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	在一百年內 , 現今的頭條新聞會有多少人很重要 ? 1000年 ? 柯克特朗的《長期新聞》專案計畫收集到的新聞 , 不僅僅是現今的新聞 , 還會在數十年間產生共鳴 。 在ted2010年 , 他強調了近期的頭條新聞 , 用有潛在的潛力來塑造我們的未來 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:現在則是真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社的人 , 一年就有三百五十萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	這只是一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:在長期來看 , 那些故事有多少才是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是長期新聞背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這個計畫是長久以來的 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括凱文凱利和史都華特•布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的新聞報導 , 可能在未來的50、100 , 000年 , 仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過篩選器看新聞時 , 很多東西會從旁邊掉下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	以去年p.上個故事為例 , 這在十年內會有什麼影響嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會有什麼影響嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還蠻酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟狀況 , 我敢打賭 , 遲早 , 這次的衰退將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事能為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血流 , 來修復東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是老鼠 , 那一天已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真正的蜜蜂毒液 , 將基因送入大腦 ; 他們建造的一個可以爬過人體的機器人 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽九十億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	現今 , 餵飽60億人的糧食問題很嚴重 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	如同我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過十億人挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國在沒有修改作物的情況下會挨餓 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲已經投入了十億美元在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那麼 , 全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	當中國設立議程時 , 世界將會變得非常不同 , 而且他們有可能會 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	美國是世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們超過德國作為最大的出口國 , 他們開始對兒童做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的職業生涯 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們在尋找各種方法去推開已知的極限 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近有一些發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 已經從阿根廷散播到每一個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 有一個自我導向的機器人科學家 , 很快的發現 , 很快的 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命也不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎 , 有沒有我們 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我過去一年的長期新聞中 , 選出了這個:在月球上 , 水找到了 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	要把一個蟻群放在那裡容易多了 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不這樣做 , 中國可能會 , 或這個房間裡的某人可能會寫很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 有些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家卡羅琳•帕爾科在土星航行時所展示的影像 , 焦點在它最大的衛星泰坦 , 以及冰凍的土衛二上 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 探索 , 科學 , 科技 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco飛向土星
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	接下來的18分鐘 , 我要帶各位踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是一段旅程 , 你和我已經經歷了很多年了 , 50年前 , 人類第一次踏出地球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不但真的登上了月球 , 我們還把太空飛行器分散到所有八個行星上 , 我們在小行星上著陸 , 曾與彗星重聚 , 此時 , 我們有一艘太空飛行器 , 前所未有的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械任務都是人類更大的旅程的一部分:一趟旅程 , 去了解事物 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的起源 , 了解地球 , 我們的地球 , 和我們的生活方式 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中的所有地方 , 我們可能會去尋找像這樣的問題的答案 , 土星 。 在1980年代初期 , 我們去過土星 , 已經去過土星了 , 但我們對土星的調查已經變得更深入 , 細節自卡西尼號太空船飛越過了星際空間七年 , 在2004年的夏天 , 登陸環繞地球運行的軌道 , 成為人類最遙遠的機械飛行器 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 且顯然超越了比較 , 且對這個系統的調查有著巨大的進展 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是單獨研究光環 , 我們就能學到很多關於恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是一張andromedanebula美麗的照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 也是銀河系中最大的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	接下來 , 這是由哈勃太空望遠鏡拍攝的美麗複合體 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 回到土星的旅程 , 其實是部分的 , 也是人類旅程的一個比喻 , 用來了解我們周遭事物的相互連結 , 以及人類如何融入這張照片 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們所有我們學過的卡西尼 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向你們展示我們在過去兩年半拍攝的所有美麗照片 , 因為我沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以 , 我要把焦點放在這次重大探險旅程中最令人興奮的兩件最令人興奮的故事 , 我們在土星上進行探險 , 已經持續了兩年半 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	土星有著非常大且多樣化的衛星 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里寬到像美國一樣大 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝的土星美麗照片 , 事實上 , 土星與它的衛星同行 。 這是土星與土星同行 。 這是土星和土星同行的 。 這是土星 , 展示了土衛六的光環 , 向你們展示它們是多麼的薄弱 , 由土衛二和土衛二 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中有兩顆衛星是站著的 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	那些是土衛六土衛六和土衛二 。 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達那裡之前 , 我們在太陽系中最大的單獨的單獨地擴張地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它的身體長久以來一直被觀察行星的人們吸引 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它的大氣層非常厚 , 事實上 , 它的表面環境被認為比較像地球上的環境 , 至少過去曾有過的太陽系中的任何其他屍體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是氮分子 , 就像你在這裡呼吸的氮氣 , 只是它的大氣層被簡單的有機物質所包圍 , 像是甲烷、丙烷 , 和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	泰坦大氣中的這些分子會被分解 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 形成霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這種霧狀物無所不在 , 它是全球性且封閉的土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	這也就是為什麼我們不能用肉眼可見的光譜來看待這個表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但在卡西尼號到達之前 , 數十億年來 , 這些霧狀顆粒緩慢地移向地表 , 覆蓋在厚厚的有機泥土中 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	所以 , 就像泰坦的泰坦 , 泰坦的油 , 或石油 , 或我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是泰坦的表面溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是泰坦水對地球的影響 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是可以被凝聚的 , 所以 , 認識到這種情況 , 將它帶到前所未有的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲上方 , 有數百公里的霧狀物 , 可以防止任何陽光進入地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	但 , 儘管很冷 , 土衛六上仍有大雨落下 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上 , 降雨對地球造成的影響是:它會雕刻出石頭 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它會形成峽谷 ; 它可以在大盆地及大型的隕石坑中聚集 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥土沖掉高山的山頂 , 沖到低地 。 所以停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	它是黑暗的 。 土衛六上的中午跟地球上的微弱地球一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	很冷、很怪 , 很迷霧 , 很有可能下雨 , 你可能就站在密西根湖邊 , 帶著油漆 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達之前所看到的土衛六表面 , 我可以告訴你 , 我們在泰坦身上發現的土衛六表面 , 雖然它的細節並不相同 , 但它的奧妙之處就如同故事一樣 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像是卡西尼人 , 一直以來 , 它就像是叢林凡爾納的冒險 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我先前所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 由太陽照亮 , 光環則是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	還有另一顆衛星 , 我甚至不知道是哪一顆衛星 。 它是非常廣大的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器 , 可以透過大氣層看到海面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮而黑色的區域 , 差不多就是它為我們帶來的 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這真是太神秘了:我們無法在泰坦看到我們所看到的 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你靠近這個區域時 , 你會開始看到一些東西 , 像是seantchannels我們不知道的 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	我們後來發現 , 這其實是一座坑洞 , 但土衛六表面上只有極少數的隕石坑 , 意思是說土衛六是個非常年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來像地殼構造 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	他們看起來好像被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上有線性的東西時 , 它就意味著有碎片 , 像斷了一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它在地面上已經被改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一場事件 , 許多人都認為卡西尼的 「 土衛六調查 」 突出了 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲的太空船號探測器 , 卡西尼號在整個太陽系內運行了七年 。 我們將它部署到土衛六的大氣層 , 花了兩個半小時才下降 , 降到地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調一下這個事件有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是一種人類製造的裝置 , 它在人類史上首次登陸在外太陽系中 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這實在太重要了 , 在我看來 , 這是一個活動 , 應該要在美國和歐洲各地的城市裡 , 都要用浮標錄音帶遊行慶祝 , 很遺憾 , 並不是如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這很重要的另一個原因 , 這是個國際性的使命 , 這個活動在歐洲、德國都慶祝 , 而慶祝的演講被用英語口音、美國口音 , 和德國口音 , 法語、義大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是一場正在進行的演示 , 說明了 「 聯合國 」 應該要表達的意思:一個真正的國家團結在一起 , 共同努力進行著巨大的努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 人類為了探索一個星球 , 為了理解一個星球 , 一個在人類歷史上 , 一直都無法達成的星球系統 , 而現在 , 人類已經觸及了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我在談論雞皮疙瘩 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個非常激動人心的活動 , 而且是我個人永遠不會忘記的 , 你也不該忘記的 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	不管怎樣 , 探測器在大氣層下方進行測量 , 還拍了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 從探測器上看到泰坦的表面是怎樣的感覺 。 這是我們所看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	那是很驚人的 , 因為那是我們想要其他的照片從軌道拍攝到的 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是一個明確的圖案 , 一個地質圖案 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這種樹突排水模式的形成方式 , 只有液體的流動才能形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些頻道走 , 你可以看到它們是如何融合在一起的 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	他們匯聚到這條通道中 , 流入這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里內拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這張照片是在8公里高的地方拍的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大概是航空公司的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫越美國 , 你會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在鐵達尼亞航空公司的窗口飛越土衛六地表的照片 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器在地表上靜止下來 , 我要給你們看 , 各位先生女士 , 這是第一個從外太陽系月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些很可能是水冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很顯然 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、黑暗的區域 , 看不到它的下沉 。 所以它並不是我們降落的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器下降的位置等同於一片泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是一片未整齊的土地 , 裡面滿是液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	我們看到的這些通道中 , 這種材料已經被沖洗掉了土衛六的高地 , 經過數十億年的時間 , 流出了低窪的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但仍然 , 我們的影像中沒有標誌 , 或甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	它們在哪裡 ? 在我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人困惑了 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們電影中的泰坦區域的電影 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘有100公尺高 , 被幾公里的沙丘分開 , 延續好幾英里的距離 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	那裡有數百 , 高達一千或一千 , 200英里長的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	很顯然 , 它是個非常乾燥的地方 , 否則你不會得到沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 這也讓人困惑的是 , 沒有任何液體 , 直到最後 , 我們看到北極的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	在南極的極地帶有一個湖泊 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	差不多跟安大略湖一樣大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 一個禮拜半前 , 我們飛越了北極 , 發現了 , 同樣的 , 我們發現了加州海域大小的一個特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	由於某些原因 , 我們不明白這些液體 , 或至少在這個季節 , 顯然是在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們應該會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個神秘的地方 。 它很奇特 , 它很奇特 , 但卻很像地球 , 而且有著像地球一樣的地質結構 , 和非常驚人的地理多樣性 , 而且是一個非常迷人的世界 , 一個太陽系中唯一與複雜和豐富的對手的世界 , 就是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二 。 土衛二是一個小衛星 , 大約是土衛六的第十個大小 。 你可以在英國旁邊看到它 , 只是讓你們看看它的大小 。 這不是威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二是非常白的 , 非常亮 , 它的表面顯然有裂痕 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它在地質上非常活躍 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多是南極發現的 , 而我們現在看到的是南極 , 在這裡 , 我們發現了破裂的系統 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們的組成不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被覆蓋著 , 這些裂痕被有機物覆蓋著 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極區 , 整個南極區域 , 溫度上升了 。 這是地球上最熱的地區 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	奇怪的是 , 地球上的南極洲比熱帶地區還熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍了更多的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些裂縫中 , 有著微弱的冰粒 , 延伸到太空中數百英里的距離 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們把這張圖譜編碼出來 , 呈現出微弱的光度 , 我們會看到這些噴射噴射流的光度 , 事實上 , 在其他影像中 , 我們可以看到 , 在土衛二上方數千英里的太空中 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊研究了像這樣的影像 , 像這張 , 思考了卡西尼的其他結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是這些噴射流可能是從土衛六地表下的液態水口噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以 , 我們有可能有液態水、有機材料 , 以及過多的熱量 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們很有可能在現代行星探索的聖杯上發現了 , 換句話說 , 我們的環境很有可能適合生物生存的生物 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 其他生命的發現 , 不論是在土衛二上或其他地方 , 都會有龐大的文化和科學上的意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明創世紀的發生不止一次 , 而是在我們的太陽系中 , 獨立發生了兩次 , 那就表示 , 根據推斷 , 它在整個宇宙中發生了驚人的次數 , 以及它的137億年歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	現在 , 地球是我們所知唯一還充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它是獨一無二的 , 到目前為止 , 它仍然是我們唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們當中有人在1960年代有警戒和連貫性 , 我們會原諒你們 , 如果你們沒有 , ok , 你們會記得1968年由阿波羅八號太空人拍下的這張非常有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	這是第一次從太空拍攝地球 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的衝擊 , 以及我們對於地球保護的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們在卡西尼號拍的第一張相同的照片 , 一張前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是太陽的全蝕 , 從土星的另一側看到的 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張令人難以置信的美麗照片中 , 你會看到太陽背光的主光環 , 你會看到太陽的折射影像 , 事實上 , 這個光環是由土衛二的延伸所造成 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們可以從這張美麗的圖片中發現 , 我們自己的星球 , 在土星的光環的臂彎中 , 搖晃著 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	現在 , 看到我們自己從遠處 , 捕捉到我們在其他星球的天空中所見到的景象 , 深深移動著 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而那 , 和我們從中得到的觀點 , 可能是 , 最終 , 我們從這個發現的旅程中得到的最好的獎勵 , 大約是半個世紀前的 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到2005年 , 全球僅有15%的人被繪製出地圖 。 這減緩了災難後的援助 , 隱藏了未使用土地和未知的道路的經濟潛力 。 在這個簡短的演講中 , 谷歌已故的卡達示範者 , 全球各地的人們使用地圖繪製他們的世界 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、技術 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	最近 , 卡拉格達:對抗災難的地圖 , 建造經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 颶風納格毀滅了緬甸人 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要把人和供應給給趕到這個地區 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖 , 沒有道路地圖 , 沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 沒有辦法幫助惡性循環受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被地圖化的細節所繪製出來 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國的跑頭證實了世界上大部分人口臉孔的問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救命來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 40名志工用新軟體繪製出120 , 000公里的道路 , 3000間醫院 , 物流和救援點 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker 。
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一項技術 , 讓每個人可以在當地地圖繪製出我們已知的資訊 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流、學校、當地企業 , 及影片商店 , 到角落商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人赫爾•赫南多•德索托了解到 , 對大部分發展中國家而言 , 經濟利益的關鍵在於要利用大量的未獲利的土地 。
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度 , 就有一兆美元的房地產尚未被記載 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是去年 , 170個國家的數千名使用者就已經繪製出了數百萬筆資訊 , 創造出了一幅從未想過的細節地圖 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這種現象的發生 , 是因為有熱情的使用者無所不在 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	現在我們來看看使用者製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 在我們說話的同時 , 在這170個國家中 , 人們在繪製世界地圖 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑剛在塞內加爾繪製了一條道路 。
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家更近 , 查盧亞 , 班加羅爾的g路線 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學、手勢識別和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是成千上萬使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市 , 一個使用者 , 一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是對70%未被開發的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	在2003年 , 布德魯斯的巴勒斯坦村 , 建設了一個長達10個月的非暴力抗議活動 , 去阻止他們在橄欖車上蓋一座障礙 。 你聽說了嗎 ? 沒有這麼想 。 巴西的電影製片人julicha問為什麼我們只關注以色列衝突中的暴力 , 而不是那些非暴力領袖 , 那些有一天可能會帶來和平的非暴力領袖 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情心、娛樂、電影、和平、戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	juliabacha:請注意非暴力行為 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人試圖用和平手段來結束衝突的人們 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總是有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不使用非暴力抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我面臨的挑戰是 , 我常常從中東回到中東 , 在那裡 , 我拍攝了數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 不論是以色列士兵或移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導者正試著要打造一個龐大的全國非暴力運動 , 來終結該區域的佔領 , 並建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 在座大部分人可能從來沒有聽過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	國外發生的事和感知之間的差別 , 是我們還沒有的主要原因之一 , 巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動已經成功了 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以今天我來這裡是要談談注意力的力量 , 你的注意力的力量 , 以及在西岸、加薩 , 和其他地方的非暴力運動的興起和發展 , 但今天 , 我的個案是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 最缺少非暴力成長的 , 並不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是我們開始關注那些已經擁有的人們 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我用布德鲁斯村的布德鲁斯村來說明這個點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣布要建造出一道分離的障礙 , 部分的障礙會建在村落上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 被包圍 , 所以他們會失去自由地進入西岸的其他人 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地的領導力 , 他們發動了和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些簡短的片段 , 你們可以明白地面上真正的樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知這堵牆將分離巴勒斯坦和以色列 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村 , 我們發現這堵牆會偷走我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男子:事實上 , 柵欄已經解決了恐怖問題 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你被邀請去和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:沒有什麼比非暴力抗爭更嚇人了 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女人:我們看到男人試圖推動士兵 , 但他們都不能這樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們可以做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空我們傳統的想法 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯政黨成員:我們在完全和諧的狀態下 , 想要把它散播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫 , 哈馬斯和受歡迎的前線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主持人:圍籬的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊境警察被派去散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活的子彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就像法魯吉 , 到處開槍 。
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列抗議人士:我確信我們都會死去 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但 , 我身邊有其他人甚至不用牛奶 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭不會阻止伊斯蘭教徒 。
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們可以做到 ! 我們可以做到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴查查:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體無法報導七年前發生的非凡事件 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更讓人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了 。
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過了10個月的和平抗爭 , 說服了以色列政府 , 將他們的土地和綠線的路線移開 , 也就是以色列和巴勒斯坦領土之間的國際認可界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗藥性自從傳到西岸的村落 , 到耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體仍然在這些故事中保持沉默
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默對非暴力的可能性造成很深遠的影響 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦成長或甚至存活的可能性 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭有一項非常重要的共通點 , 兩者都是一種劇場的形式 , 尋求觀眾的理想 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一不斷地登上頭版並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的問題 , 對非暴力領袖來說 , 對他們的社區來說 , 公民不服從是非常困難的 , 對他們來說 , 公民不服從是可以解決困境的選項 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量可能對在座的父母一點都不意外 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓你的孩子越來越大聲丟棄的方法 , 就是讓他第一次把注意力丟出去 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	反覆思考會變成童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子已經知道 , 他可以從中得到父母的關注 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母可以透過給予或減低孩子的注意力 , 來鼓勵或抑制他們的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人來說也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為會受到影響 , 根據國際社群選擇把注意力放在哪裡 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東衝突的核心 , 將和平帶給我們 , 就是要把非暴力的行為轉變成功能性行為 , 做法就是讓大家更注意現今的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在我拍攝電影到西岸、加薩、東耶路撒冷村莊的村落中 , 我見識到連一部紀錄片都可以影響整個轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個叫做瓦拉耶的村莊 , 非常靠近耶路撒冷的村落 , 這個村落正面臨著和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去了很多土地 , 也失去了自由 , 不論是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段約兩年了 , 但自從沒有人注意到他們之後 , 他們就開始變得不知所措 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了篩選螢幕 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一週後 , 他們舉行了目前為止最熱門且有紀律的示威 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	組織者說 , 村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事在一部電影中 , 覺得確實有人在追蹤他們所做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這一邊 , 有一場新的和平運動 , 叫做索里達里德羅 , 意思是希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導者把布德鲁斯村當作主要的招募工具 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人以前從來沒有活過來 , 看過電影 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里達里德拉克運動的例子顯示 , 即使是一部小型預算獨立電影也可以扮演一個角色 , 將非暴力行為轉化為功能性行為 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	現在 , 想像一下 , 如果大型媒體玩家開始報導每週發生的非暴力的示威 , 在像bil'in , ni'lin , 瓦拉吉 , 在耶路撒冷 , 像謝赫•賈拉 , 和絲林這些非暴力領袖會變得更明顯 , 更有價值 , 更有效率 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們就隱形了 , 就好像從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但是我親眼見到如果我們這麼做 , 他們會倍增 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們倍增 , 他們的影響力會在以巴衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	他們的影響力終於可以解開局面 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力行為在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方是可行的 。
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	咱們把注意力交給他們 , 讓他們可以證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•薩克有個簡單但強大的模式 , 能鼓舞人心的領導力 , 一切都從金色圓圈開始 , 還有 「 為什麼 ? 」 他的例子包括蘋果 , 馬丁•路德金 , 和萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	野牛、商業、企業家、領導、銷售、銷售、成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•薩克:偉大的領導者如何鼓舞大家採取行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你如何解釋當事情不如我們預想的那樣 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或更棒的是 , 你要如何解釋當其他人能夠達成似乎違反所有假設的事物時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	舉例來說:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 比他們所有的競爭對手都還要創新 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一間電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他所有人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們擁有相同的才華 , 相同的機構 , 一樣的顧問 , 一樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼馬丁路德金主導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國遭受過預防權利的人 , 他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠在有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金時 , 想出控制權、有動力的人飛行 ,
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有實現有力的飛行員 , 萊特兄弟打敗他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我發現了一件事 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深改變了我對世界運作方式的看法 , 甚至深深改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果發現 , 世界上所有的偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果電腦、馬丁路德金 , 或他們所想的萊特兄弟 , 採取行動和溝通 , 都是一樣的 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全相反 , 其他人也一樣 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是編寫它 , 它可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圓 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領袖能夠啟發其他人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們的行為 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼辦到的 , 不管你怎麼稱呼它為你分辨的價值主張、或你的私人過程或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做這些事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	所謂的 「 為什麼 」 指的不是 「 賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 , 總是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂 「 為什麼 」 的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的目標是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們的思考方式 , 我們的行為方式 , 我們溝通的方式是從外面來的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯的 , 我們從最清楚的事物變成最模糊的 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但 , 鼓舞人心的領導者 , 以及鼓舞人心的組織 , 不論它們的大小 , 不論它們的產業全都在思考、行動和溝通 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我會用蘋果 , 因為它們很容易懂 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦跟其他人一樣 , 他們的行銷訊息可能聽起來會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們的設計很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想要買一台嗎 ? " 我 "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方法 , 多數銷售都是這樣做的 , 多數人與人之間的交流就是這樣 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們所做的事 , 我們說我們如何不同 , 說我們如何好 , 期待某種行為 , 購買 , 投票 , 諸如此類 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶做生意的表演 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車 , 它有很棒的汽油里程 , 有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這是蘋果電腦溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的方式思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是 , 把我們的產品做得很漂亮 , 很簡單 , 很容易使用 , 且很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好做了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想要買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣的右邊 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	這證明了人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一位都很自在從蘋果電腦買一台電腦 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常自在地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是蘋果電腦的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 就像我之前說的 , 蘋果電腦只是一間電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能分辨出它們的結構性與其任何競爭者 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過了 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , 蓋茲公路上發佈了平面的電視節目 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯有資格製作平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	多年來 , 他們一直在製作平面螢幕監視器 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾發表了mp3播放器和pda , 他們做出了很棒的品質產品 , 他們可以做出完美的設計產品 , 沒有人買的 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 現在談到這點 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你要買電腦公司的mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是要和所有需要你的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的人們做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的部分是:我跟你說的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都是基於生物學的基礎 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學 , 生物學
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人類大腦的剖面圖 , 從上往下看 , 你看到的是 , 人類的大腦實際上是分成三個主要元件 , 與黃金圈完美的相關 。
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的大腦 , 我們的智人大腦 , 我們的大腦皮質 , 與 「 什麼 」 的層次對應 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間這兩個區塊構成我們的邊緣大腦 , 我們的邊緣大腦負責所有的感覺 , 例如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也負責所有人類的行為 , 所有的決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外面溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以了解大量複雜的資訊 , 如特徵、利益、事實和數字 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	只是它不會驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能從內而外的溝通時 , 我們會直接和控制行為的大腦溝通 , 接著 , 我們讓人們將它合理化 , 用我們說和做的有形事物 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這就是我們的直覺決策來源 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道 , 有時候你會給別人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節說了什麼 , 但那感覺不對 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	我們為什麼要用這個動詞 , 卻不 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦部區域不控制語言 。
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們盡力而為: 「 我不知道 。 感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者有時你會說你在帶著你的心 , 或者你是帶著你的靈魂去領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想對你們說 , 那些其他的身體部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	一切都發生在你大腦邊緣的大腦中 , 控制決策而非語言的那部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你要做你所做的事 , 人們會回應你為什麼要做你要做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們去投票 , 或買東西給你 , 或 , 更重要的 , 去忠誠地去做你想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你東西的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的人們 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你雇用員工 , 只因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你雇用了那些相信你所相信的的人 , 他們會用血、汗水和淚水來幫你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	比起萊特兄弟 , 還有更好的例子 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求權力人機的追求 , 就像當時的網路一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierperpontlangley , 我們認為是成功的秘訣 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品 ? 為什麼你的公司失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是會給你同樣的三件事:不幸的、不對的、不好的市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	這三樣東西都是一樣的 , 所以讓我們來探索一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierperpontlangley得到五萬美金的資金 , 由戰爭部門得知這台飛行機器 。
money was no problem .	錢也沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛舉辦了一座座座椅 , 在史密森尼亞州工作 , 他認識當時所有人的心智 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的頭腦資金 , 市場條件非常棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 所有人都支持langley 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那我們為什麼從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley呢 ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠在俄亥俄州的威爾伯•萊特 , 他們沒有一個成功的秘訣 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們用自行車店的程序來支付他們的夢想 ; 萊特兄弟的團隊中沒有任何一個人有大學教育 , 甚至不是ville或wilbur ; 紐約時報到處都是 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 歐威爾和威爾堡的動力來自於一個目的 , 一個目的 , 一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這台飛行機器 , 就能改變世界的軌跡 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要有錢 , 而且他想要有名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求財富 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信萊特兄弟夢想的人們用血汗和淚水和他們一同工作的人 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他的則只是為了賺錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們講述的故事是 , 每次萊特兄弟出門 , 他們都得先拿出五組零件 , 因為那是他們進來吃飯前會墜機幾次 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 1903年12月17日 , 萊特兄弟開始飛行 , 甚至沒有人可以體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	幾天後 , 我們發現了這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley的動機是錯誤的:萊特兄弟當天起飛了 , 他放棄了 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 各位 , 這是個驚人的發現 , 我會改善你們的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一位 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他放棄了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你的信仰 , 你就會吸引那些相信你所相信的信念的人 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的信念的人很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂的 「 創新的散播法則 」 , 如果你不懂法律 , 你一定會知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	前2.5%的人口是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%的人口是早期採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數 , 晚期的多數人和後代的後代 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人只買了觸控電話的唯一理由 , 就是因為你再也買不了轉子手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	在這個尺度上 , 我們都坐在不同的地方 , 但創意的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場的成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就無法擁有它 , 直到你達成了15%到18%的市場市場佔有率的高峰期 , 然後系統就會崩潰 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你在新企業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很樂意跟你說: 「 喔 , 大概10%吧 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓客戶超過10%的客戶使用 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的人 「 懂了 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣形容他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就像那種直覺 , 「 喔 , 他們就是懂了 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:在你和他們做生意之前 , 你要如何找到那些無法得到它的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	正如jefreymoore所說的 , 就是這個小小的缺口 " 跨越了隔閡 " 因為 , 你知道 , 早期大多數人都不會嘗試直到有人嘗試
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人 , 創新者和早期採用者 , 他們對於做出這些膽量的決定感到很自在 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更加自在地做出這些直覺性的決定 , 由他們對世界的信念所驅動 , 而不僅僅是產品的可得性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排隊排了六個小時 , 第一次出櫃時 , 才買到iphone , 下星期你只要走進商店 , 再從架上買了一支手機 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人花了4萬美金在平面螢幕上 , 第一次上映時花了4萬美金 , 儘管這項技術還不夠用了 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順道一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術太棒了 , 他們自己做了 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想成為第一人 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做的事只證明你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做一些證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	在前六個小時 , 人們買iphone的原因 , 排在六個小時 , 是因為他們對世界的信念 , 以及他們想要每個人看見的 , 他們是第一名 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗 , 以及一個有名的成功案例 , 關於創意的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業性的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如我們先前所說 , 第二 , 成功的秘方就是金錢 , 右派和右派市場條件 , 對嗎 ? 你應該要成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從第八、九年前的tivo出版到今日 , 他們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 請舉手 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們的資金非常高 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場的條件非常棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是在我的垃圾時間華納dvr上做很多東西 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo是個商業性的失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們上了ipo , 他們的股票大約是30到40美金 , 然後就下跌了 , 從來沒有在10歲以上交易過 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它是在六歲以上交易的 , 除了幾個小突點之外 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個產品可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 轉播現場電視節目 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 甚至不問你 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控你生活的各個層面的人 , 那麼 , 我們有這個產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場的電視節目 , 跳過廣告 , 記得你的收視習慣 , 等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你所做的只是證明你所相信的
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在 , 讓我給你一個成功的例子 , 關於創新的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年的夏天 , 有25萬人出現在華盛頓的購物中心聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何邀請函 , 也沒有網站查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	你怎麼做到的 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說者 。
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是美國唯一一個遭受過預防權利的人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子不好 。
but he had a gift .	但他有份禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	那些相信他所相信的的人把他的理想拿走 , 把理想變成他們自己的理想 , 然後他們告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	其中一些人創建了結構 , 讓更多人接觸到這個字 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 有25萬人在正確的日子出現 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而出 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們坐上八個小時的公車 , 在八月中期站在華盛頓的陽光下 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人:百分之二十五的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信 , 世界上有兩種法則:那些法律是由更高的權威制訂的 , 和那些人所制訂的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有人類所制訂的法律都和更高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們會生活在一個正義的世界裡 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正因為如此 , 民權運動才讓他有了人生的理想 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟著 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順道一提 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演說 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演說 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽聽現在的政治家用他們全面性的12點計畫
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有鼓舞任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者 , 也有領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但領導的人鼓舞了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們追隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些從 「 為什麼 」 開始的人 , 有能力啟發他們周遭的人 , 或去找那些啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼記得你在車子的哪個位置 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝正確的方向移動的 ? 神經科學家尼爾•尼爾•塞爾研究了在我們周遭的神經機制 , 以及它們如何連結記憶和想像 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 。
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大型停車場停車時 , 我們怎麼記得我們停車的地方 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是荷馬面對的問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們會試著去了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬迴開始 , 以黃色標示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你在那兒受損 , 就像在阿茲海默症 , 你記不得東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文 「 海馬 」 , 和 「 海馬 」 很像 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內有約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元之間會互相溝通 , 通過互相連接來發送小脈衝或電刺激 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬迴是由兩片非常緊密的細胞組成的 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠或老鼠的個別神經元 , 來探索一個尋找食物的環境 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像一下 , 我們正在從這隻老鼠海馬體中紀錄一個神經元 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一些電流刺激時 , 會有一個紅點和一個點擊 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們看到這個神經元知道這隻老鼠在環境中的某一個特定位置
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	大腦的其他部分藉由電流刺激 , 來向大腦發送訊號 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	我們可以將神經元的發射率作為動物的位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄許多不同的神經元 , 我們會發現 , 當動物在不同環境的不同區域時 , 不同的神經元會發出訊號 , 就像這個方形方形方形方形方形方形方形方塊在這裡 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起 , 為大腦的其餘部分畫出一張地圖 , 不斷告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也在人類身上被記錄下來 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以 , 癲癇患者有時需要他們大腦的電訊活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人玩電玩遊戲 , 他們在小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬丘中的位置細胞會發動 , 變得活躍 , 每當它們開車穿過一個特定的小鎮時 , 就會開始發送電子脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	所以 , 一個安慰劑細胞如何知道環境中的老鼠或人在哪裡 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這邊這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境的邊界非常重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	最上方的那一隻會在老鼠的老鼠的牆壁之間發出訊號 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子擴大 , 發射位置就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的這棵樹會在靠近南邊的一道牆時發出火
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一面牆放進盒子裡 , 不管在南方哪裡都有一道牆 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 , 細胞都會被激發 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測會感測到你周圍的邊界和方向 , 延伸出建築物等等 , 對海馬迴來說特別重要 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在輸入海馬迴的輸入資料中 , 發現了海馬迴的哪些專案 , 對於偵測到邊界或邊緣的確有反應 , 尤其是當老鼠在探索時 , 會從老鼠或老鼠的指令和方向 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 當動物靠近牆壁時 , 它會發出訊號 , 不論是方形方框的邊緣或是圓形的圍牆 , 或甚至是桌子邊緣的邊緣 , 動物會在周圍移動 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞在任何時候都會被激發 , 不論是桌子邊緣或是牆壁 , 或甚至是兩張桌子之間的落差 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以 , 我們認為位置細胞會決定動物在四處探索的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體在哪裡 , 例如這個目標旗幟 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或說 , 你的車會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 去看看他們必須記得的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回到環境中 , 通常它們非常擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟或車子的地方 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟的位置是如何改變你如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你看到的國旗代表跨越小平方形環境的位置 , 然後如果你問人們那裡的位置 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟的位置與發射的位置完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你記得國旗在哪裡 , 藉由在你位置上儲存你位置細胞內的發射模式 , 然後你就可以藉由四處移動來回那個位置 , 這樣你就能找到最適合你位置細胞的當下模式 , 以儲存該位置的圖案 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	那會引導你回到你想要記得的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道 , 我們透過運動來到哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們走了一些邊界的路 , 也許我們停車 , 離開時我們會知道 , 因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路的方向 , 回去的方向大概就是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也能從所謂的網格網格細胞中得到這種整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞又再次被發現 , 在海馬迴的輸入中 , 它們有點像位置細胞 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個個別細胞會在一系列不同位置的位置發射 , 以驚人的三角形網格呈現 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從數個網格細胞中紀錄 , 這裡有不同顏色的網格細胞 , 每個細胞的網格狀激發模式 , 會稍微改變相對的細胞 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的 , 在這個網格上發出綠色的 , 還有藍色的 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	總而言之 , 這就好像老鼠可以在環境中放置一個虛擬的網格 , 有點像地圖上的緯度和長度線 , 但用的是三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它四處移動時 , 電子活動可以從這些細胞傳遞到下一個細胞 , 以追蹤它的所在 , 這樣它就可以用它自己的動作 , 來知道它在環境中的哪裡 。
do people have grid cells ?	人有電網細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有類似電網的發射模式都有相同的對稱軸 , 在這裡的橘色方向 , 表示所有電網的淨活動 , 在大腦的某個特定區域 , 都應該根據這六個方向來改變 , 或是在中間的六個方向來跑 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人放到核磁共振成像掃描儀中 , 讓他們做一個小遊戲 , 就像我給你們看的 , 並且尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你在人腦內的內皮質也就是你在老鼠身上看到網格細胞的同一個部位
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車在他停車的地方附近的距離和方向 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被邊界偵測細胞的發射所代表 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車停車場走出的路 , 這將會是以網格細胞激發出來的 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種類型的細胞都可以讓位置細胞被激發 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動來返回停車位的位置 , 找到他目前大腦中最適合的位置 , 與他車子停車的位置 , 來配合他目前儲存的位置模式 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	那引導他回到那個位置 , 視覺提示的位置 , 像是他的車到底在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被用完了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡取得它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們在整體大腦中尋找類似的發射模式 , 我們會在一系列的位置上看到它 , 當我們做各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是很活躍 , 比如說 , 記得你上次去婚禮時 , 記得它 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 也許神經機制 , 代表我們周遭的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 這樣我們就可以重現空間的場景 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像時 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果發生了 , 你的記憶就可以從位置細胞透過這些密集的交互連結來啟動彼此 , 然後啟動邊界細胞 , 在你的觀點周圍創造出空間的結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個視角 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種類型的頭向細胞 , 我還沒提過 , 它們就像指南針一樣 , 根據你面對的方向 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義觀看的方向 , 例如你想要為你的視覺影像產生影像 , 所以你可以想像 , 當你在婚禮時發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	所以這只是一個新時代的例子 , 在認知神經科學中 , 我們開始了解心理過程 , 像是你如何記得、想像 , 或甚至思考 , 在數十億個獨立神經元所組成的大腦所採取的行動中 。
thank you very much .	非常謝謝 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 一個全球安全的驅動力 , 是由組織、政府、私營部門 , 和公共機構合作推動的 , 這不僅僅是遙遠的開放資源的希望 , 這是jamesstavridis的願景 , 北大西洋最高層的指揮官 , 他們分享了來自近代軍事歷史的活力 , 來解釋未來的安全性 , 是否應該被建造在橋樑上 , 而不是牆壁 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、開放資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯特瓦里迪斯:北約的最高指揮官是如何看待全球安全的 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談的是開放資源的安全 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們的安全性必須更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 咱們先回顧二十世紀 , 了解安全的風格對我們是如何運作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場 , 位在比利時北部的北部 。
